601 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vasquez


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


182 Conn. 242; 438 A.2d 424; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 978


June 5, 1980, Argued  
August 19, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the third degree, possession of burglary tools, larceny in the fourth degree, and interfering with a police officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Schaller, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of burglary in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-103, possession of burglary tools in violation of § 53a-106, larceny in the fourth degree in violation of § 53a-125, and interfering with a police officer in violation of § 53a-167a.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with burglary in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-103, possession of burglary tools in violation of § 53a-106, larceny in the fourth degree in violation of § 53a-125, and interfering with a police officer in violation of § 53a-167a. He pleaded not guilty to each of those charges and elected to be tried by a jury, which returned a verdict of guilty on each count. On appeal, the issue was whether the trial court erred in its instructions to the jury regarding the manner in which they should ascertain defendant's state of mind or intent. The precise statement from the court's instructions on intent to which defendant objected and upon which he based his appeal was: "The person is presumed to have intended to do the acts which he did do." The court concluded that defendant was not denied due process of law and that jury were sufficiently informed by the instructions that any presumption on the element of intent was permissive and that no burden of any sort rested upon defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

602 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Board of Trustees v. Freedom of Information Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


181 Conn. 544; 436 A.2d 266; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 919


May 13, 1980, Argued  
July 22, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiffs from a decision of the defendant commission brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Bernstein, J.; judgment affirming the decision of the defendant commission but remanding the cause for further action, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an academy, a board of trustees, and officers, appealed the judgment of the Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut) sustaining the decision of defendant, the Freedom of Information Commission, that the school was a "public agency" within the meaning of the Freedom of Information Act (FOIA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-15 et seq., in plaintiffs' action against the Commission and defendants, taxpayers and a taxpayer association.


OVERVIEW: The academy was established by special corporate charter to operate a school for the surrounding inhabitants. Because the town had no public high school, virtually all the children in the town who sought a free secondary education attended the academy. The town paid the entire tuition for those students pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-34. The town and two nearby towns contributed 95.32 percent of its operating expenses. Defendants filed a complaint under the FOIA requesting disclosure of the academy's past and present operating records. After hearings, the Commission directed plaintiffs to comply with the request. On appeal, the trial court affirmed the Commission's decision. On further appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that a nominally private corporation, such as the academy, which served a public function was a "public agency" under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-18a(a) for purposes of the FOIA. The court applied the functional equivalent test and found that it was almost entirely publicly funded, was examined and certified by the state for reimbursement purposes, and was created for the sole purpose of maintaining a public school for area inhabitants.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no error with regard to the trial court's judgment.

 

603 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Berlin v. Santaguida


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


181 Conn. 421; 435 A.2d 980; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 900; 109 L.R.R.M. 2055


April 9, 1980, Argued  
July 1, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of the compulsory binding arbitration provisions of the Connecticut Municipal Employees Relations Act, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Goldberg, J.; judgment declaring the provisions unconstitutional and enjoining the defendants from resorting to those provisions, from which the defendants, on a joint appeal, appealed to this court.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, employees and unions, challenged a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which declared, in an action brought by plaintiffs, several municipalities and a taxpayer, that the provisions of the Connecticut Municipal Employees Relations Act regarding compulsory binding arbitration were unconstitutional and enjoined defendants from resorting to the Act's provisions.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs instituted a declaratory judgment action seeking an injunction and a determination as to the constitutionality of the compulsory binding arbitration provisions of the Act. At the time the lawsuit was filed, the municipalities had collective bargaining agreements in effect that contained provisions regarding wages, work hours, and fringe benefits. After determining that plaintiffs had standing, the trial court declared the disputed provisions to be unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that neither the municipalities nor the taxpayer had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the Act. The court held that although municipalities generally did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of state legislation, the municipalities could question a statute's constitutionality if they were before the court on a nonconstitutional question. The court found that the sole issue before the trial court was the constitutionality of the Act. Thus, the municipalities had no standing. The court held that the taxpayer did not have standing either because he was not affected by the challenged legislation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had declared the compulsory binding arbitration provisions of the Act to be unconstitutional, and remanded the action with instructions to dismiss the action.

 

604 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Washington


Supreme Court of Connecticut


1980 Conn. LEXIS 907


Argued December 11, 1979  
July 1, 1980, decision released; substitute opinion December 9, 1980


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On transfer from the Juvenile Court, indictment charging the defendant with the crime of felony murder, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County, and tried to the jury before Testo, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, and appeal by the defendant. Error; new trial. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction in the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) of the offense of felony murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c. Defendant was a juvenile, and his case was transferred from the juvenile court to the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction in the trial court for the offense of felony murder. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred when it denied his motion to suppress his confession and when it instructed jurors that they were permitted to discuss evidence that they heard provided that they did not come to any decision about the case. Upon review, the court found error, and decided that because the trial court's instructions were erroneous, there was no need to review the admission of defendant's confession. The court noted that upon a juror's inquiry, the trial court instructed the jury that it could discuss the evidence as it was presented and specifically warned the jurors against deciding the case until the close of evidence. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-245 prevented jurors from conversing with any person not a member of the jury relative to the case under the jury's consideration. Alternate jurors were not segregated from the petit jurors pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-243(c) and were not members of the jury. Therefore, the trial court's instructions permitted the alternates to exert impermissible outside influence on the jury.


OUTCOME: The court found error.

 

605 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Washington


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


182 Conn. 419; 438 A.2d 1144; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 1004; 21 A.L.R.4th 435


December 11, 1979, Argued  
July 1, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued October 14, 1980. Substitute Decision Released December 9, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of felony murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Testo, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.

The state filed a motion for reargument which was granted.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a motion for reargument after the court set aside the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of murder, and ordered a new trial because of error in the instruction that permitted alternate jurors to discuss the case with regular jurors in contravention of their statutory duty.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether it was unconstitutional for the trial court to instruct the jury that prior to the time that the case was submitted to them, they could "discuss" the evidence they had heard provided that they did not "deliberate, take a vote, or come to a conclusion." Defendant claimed that the trial court's instruction early in the trial granting the jurors permission to discuss in the jury room the evidence heard daily before the termination of the case deprived him of due process under the federal and state constitutions. The court agreed that the instruction regarding the jurors' discussion of the evidence prior to the time the case was submitted to them deprived defendant of due process of law. The court determined that the juror's oath set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-25, and Conn. Prac. Book, R. Super Ct. P. § 850 did not prohibit or mention instructions regarding the jurors not discussing the evidence among themselves before the termination of the case. The court held that it was the Due Process Clause of the federal and state constitutions and the right to trial by an impartial jury that were the sources of the prohibition of such discussions.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant, and ordered a new trial.

 

606 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stepney


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


181 Conn. 268; 435 A.2d 701; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 885


March 7, 1980, Argued  
June 24, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictments charging the defendant in each case with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and reserved by the court, Allen, J., in the first case and Covello, J., in the second case, for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to motions by defendants and the State after separate indictments charging each defendant with murder, the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut) certified the question of whether the instruction given to each grand jury that "ordinarily a person is presumed to intend the result which follows his acts" met the due process requirements of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Prior to the examination of witnesses, each grand jury was instructed that that intent to cause the death of the victim was an element of the crime charged in the indictment and that "ordinarily a person is presumed to intend the result which follows his acts." After reviewing the evidence and interviewing witnesses, each grand jury returned a true bill. The trial court certified the question of the constitutionality of the instruction in light of the Sandstrom test, which found such an instruction to a petit jury to be a violation of due process. On review, the court found the instruction constitutional. The court held that the interests intended to be protected by the prohibitions delineated in the Sandstrom test with regard to a petit jury are not equally imperiled within the context of a grand jury proceeding. A conclusive presumption of intent did not conflict with the presumption of innocence or invade the factfinding function as it did with a petit jury. The presumption of innocence did not apply before the grand jury, which considered only probable cause.


OUTCOME: The court answered the superior court question in the affirmative.

 

607 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Buckley v. Warden, Connecticut Correctional Institution


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


181 Conn. 286; 435 A.2d 348; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 891


April 1, 1980, Argued  
June 24, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus alleging failure to credit time earned against sentence imposed, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Graham, J.; judgment granting the writ, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant warden appealed from an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted petitioner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus alleging that the warden failed to credit him with 14 days "good time" as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-98a.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court granted petitioner a writ of habeas corpus, the warden sought review. The sole issue on appeal was whether the discretion bestowed upon the warden by § 18-98a empowered the warden to classify inmates' job assignments such that only those employed in so-called "seven-day" jobs were eligible for credit against their sentences in accordance with the statute. The court found error, set aside the judgment, and directed entry of judgment for the warden. The court held that the warden's job classifications and housing limitation rules, which were promulgate to minimize the disruption to inmates in the performance of their work assignments, was not an abuse of the general discretion granted to the warden under § 18-98a. Further, petitioner was aware that he was required to accept a seven-day job and to live in a designated area to obtain credit but chose to accept a five-day job so that he could remain in his cell. Also, even though petitioner was assigned a five-day job, he agreed to perform it for seven days after being told that he would receive extra compensation for the work but would not receive credit.


OUTCOME: The court found error in the trial court's judgment . The court set aside the judgment with direction to enter judgment for the warden.

 

608 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Friedson v. Westport


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


181 Conn. 230; 435 A.2d 17; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 878


April 9, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
June 17, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment declaring unconstitutional and ultra vires certain zoning regulations restricting the maintenance of an advertising sign on the plaintiff's premises, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport, where the defendants filed a counterclaim for an injunction restraining the plaintiff from willfully violating the zoning laws of the named defendant; the issues were tried to the court, Novack, J.; judgment for the defendants on the counterclaim, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenant appealed an order of the Superior Court of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut), which granted a judgment in favor of defendant town in the tenant's declaratory judgment action to have declared unconstitutional and ultra vires zoning regulations restricting the maintenance of an advertising sign on the tenant's premises. The town filed a counterclaim for an injunction restraining the tenant from willfully violating the laws.


OVERVIEW: The tenant leased a retail store in the town. The previous tenant had maintained a sign advertising its business on the roof of the building. The sign was supported by a metal frame and fastened to metal brackets that were fastened to the roof. The sign had been left in tattered condition. The tenant had the sign painted. The sign was removed to the painter's place of business. It was then returned to the store and replaced in the same location and in the same manner as it was before it was removed. While the sign was being painted, the zoning enforcement officer contacted the tenant. The tenant knew that an attempt to put the sign back in the same place was considered a violation of the zoning ordinance. The planning and zoning commission issued a cease and desist order to the tenant, who appealed to the zoning board of appeals for a variance. After a public hearing, the variance was denied. The court affirmed. The tenant failed to proved a valid nonconforming use of the sign as of the effective date of the zoning regulation. Therefore, the trial court's conclusions that he did not establish a valid preexisting nonconforming use of the sign were not in error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granted to the town.

 

609 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Paoletto


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


181 Conn. 172; 434 A.2d 954; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 856


March 5, 1980, Argued  
June 10, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in each case charging the defendant with the crimes of larceny in the first degree and burglary in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and tried to the jury before Testo, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant in each case.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of judgments from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut), which convicted them of larceny and burglary. The court granted defendants' motion to combine their cases on appeal. They claimed violations of their Fourth Amendment rights.


OVERVIEW: While directing traffic, an officer observed a black automobile approaching at a rate in excess of the posted speed limit. Defendants were passengers in the car. The officer, after stopping the car, noticed a pry bar in the passenger compartment. The car and the three passengers were searched. The officers found a screwdriver and two pair of gloves under the driver's seat, a clothes basket in the back seat, and in the trunk, numerous items later identified by the victims of a housebreaking to which the officers gained access by removing the back seat and back rest. Upon review, the court found no error. The conduct of defendants plus the circumstances preceding the arrest supported a finding of probable cause. The officer was well aware of the high incidence of burglaries in the area and recognized the vehicle by its marker number as one that had been identified by the police department as possibly connected with the crimes. The circumstances within the officer's knowledge, and of which he had trustworthy information, were sufficient to justify a reasonable belief that an offense had been or was being committed.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

610 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ruth


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


181 Conn. 187; 435 A.2d 3; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 859


March 5, 1980, Argued  
June 10, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and tried to the jury before Levister, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut), which, upon a jury verdict of guilty, convicted defendant of felony murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress his confession, in refusing to charge as requested on the matter of accomplice testimony, and in its charge to the jury on the element of intent. The court first held that defendant's arrest was not illegal and that the trial court properly denied the suppression of the confession. The court concluded that where the police entered defendant's dwelling pursuant to a valid search warrant, they could arrest him under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-1f because they had probable cause to believe he committed a felony. Thus, defendant's arrest did not violate the Fourth Amendment, and the confession was properly admitted. Second, the trial court did err in its instruction to the jury as to the credibility of accomplice testimony. The court found, however, that the error was harmless because it was not likely that it affected the result and did not rise to the level of depriving defendant of a fair trial as the evidence against defendant was overwhelming. Finally, any error with regard to the charge concerning intent was harmless because it related to the crime of manslaughter, of which defendant was not convicted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder.

 

611 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Hartford Federal Sav. & Loan Asso. v. Stage Harbor Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


181 Conn. 141; 434 A.2d 341; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 850


April 9, 1980, Argued  
June 3, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for foreclosure of a mortgage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, N. O'Neill, J.; judgment of strict foreclosure for the plaintiff, and appeal by the defendant Country Lumber, Inc., to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant lumber company challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which entered a judgment of strict foreclosure for plaintiff mortgagee on four properties secured by a promissory note and mortgage deed from defendant mortgagor in favor of the mortgagee. The company owned an interest in the four properties subordinate to that of the mortgagor.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagor planned to construct four single-family dwellings on the four properties, but construction had not begun on two of them before the mortgagor defaulted. None of the defendants, including the lumber company, made disclosure of defense in response to the mortgagor's written demand. The trial court rendered judgment of strict foreclosure in favor of the mortgagee pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 236 and denied the company's motion to open the judgment of strict foreclosure. The court held that (1) pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-15, a trial court's discretion in granting or refusing an application to open a judgment could not be disturbed on appeal, absent an abuse of discretion; (2) the denial of such relief to a company who, through its own negligence, failed to defend properly was not an abuse of discretion; (3) the nonexistence of construction on two properties was easily discoverable by the company prior to the trial court's judgment; (4) the lis pendens statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-325, had no effect because judgment had been entered; and, (5) the court could not review questions not raised at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

612 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nims


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


180 Conn. 589; 430 A.2d 1306; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 807


November 7, 1979, Argued  
May 20, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Hull, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder. On appeal, the court set the judgment aside and ordered a new trial. The court did not agree with defendant that a 16 month delay was unreasonable per se. The court found that there was no showing of prejudice regarding the delay. The court could not agree with the trial court's conclusion that the selection process did not constitute an intentional discrimination because of sex. The court held that it was in the nature of the practices challenged that proof of actual harm, or lack of harm, was virtually impossible to adduce. In light of the great potential for harm latent in an unconstitutional jury-selection system, and the strong interest of the criminal defendant in avoiding that harm, any doubt was resolved in favor of giving the opportunity for challenging the jury to too many defendants, rather than giving it to too few.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court convicting defendant of murder and denying him a new trial was set aside and remanded.

 

613 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Manor Dev. Corp. v. Conservation Com. of Simsbury


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


180 Conn. 692; 433 A.2d 999; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 811; 12 ELR 20063


January 17, 1980, Argued  
May 20, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiff from a decision of the defendant commission acting as the inland wetlands authority in denying an application to build a roadway on certain wetlands, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Schaller, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sought review of the decision by the Court of Common Pleas (Connecticut), which denied its appeal from the denial of its application to build a roadway on wetlands pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22a-36 through 22a-45.


OVERVIEW: A landowner applied to a commission to build a roadway on wetlands. The application was denied. The landowner appealed, contending that there was an unconstitutional taking of its property without compensation in contravention of the U.S. Const. amend. V and the Connecticut Constitution. The court found that the denial, based on the commission's finding that overdevelopment in wetlands created problems and that the land in question was in a wetlands area, were a sufficient basis to deny the application when the language of the enabling statute was considered. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-36. The court found that the commission did not act illegally, arbitrarily or in abuse of its discretion in denying the application for the reasons that it stated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

Seymour v. Seymour


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


180 Conn. 705; 433 A.2d 1005; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 813


March 11, 1980, Argued  
May 20, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the dissolution of a marriage, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Berdon, J.; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting custody of the minor child to the defendant, and appeal to this court from the order of custody by the plaintiff and by the attorney for the minor child.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father sought review of the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which dissolved the couple's marriage and granted custody of the minor child to defendant mother.


OVERVIEW: After the parents separated, they tried to share custody of the minor child without success. The parties were very different and therefore were unable to agree as to how the child should be attended to. The court conducted several hearings and sided with one of the psychologists, who stated that the minor child had more of an attachment to her mother. The lower court concluded that pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-56(b), the best interests of the minor child were best served with her mother. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional because it vested the lower court with discretion in determining the best interests of the child. The court concluded that the trial court did not err when it looked to other factors, such as the child's psychological relationship with her parents, in determining who should retain custody of the minor child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment.

 

615 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Kukanskis v. Griffith


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


180 Conn. 501; 430 A.2d 21; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 869


January 8, 1980, Argued  
May 13, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application by the plaintiffs for a prejudgment remedy by way of an attachment of certain real estate of the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Pickett, J., granted the application ex parte; the defendant filed motions to dissolve the attachment and a notice of lis pendens, which were granted by the court, Pickett, J.; the plaintiffs' motion to confirm the original attachment and lis pendens was denied by the court, Hadden, J., from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff buyers appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which denied their motion to confirm an original prejudgment attachment and lis pendens that was filed against defendant property owners.


OVERVIEW: Property owner agreed to construct a home for the buyer on the owner's land. The buyers brought a breach of contract action against the owner seeking specific performance and money damages. The lower court granted the buyers a prejudgment remedy of attachment against the owner's interest in certain land. The buyers also filed a notice of lis pendens. The owners without notice to the buyers secured a release of the prejudgment attachment and dissolution of the lis pendens. The trial court denied the buyers' motion to confirm the original attachment and lis pendens. On appeal, the court found that there was an insufficient factual basis from which the lower court could find probable cause to issue a prejudgment attachment as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-278e(1). The affidavit filed in support of the attachment made only a conclusory statement that a contract existed. Moreover, the court found that the underlying contract was not presented to the lower court for review. The court also found that the lis pendens statute found in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-325 was unconstitutional because it failed to provide the barest minimum due process protections.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court, which denied the buyers motion to confirm an original prejudgment attachment and lis pendens against the property owners.

 

616 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wilson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


180 Conn. 481; 429 A.2d 931; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 797


February 15, 1980, Argued  
May 6, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in three counts charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the first degree, attempted burglary in the first degree, and conspiracy to commit burglary in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Bracken, J.; the court directed a verdict of acquittal on the second count; verdict and judgment of guilty on the first and third counts, and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him of assault in the first degree and conspiracy to commit burglary in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that (1) the trial court erred in denying his motions to suppress and dismiss on the ground that there was insufficient justification for his arrest and consequent search; and (2) the trial court erred in admitting testimony concerning his tracking by a bloodhound. Upon review, the court found defendant's arguments without merit. In light of the State's offer of proof as to the qualifications of the trooper and the dog, the circumstances surrounding the finding and protecting of the footprint, and the time the tracking took place, the trial court did not abuse its discretion or misconceive the law in admitting the testimony of the trooper concerning the dog's tracking activities on the night in question. It was clear that the testimony was probative of the issue of defendant's identity. The trooper's testimony, which corroborated other evidence linking defendant with the crime, although clearly damaging to defendant's cause, was not prejudicial, particularly in view of the foundation that was laid before its admission. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting that testimony over any objection on the grounds of relevancy.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for assault in the first degree and conspiracy to commit burglary in the first degree were affirmed.

 

617 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rodriguez


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


180 Conn. 382; 429 A.2d 919; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 796


October 9, 1979, Argued  
April 29, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before McGrath, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of manslaughter in the first degree, and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of manslaughter in the first degree. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss the jury panel, in allowing and denying various witnesses' testimony, and in denying his motion to set aside the verdict.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of manslaughter in the first degree and asserted on appeal that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss the jury panel, in allowing and denying various witnesses' testimony, and in denying the defendant's motion to set aside the verdict. The court granted defendant's motion to set aside the verdict of the trial court, concluding that the trial court did not err in denying the defendant's motion to dismiss the jury panel, but that the trial court's erroneous exclusion of evidence offered defendant bearing on the truth and veracity of the two child complainants was harmless because the veracity of these witnesses was crucial to the state's case, and that the trial court erred in refusing to set aside the verdict because defendant based his motion to set aside the verdict on the ground that there was no foundation either in the law or the evidence at trial to support the verdict of guilty of manslaughter in the first degree where the evidence supported an instruction on a lesser degree of homicide than that charged, it was error to refuse to give such an instruction.


OUTCOME: The court found error, the judgment was set aside, and the case was remanded for a new trial on the charge of manslaughter in the first degree.

 

618 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pickering


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


180 Conn. 54; 428 A.2d 322; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 728


December 13, 1979, Argued  
March 4, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of risk of injury to children and one count of sexual assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Berdon, J.; verdict of guilty of two counts of risk of injury; the court declared a mistrial on the sexual assault count and rendered judgment, on motion by the defendant, dismissing the information on all counts, from which the state, on the granting of permission by the trial court, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the order of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which granted defendant's motion for mistrial on a count of sexual assault in the second degree and dismissed the information that also charged two counts of risk of injury to children under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 after finding that § 53-21 was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of molesting his daughter and attempting to have sexual intercourse with her. Defendant was indicted. The jury returned a guilty verdict on two counts of violation of § 53-21. The superior court granted defendant's motion in arrest of judgment and to dismiss the information on the grounds that § 53-21 was unconstitutionally vague as applied to his case. The State appealed. The court reversed and directed a conviction. The court determined due process was satisfied because an innocent defendant was given fair warning by § 53-21 and, therefore, § 53-21 avoided unconstitutional vagueness. In addition, defendant had adequate notice that sexual acts with a child under 16 years of age violated the core meaning of § 53-21. The State was entitled to reinstatement of the jury verdict and conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the superior court, which had dismissed the indictment against defendant. The court reinstated the jury verdict and remanded with directions to render a guilty judgment and sentence defendant.

 

619 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


United Illuminating Co. v. New Haven


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


179 Conn. 627; 427 A.2d 830; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 713


October 4, 1979, Argued  
February 19, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Actions for declaratory judgments determining the constitutionality of a statute and a municipal ordinance, and for injunctive relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Hadden, J.; judgments holding the statute and ordinance unconstitutional, from which the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgments directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city, its tax collector, and its assessor, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted the declaratory relief sought by plaintiff utility companies, and which determined that the property tax assessment procedures in the city ordinance and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-62 violated the Equal Protection Clauses of Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 1, 20 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: After the state legislature passed Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-62, the city passed an ordinance that provided for staged increases in certain real property tax assessments. When the utility companies learned of a tax increase, they filed actions against defendants on the grounds that the tax procedures violated equal protection principles. The trial court found the ordinance and the statute to be unconstitutional, and defendants appealed. The court reversed, holding that the utility companies had failed to meet the burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that the legislation violated equal protection. The court noted that statutes were presumed to be valid. Further, the rational basis test applied to classifications within the tax statutes because they did not contain a suspect classification or impinge upon a fundamental right. Although the tax statutes had established a rather arbitrary line for the classification, the decision of the legislature was accepted because it was within the range of a reasonable mark. Moreover, the legislatures' attempts to mitigate the burden of increased assessments was a valid consideration in enacting the statute and the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the declaratory judgments and it remanded the action with directions to render judgments declaring the statute and the ordinance to be constitutional.

 

620 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Eielson v. Parker


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


179 Conn. 552; 427 A.2d 814; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 700


November 8, 1979, Argued  
February 5, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of a statutory compensation plan for judges of the Superior Court, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and reserved by the court, T. O'Sullivan, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action challenging the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 51-47, which established a graduated salary system for the judges of the superior court, plaintiff judges sought an order to compel defendants, the treasurer of the state and comptroller of the state to pay them salaries equal in amount to those paid to other judges of the superior court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought the class action challenging the constitutionality of the Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 51-47, which established a graduated salary system for the judges of the superior court. Plaintiffs sought an order to compel defendants to pay them salaries which were equal in amount to those paid to other judges of the superior court. The questions of law were as follows: (1) Did § 51-47 violate the separation of powers provided for by Conn. Const. arts. II and V? (2) Did § 51-47 violate the equal protection clauses of Conn. Const. art. I, § 20 and U.S. Const. Amend. XIV? (3) Must all of the judges of the superior court receive the same salary? (4) Did the supreme court have power to order defendants to pay salaries to superior court judges in the absence of any lawful statute authorizing the defendants to pay such salaries. The court answered the first two questions in the negative and held that the statute did not violate the state and federal constitutions. The court reasoned that the salary system for the compensation of judges that was contained in § 51-47 had a rational connection to a legitimate legislative objective of strengthening the judiciary of the state.


OUTCOME: The court held that the challenged statute was constitutional and did not violate the equal protection clauses of either the state constitution or the federal constitution.

State v. De Freitas


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


179 Conn. 431; 426 A.2d 799; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 683


October 4, 1979, Argued  
January 8, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with two counts of murder in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in New London County and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in New London County (Connecticut) convicted defendant of two counts of murder in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-9. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Two acquaintances of defendant witnessed evidence of defendant's involvement in a crime. In an effort to ensure that the individuals would not report the information, defendant shot one of the individuals and a friend of defendant shot the other individual. Subsequently, defendant was convicted on two counts of murder in the first degree. On review, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. In reaching its decision, the court rejected defendant's argument that the trial court erred in excluding the testimony of three defense witnesses who were called to testify about alleged third party declarations against penal interest. Furthermore, the court ruled that the trial court committed no error in denying defendant's pro se motion for a mistrial on the basis of the trial court's admission of certain testimonial evidence against defendant. The court so held, because it found that defendant's claim that the evidence was "highly prejudicial" and in violation of defendant's "constitutional rights" was far too sweeping a claim and vague. The court concluded that the trial court's ruling on the admissibility of the evidence at issue was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

622 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Connecticut Light & Power Co. v. Costle


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


179 Conn. 415; 426 A.2d 1324; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 687


October 12, 1979, Argued  
January 1, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiff from the order and decision of the named defendant, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford county and tried to the court, Bieluch, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal; motion brought in the Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford-New Britain by the named defendant to set aside the judgment and for a new trial which was granted by the court, Kelly, J., from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff power company appealed a judgment from the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which set aside the trial court's judgment because it was rendered beyond the time limits provided by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-29 and granted a new trial in the power company's appeal from an order and decision of defendant, the Acting Commissioner of Environmental Protection of the State of Connecticut (Commissioner).


OVERVIEW: The trial judge rendered his decision in the power company's administrative appeal more than four years after the close of the session at which the case was tried. The power company argued that the superior court erred in granting a new trial because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-29 did not apply to administrative appeals. The court held that certification for appeal was improvidently granted and dismissed the power company's appeal. The court found that the order granting the Commissioner's motion for new trial was only reviewable if the superior court acted beyond its jurisdiction. The court determined that § 51-29 applied to administrative appeals and that, in the particular unusual circumstances of the case, which included the facts that the time limits prescribed by § 51-29 had been extravagantly exceeded and that no claim of waiver or consent was argued or even arguable, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-270 endowed the superior court with jurisdiction to set aside the trial court's judgment. The court held that it lacked jurisdiction to review the order for new trial because the superior court acted within its jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that it improvidently granted certification for appeal and dismissed the appeal for lack of jurisdiction, without taxable costs to either party.

 

623 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Leech v. Veterans' Bonus Div. Appeals Bd.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


179 Conn. 311; 426 A.2d 289; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 962


October 3, 1979, Argued  
December 11, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiff from the denial by the defendant board of his application for a veteran's bonus, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Bernstein, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff veteran appealed the decision of the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which dismissed his appeal of the decision of defendant Veterans' Bonus Division Appeals Board. The board had upheld the action of the state treasurer, which denied the veteran's application for a veteran's bonus on the ground that the veteran did not meet the residency requirements.


OVERVIEW: The veteran appealed the board's denial of his request for a veteran's bonus provided by Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 27-140a through 27-140m. The board found that the veteran was not eligible because he had not been domiciled in Connecticut for at least one year before his entry into service. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the domicile requirement was constitutional. The court held that the bonus statute did not create a suspect classification. The court held that the domicile requirement of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 27-140a was not a durational residency requirement of the type that had some impact on the right of interstate travel. The court held that the veteran's right to travel was not effected because no matter how long the veteran resided in the state after the one year period set forth in § 27-140a, he could never become a member of the class benefited by the statute. The court held that the statute did not impinge upon a fundamental right or create a suspect classification and the distinction had a rational relationship to a legitimate state interest in granting benefits only those veterans who had a substantial nexus with the state prior to their entrance into service.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's denial of bonus benefits to the veteran and held that the domicile requirement for the veterans' bonus was constitutional.

Russo v. East Hartford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


179 Conn. 250; 425 A.2d 1282; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 947


October 11, 1979, Argued  
November 20, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an assessment of damages for land taken by the defendant for landfill use, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and referred to Hon. Louis Shapiro, state referee, who rendered judgment reassessing damages, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs landowners appealed a decision of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which rendered judgment reassessing damages for land taken by defendant town for landfill use.


OVERVIEW: The town condemned a tract of the landowners' land and filed a statement of compensation. The landowners had purchased the land and used it to dump the excess earth material from their excavating and land clearing business. A state statute enacted several years later classified the property as inland wetland requiring a permit before any regulated activity, such as filling, could be done. The town also enacted amendments to its zoning regulations which required a permit for excavation and filling operations. The landowners did not challenge these regulations. The town took the property for a landfill. The trial court granted the landowners damages. The court affirmed, finding that the trial court did not err in concluding that the landowners could not legally dump fill on the land at the time of the taking because the permits to fill had not been obtained. The court held that the town's failure to enforce the new regulations for almost three years did not estop it from exercising its police powers. The court found the evidence supported the trial court's finding that the legal effect of the regulations on the property affected the value of the property at the time of the taking.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court placing a value on the land taken by the town and awarding the landowners damages for the land taken by the town was affirmed.

Scalo v. Mandanici


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


179 Conn. 140; 425 A.2d 1272; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 921


May 2, 1979, Argued  
September 18, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the payment of salary increases to certain city of Bridgeport officials and employees and ordering the recovery of payments already made, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, I. Levine, J.; judgment ordering injunctive relief; on application by the plaintiffs, the court found the defendants in contempt for failure to comply with provisions of the injunction; thereafter, the court terminated the injunction and, on recovery of payments already made, vacated the finding of contempt; the plaintiffs and the defendants have appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant officials appealed from the decrees of the Fairfield County Superior Court (Connecticut) that enjoined the payment of salary increases to officials under a city ordinance and which found the officials in contempt for violating that injunction. Plaintiff challengers cross-appealed from decrees vacating the contempt finding and terminating the injunction upon a ruling that the ordinance did not violate Conn. Const. art. XI, § 2.


OVERVIEW: A city council passed an ordinance increasing salaries for elected and appointed officials. The challengers sued, claiming the ordinance was invalid. The superior court agreed that the ordinance was not legally enacted and enjoined the raises until they had been approved by the city's board of apportionment and taxation, as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-460. The city continued to pay the increased salaries, but five days later, the board approved the raises. The officials were found in contempt, but they purged themselves of contempt by recovering salary increases paid before board approval. The injunction was then dissolved. In affirming, the supreme court ruled that the ordinance was invalid prior to board approval because the board had final appropriation authority under Bridgeport, Conn., City Charter §§ 69 and 95. However, although Conn. Const. art. XI, § 2, prohibited the payment of gratuities to public officials, it did not forbid regular raises in compensation. Because it had been vacated, the contempt finding did not present an actual controversy for review.


OUTCOME: The decrees enjoining the salary increases, finding the officials in contempt, and vacating the contempt finding and injunction were affirmed.

State v. Anonymous


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


179 Conn. 155; 425 A.2d 939; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 920


June 13, 1979, Argued  
September 18, 1979, Decided

Hennessey, J.; judgment granting the petitions and appeal by the defendant from the judgment on the petition terminating parental rights.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mother appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court-Juvenile Matters for the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted the simultaneous petitions for neglect and termination of parental rights filed by plaintiff commissioner of children and youth services pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-43a(b). The mother appealed only from the decision to terminate her parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner filed simultaneous petitions of neglect and termination of parental rights against the mother on the grounds that the mother refused to take her infant child into her care and that she refused assistance that would have allowed her take the child into her care. The superior court granted the petitions. The mother appealed the termination of her parental rights, in part on grounds that she did not receive effective assistance of counsel. The issue of effective assistance of counsel during termination proceedings was one of first impression. Because of the substantial interests that were involved, the court found the mother did have a right to effective assistance of counsel. The court then determined that the mother had received effective assistance of counsel during the termination proceedings. The court also held that the portion of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45-61f under which the mother's parental rights were terminated was not vague because it was precise enough to warn the mother of what was and was not acceptable conduct. The court concluded that the simultaneous hearing of the termination and neglect petitions did not violate due process on its face and as applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which terminated the mother's parental rights.

Real Estate Listing Service, Inc. v. Connecticut Real Estate Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


179 Conn. 128; 425 A.2d 581; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 918; 17 A.L.R.4th 753


June 12, 1979, Argued  
September 11, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of a regulation of the defendant concerning exclusive listing agreements, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Kline, J.; judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, real estate listing service, appealed an order of Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut) that entered judgment for defendant Connecticut Real Estate Commission in a declaratory action filed to determine the validity of defendant's regulation concerning exclusive listing agreements.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the non-exclusive listing agreement was mostly an open listing that could be cancelled anytime and that the regulation was a valid exercise of the state's power to restrict the right to contract. The court did not adopt defendant's interpretation of the regulation but held that the regulation was constitutionally sound. The finding that the listing was an open listing was contrary to the contract's plain language. The broker promised to distribute the listing and solicit to find a purchaser and the owner promised to pay a commission if the property was sold at the listed price and agreed not to grant any exclusive listing. The mutual promises were sufficient consideration to support a bilateral contract. Defendant's interpretation of the regulation did not further a legitimate state interest and operated in an arbitrary manner to deprive plaintiff of a property right without due process. The court remanded the case with direction to modify the declaratory judgment. The broker did not violate the regulation by continuing to attempt to sell the property even when the owner made a later exclusive listing with another broker. Only the owner was in breach.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court with directions to modify the judgment.

State v. Harrison


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


178 Conn. 689; 425 A.2d 111; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 905


April 11, 1979, Argued  
August 28, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of accessory to attempted robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in New London County and tried to the jury before Alexander, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court in New London County (Connecticut), which convicted him of the crime of accessory to attempted robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-8, 53a-49(a)(2) after his car was used by two of his friends in an attempted robbery of a gas station and was abandoned at the gas station.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the crime of accessory to an attempted robbery in the first degree. Defendant's motion to set aside the jury verdict of guilty was denied, and he appealed. Defendant assigned 13 counts of error in the conduct of the trial proceedings, including a claim that the trial court erred in its instruction to the jury on defendant's intent, which was an element of the crime charged. Defendant claimed that the charge impermissibly shifted the burden of proof on the element of intent from the prosecution to him. Because the court's ruling on that issue was dispositive of the case, the court did not address the other claims of error. Although defendant's claim of error was not framed in constitutional language, the court analyzed the claim in light of the requirements of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court set aside the judgment because the jury instructions given at trial on the element of intent erroneously shifted the burden of proof of an essential element to the defendant and denied him the protections of the presumption of innocence and of due process of law. The court found that other portions of the instructions failed to cure the constitutional defect.


OUTCOME: The judgment was set aside and a new trial was ordered.

Rogan v. Board of Trustees


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


178 Conn. 579; 424 A.2d 274; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 885


June 15, 1979, Argued  
July 31, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for alleged violations of personnel policies by the defendant board, and for injunctive relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Dwyer, J.; judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a group of former school board employees, appealed an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland (Connecticut), which entered a judgment in favor of defendant, board of trustees for the state colleges, in plaintiffs' action for injunctive relief and to recover damages for their wrongful termination and for alleged violations of personnel policies by the board.


OVERVIEW: The employees brought an action against the board and alleged that the board had violated certain personnel policies when the board failed to give notice to the employees of its resolution to discontinue operations of the school campus on which the employees worked. The employees also alleged that the termination of their employment deprived them of due process of law. The board answered, and, by way of special defense, asserted that the individual members of the board were being sued in their official capacities as members of a state board relative to acts alleged by the employees to be within the scope of their statutory duties, that the action was thus a suit against the state, and that the state, not having consented to such a suit, was immune from suit. The trial court agreed and rendered judgment for the board, and the employees appealed. The court affirmed and held that an award of damages in the form of lost wages or back pay would have had the impermissible effect of controlling the activities of the state and would not merely have the effect of declaring the rights of the parties, but would control the activities of the board, and thus the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that favored the board of trustees in a wrongful termination action that a group of former employees had filed.

Hodge v. Hodge


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

178 Conn. 308; 422 A.2d 280; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 864

July 17, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a divorce, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in New London County and tried to the court, Wright, J.; judgment of a divorce, and orders for support and alimony, which the defendant thereafter moved to modify; the court, Jacobs, J., rendered judgment modifying only the order for support, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court in New London County (Connecticut), which denied the husband's motion to modify a divorce decree to eliminate the provision transferring the husband's interest in in-state property to appellee wife in lieu of alimony, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-22.


OVERVIEW: The wife instituted divorce proceedings against the husband. Although the husband did not appear, the trial court found that he had received actual notice and granted the wife the divorce and ordered the husband to pay child support and to transfer his in-state property to the wife. The husband filed a motion to modify both the child support order and the property transfer order, but the trial court vacated only the child support order. On appeal, the court held that § 52-22 provided the trial court with the power to transfer title. Regarding the husband's claim that he did not have adequate notice, the court found that pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46-21, the husband should have been aware that to satisfy the wife's claim for alimony, the trial court could assign to her some of the husband's property. The court rejected the husband's argument that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-22 was unconstitutional because his property had not been attached prior to trial, the court held that bringing his property within the trial court's jurisdiction was not a due process requirement for quasi in rem jurisdiction. Minimum contacts was sufficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the husband's motion to modify the property transfer order.

 

631 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Joy v. Joy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


178 Conn. 254; 423 A.2d 895; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 833


May 9, 1979, Argued  
July 3, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and referred to Hon. Raymond J. Devlin, state referee, who rendered judgment dissolving the marriage and ordering certain other relief, from which judgment the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant former husband sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which dissolved the marriage between him and plaintiff former wife on the basis of irreconcilable differences.


OVERVIEW: The main issue on appeal was the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46-32(c) insofar as it authorized a divorce decree upon a finding that a marriage had broken down irretrievably. The husband specifically claimed that § 46-32(c) was unconstitutional unless the court imposed judicial standards or guidelines to limit discretionary fact-finding by the trial courts. The court declined to circumscribe the process of fact finding by imposing the constraint of guidelines on an irreconcilable difference inquiry because it was necessarily individualized and particularized. The court further determined that the legislature had plenary power to determine the circumstances under which a marital relationship was created and terminated. The legislature could rationally conclude that public policy required an accommodation to the unfortunate reality that a marital relationship could terminate in fact without regard to the fault of either marital partner, and that such a relationship should therefore be dissoluble in law upon a judicial determination of irretrievable breakdown. The findings were consistent with those of other jurisdictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which dissolved the parties' marriage.

 

632 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kreminski


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


178 Conn. 145; 422 A.2d 294; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 818


January 10, 1979, Argued  
June 26, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in five counts charging the defendant with the crime of violating the provisions of the Connecticut Securities Act, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Wall, J.; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Hartford County (Connecticut), which convicted him of five counts of violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 36-334, a provision of the Connecticut Securities Act.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of violations of § 36-334. He appealed and argued that, because of the felony classification given to a violation of § 36-334, the requirement of mens rea should have been read into the statute. The court noted that another provision of the Act established a much more severe penalty for fraud in the sale of any security and would have rendered § 36-334 superfluous if it required fraudulent intent to be proved. The court also noted that the felony classification given to the crimes committed by defendant might have involved a forfeiture of his rights as an elector, but found that such additional consequence did not render defendant's sentence so grossly disproportionate to the offense as to breach the constitutional prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment. Defendant also claimed that the statutory provisions under which he was convicted were unconstitutionally vague. The court held that it was clear to men of common intelligence that the statute prohibited a registered salesman from selling securities except as an agent of his employer, who had to be a registered broker or dealer.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in defendant's conviction for violations of the Connecticut Securities Act.

 

633 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Grega v. Somers


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


178 Conn. 207; 423 A.2d 873; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 820


April 6, 1979, Argued  
June 26, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus alleging unlawful imprisonment, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Cohen, J.; judgment dismissing the writ, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a judgment in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford County (Connecticut), which dismissed his request for habeas corpus relief.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was arrested under Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 54-43 upon probable cause that he shot the victim. The affidavit set forth in detail all of the events leading to the murder charge. He was indicted by a grand jury and charged with the victim's murder. Following a plea of not guilty and a jury trial, petitioner was convicted of manslaughter in the first degree. Thereafter, the trial court dismissed his amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus seeking his release from confinement. Upon certification under Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 52-470, petitioner appealed. Petitioner asserted that former Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. §54-43 was unconstitutional on its face because the statute did not specifically provide for a warrant supported by oath or affirmation. On review, the court held that the statute did not require the explicit language regarding the warrant. The statute could be construed to be constitutionally valid. The court held that precedent was scrupulously followed, that the trial court had jurisdiction, and that petitioner's conviction was valid.


OUTCOME: The court found no error and affirmed.

 

634 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Nagle v. Wood


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


178 Conn. 180; 423 A.2d 875; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 821


April 4, 1979, Argued  
June 26, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the construction of the law governing the ascertainment of distributees of an intestate estate, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Cohen, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An action brought by plaintiff administrator was presented to the court for the construction of the law governing the ascertainment of defendant distributees of an intestate estate, reserved on stipulation by the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut). The essential issues was the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 45-274 and the effect of its amendment.


OVERVIEW: The intestate died leaving no surviving spouse. He was survived by his parents and two young children, whose mother had never married the decedent. During his lifetime, the decedent, the mother, and the children lived together as a family unit. The decedent acknowledged paternity, he was named as their father on their birth certificates, and he claimed them as dependents on his federal income tax return. The issue for reservation was whether the word "children" as used in Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 45-274 embraced illegitimate children. The distributees claimed that the statute as written at the time of the decedent's death was unconstitutional but that its amendment had retrospective effect. The court held that the children were not included within the statute. At the time of his death, the terms of § 45-274 barred illegitimate children from inheritance and required the subsequent marriage of the parents. The unnecessary exclusion of illegitimate children violated the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution. However, the court found nothing in the amendment indicating a clear legislative intent that the substantive changes created had a retrospective effect.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the statute was unconstitutional and that the amendment had prospective effect.
