In re Juvenile Appeal


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


177 Conn. 648; 420 A.2d 875; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 800


April 10, 1979, Argued  
June 12, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiff mother from the decision of the Juvenile Court for the second district denying her petition to revoke the commitment of her child to the defendant commissioner, and granting the defendant's petition to terminate the plaintiff's parental rights, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the court, Santaniello, J., which rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, and then to the court, Conway, J., which denied a motion for immediate visitation pending the appeal, from which denial the plaintiff filed a separate appeal to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother sought review of a judgment from a lower appellate court (Connecticut), which dismissed her appeal in which she challenged the trial court's denial of her petition to revoke the commitment of her child to defendant Commissioner of the Connecticut Department of Children and Youth Services and that granted the commissioner's petition to terminate plaintiff's parental rights.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a motion to revoke the commitment of her child to the department. The commissioner subsequently filed a motion to terminate plaintiff's parental rights to the child. The trial court denied plaintiff's motion to revoke the commitment and granted the commissioner's motion to terminate. A lower appellate court affirmed and dismissed plaintiff's appeal. Upon review, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court found the state met its burden of proving that the return of the child to plaintiff would not have been in the child's best interest pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-62(f) where there was evidence that plaintiff and her child had been separated for a one year and nine month period and that the child had developed a relationship with her foster family. The court held plaintiff's parental rights were improperly terminated where the evidence presented by the commissioner failed to satisfy the requirement under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-43a that there was an absence of an ongoing parent-child relationship between plaintiff and her child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed part of a judgment that dismissed plaintiff's appeal from a trial court's order denying her petition to revoke commitment. The court reversed and remanded part of a judgment that granted the commissioner's petition to terminate the parental rights of plaintiff.

 

636 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. De Witt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


177 Conn. 637; 419 A.2d 861; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 802


April 5, 1979, Argued  
June 12, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the third degree, robbery in the first degree, and kidnapping in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the jury before McCarthy, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which convicted him of burglary in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-103a, robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(2), and kidnapping in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-94 and 53a-91(2)(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a black male were tried jointly. The court held that the victim's movement at knife-point, his detention during a robbery, and his being left tied up, were sufficient to find the restraint and intent necessary to constitute kidnapping in the second degree. A pretrial identification of defendant was not unduly suggestive even though the victim was aware that a photograph of a suspect would be in a group of pictures and the photographs included several men with long hair, and one with glasses, although the victim indicated that the intruder had short hair and wore no glasses, given the victim's unrestricted opportunity to view defendant in full daylight for at least ten minutes, the accuracy of his description, and the brevity of time between the crime and the identification. Although a corridor confrontation between the victim and defendant was unconstitutional, it did not taint the victim's in-court identification where it was based on his original observation of defendant at the scene of the crime. The trial court acted within its discretion in denying a mistrial on the basis of the corridor confrontation where defendant was not substantially prejudiced.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

637 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Papa v. Greenwich Green, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


177 Conn. 295; 416 A.2d 1196; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 744


February 9, 1979, Argued  
April 10, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mechanic's lien, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County where the court, Saden, J., on motion by the defendants Thomas F. Walsh et al., rendered judgment discharging the mechanic's lien, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a general contractor, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which dismissed its mechanics lien pursuant to a motion filed by defendants, a developer and 31 condominium unit owners.


OVERVIEW: Upon completion of a condominium complex, the contractor filed a certificate of mechanic's lien with the town clerk and served a copy of the certificate on the developer. No service of the certificate was made upon the 31 defendant unit owners. The trial court dismissed the contractor's action to foreclose on the lien, on grounds that the contractor failed to serve all of the owners of the property as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-34, and because notice of intention to claim a mechanic's lien was not given to the owners of the condominium units, as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-35. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court stated that when an individual's property right might be adversely affected, he had a constitutional prerogative to a timely hearing, and was entitled to a fair and suitable notice of the recording of a mechanic's lien against that property. The court rejected the contractor's contention that the term "owner" as used in § 49-34 did not include the unit owners who acquired an ownership before the recording of the mechanic's lien.


OUTCOME: No error was found.

 

638 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Caldor's, Inc. v. Bedding Barn, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


177 Conn. 304; 417 A.2d 343; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 743; 10 A.L.R.4th 230


February 13, 1979, Argued  
April 10, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants from operating their businesses on Sunday, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Cioffi, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed and the defendants cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retail establishments appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) declaring 1978 Conn. Pub. Acts 329, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-302a (the Act), to be unconstitutional. Plaintiffs sought to enjoin the defendants, competing retail establishments, from engaging in business operations on Sundays in violation of the Act. Defendants cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had concluded that the Act was unconstitutional because it did not bear a reasonable and substantial relation to the legitimate state objective of providing a common day of rest for workers. The Act did not prohibit Sunday employment of most of Connecticut's workers. The court held that the Act was unconstitutional, but for a different reason. The Sunday closing law, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-302a, as reenacted by 1978 Conn. Pub. Acts 329, failed the rational connection test because its classifications were too arbitrary, discriminatory, and unreasonable to comport with the requirements of equal protection and due process. As an example, various food items could be sold by small retail food stores, retail drug stores, prepared food service organizations, and dairies, but not by a supermarket. There was no rational connection between the items whose availability the legislature deemed appropriate to a day of rest and recreation, and the business establishments permitted to offer them for sale. The court held that that the defendants had sustained their burden of demonstrating that § 53-302a was unconstitutional as a violation of equal protection and due process.


OUTCOME: Both the appeal of the plaintiffs and the cross-appeal of the defendants were sustained insofar as they challenged the basis upon which the judgment of the trial court was predicated. However, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

639 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Monroe v. Monroe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


177 Conn. 173; 413 A.2d 819; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 728


January 2, 1979, Argued  
March 27, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motions by the plaintiff to vacate a judgment of divorce, brought to the Superior Court in New London County where the court, at separate hearings before Jacobs, J., and Daly, J., denied the plaintiff's motions to vacate and granted the defendant's motions to erase, and appeal by the plaintiff to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife appealed an order by the Superior Court in New London County (Connecticut), which denied her motion to vacate a judgment of divorce and granted defendant husband's motion to erase. The wife contended that the state referee who rendered the decree of dissolution lacked subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The wife's divorce action was referred to a state referee. The referee granted a divorce and incorporated the stipulated settlement of the parties into the judgment. Neither party had signed the stipulation, nor did they testify at the hearing. The wife's counsel informed the referee that each party had discussed "each aspect" of the settlement with their counsel and accepted its terms. Neither party appealed the judgment. Several years later, the wife sought to set aside the judgment. The trial court denied her motion. On appeal, the court found no error, concluding the Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-434, which permitted retired judges to serve as referees, was constitutional. The court also found that the wife had not sustained her burden of establishing a miscarriage of justice to set aside the judgment. The wife was bound by the acts of her attorney. The referee's failure to inquire as to the parties' actual consent to the stipulation did not make the judgment vulnerable to collateral attack as a miscarriage of justice. The court noted that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-51 now requires parties, not their attorneys, to make written or oral in-court stipulations.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

640 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Frazier v. Manson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


176 Conn. 638; 410 A.2d 475; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 708


November 7, 1978, Argued  
February 27, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus alleging unlawful imprisonment, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Henebry, J., for the advice of this court.

The plaintiff filed a motion for reargument which was denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner brought a habeas corpus petition, which the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) reserved for the advice of the court as to whether the good time provision of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-7a was applicable to persons sentenced to a term of imprisonment prior to the effective date of the act, and, if not, whether lack of retroactive application violated equal protection under the Fourteenth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, § 20.


OVERVIEW: Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-7, which remained in effect for prisoners sentenced prior to the date of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-7a, provided less good time credit than § 18-7a. The court held that the plain language of § 18-7a, which stated that it applied to any person sentenced on or after October 1, 1976, was unambiguous, so that there was no reason to further construe it. Furthermore, there was no repugnancy between the two statutes. The legislature intended that the two groups of prisoners be sentenced according to the applicable statutes, and that result was neither unreasonable nor irrational. The court also held that denial of retroactive application of § 18-7a did not violate due process. The court first noted that the Fourteenth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, § 20, had a like meaning and imposed similar constitutional limitations. The court then held that the legislative classification of the prisoners was not inherently suspect and that the legislation did not impinge upon a fundamental right. Thus, strict scrutiny was not required. The legislation had a rational basis and was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court advised the trial court that the statute at issue did not apply to prisoners sentenced prior to October 1, 1976, and that failure to apply the statute retroactively did not violate equal protection.

 

641 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


McKinney v. Coventry


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


176 Conn. 613; 410 A.2d 453; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 677


November 15, 1978, Argued  
February 13, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the return of a conveyance tax paid under protest by the plaintiffs, and for an injunction, brought to the Superior Court in Tolland County and tried to the court, Driscoll, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in Tolland County (Connecticut) that denied their claim for a refund of the conveyance tax paid under 1972 Conn. Acts 152 and that also denied a request for a permanent injunction restraining defendant county from imposing the tax.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers contended that 1972 Conn. Acts 152, § 1 which imposed a conveyance tax on property classified as farmland and transferred within the first 10 years of that classification was unconstitutionally vague as to the "holding period" which determined the sliding scale rate of tax. The court rejected the contention and affirmed the judgment in favor of the county. A reading of the § 1 made it clear that the tax was imposed when classified farmland was sold within a period of 10 years from the time of initial acquisition or classification, whichever is earlier. Thus, in terms of due process analysis, it was reasonably clear, certain, and sufficiently definite to provide a person of ordinary intelligence with a reasonable opportunity to comprehend its meaning. Also, § 1 sufficiently informed a person that "tacking" of successive periods of ownership was not authorized in order to defeat the tax. Furthermore, even if the statute was susceptible to different interpretations that did not void it because the level of scrutiny was less for such a statute as compared to one that regulated First Amendment rights or to a penal statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied the taxpayers' claim for refund of the conveyance tax and that denied them a permanent injunction restraining the county from imposing the tax.

643 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Society for Sav. v. Chestnut Estates


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


176 Conn. 563; 409 A.2d 1020; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 681


October 19, 1978, Argued  
February 6, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mortgage, brought to the Superior Court in Tolland County where, after judgment of strict foreclosure, the court, Sidor, J., appointed appraisers who filed their report, to which the defendant Vincent Osowiecki filed an objection; the court, Wright, J., overruled the objection to the report and sustained a demurrer to the defendant Osowiecki's objection to the plaintiff's motion for a deficiency judgment; the court, Burns, J., rendered a deficiency judgment for the plaintiff which was modified by the court, Henebry, J., from which the defendant Osowiecki appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mortgagee sought review of the decision of the Superior Court in Tolland County (Connecticut), which overruled the mortgagee's objection to the appraiser's report and entered a deficiency judgment in favor of plaintiff mortgagor in its action to foreclose the mortgage.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagor bought a foreclosure action against the mortgagee on 41 parcels of land, with buildings and improvements. The trial court ordered a foreclosure and appraisers were appointed. Based upon the appraisers' report, the trial court entered a deficiency judgment. On appeal, the mortgagee contended that the statute providing for the appointment of appraisers, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-14, was unconstitutional because it violated the Due Process clause of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and the Conn. Const. art. 1, §10. The court found that the property right at issue was constitutionally cognizable because the appraisers' conclusion as to the value of the property determined how much the mortgagee owned on the note. The procedure in § 49-14 did not provide the mortgagee with the notice and opportunity to be heard. The statute was constitutionally defective both because it did not require that the mortgagee be afforded an opportunity to have participated in the determination of the value of the property by presenting evidence and because it did not provide the opportunity for cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment and remanded with directions to enter judgment for the mortgagee.

 

644 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Vecchio v. Sewer Authority of Branford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


176 Conn. 497; 408 A.2d 254; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 685


November 14, 1978, Argued  
January 23, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from levies of sewer assessments by the defendant, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County where the court, Belinkie, J., sustained the defendant's plea in abatement and rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners brought suit against defendant, a town sewer authority, challenging sewer assessments. Plaintiffs appealed from the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County (Connecticut), which sustained defendant's plea in abatement and rendered judgment dismissing the appeal under Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 7-250.


OVERVIEW: The landowners appealed from an assessment of benefits levied by the sewer authority for the construction of a town sewage system. The town filed a plea in abatement, alleging that the court was without jurisdiction to entertain the appeal because the landowners failed to file their appeal within 21 days of the filing of the assessment as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 7-250. The trial court sustained the plea in abatement. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment, holding that the failure to receive notice did not preclude the trial court from making a determination that it was, in fact, actually sent in accordance with the provisions of the statute. The court thus reasoned that the city's plea in abatement was properly sustained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the landowners' appeal.

 

645 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Zeko


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


176 Conn. 421; 407 A.2d 1022; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 665


November 7, 1978, Argued  
January 9, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of failure to appear in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the jury before O'Brien, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which convicted him of failure to appear under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-172. He alleged that the trial court erred in denying his pretrial motions, in its charge to the jury, and that § 53a-172 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that he was prejudiced by the trial court's action in permitting the failure to appear case to be tried before his arson case. Defendant alleged that this sequence of trials enabled the State to use the conviction obtained in the failure to appear case as evidence of consciousness of guilt in the arson case. The trial court found that the State's grounds for proceeding with the failure to appear case first was sufficient to constitute good cause. The court affirmed the conviction and held that the trial court was well within its discretion in denying the motion. The court upheld the denial of defendant's motion to suppress statements made to the bondsman. The court held that at the time that he made the statements, defendant was not in police custody. The person to whom he made the statements was neither a police officer nor a member of the prosecutor's office. Therefore, Miranda warnings were not necessary. Finally, the court held that § 53a-172 was constitutional because it reasonably related to the State's interest in assuring the smooth functioning of its courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for failure to appear.

Andrulat v. Brook Hollow Associates


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


176 Conn. 409; 407 A.2d 1017; 1979 Conn. LEXIS 663


November 14, 1978, Argued  
January 2, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover on a bond substituted by the defendants for the plaintiff's certificate of mechanic's lien, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County where the court, O'Brien, J., rendered summary judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to recover on a bond substituted by defendants a landowner and a surety, for plaintiff contractor's certificate of mechanic's lien, the contractor appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) entered in favor of the landowner and the surety. The contractor contended that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-39 did not bar the action.


OVERVIEW: The contractor alleged that he rendered services and furnished materials to premises owned by the landowners and that he filed a mechanics lien. The landowners and the surety substituted a bond for the lien. Subsequently Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-39 reduced the limitations period to one year but allowed prior liens to be "validated" until September 23, 1975 under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-37a. The contractor contended that his action was timely because he filed his action within one year of validating his lien. The court affirmed the judgment for landowner and the surety. The court held that the contractor's action was barred because the statute of limitations was tolled for a few months by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-37a until the contractor validated his lien but the period of limitations started when the lien was file and not when the lien was validated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding that the contractor's action against the landowner and the surety was time barred.

 

647 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Connecticut Light & Power Co. v. Public Utilities Control Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


176 Conn. 191; 405 A.2d 638; 1978 Conn. LEXIS 991


July 26, 1978, Argued  
October 3, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for review of orders of the defendant authority, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Covello, J.; judgment remanding the case for further proceedings, from which the defendants appealed to this court.

The appellees filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant electric authority and intervening defendants, officer of consumer counsel, a consumer group, and others, challenged the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut) that remanded the case to the authority for further proceedings. Petitioner electric companies had appealed the grant of applications for rate increases. Intervening defendants had cross-claimed that the applications should have been dismissed.


OVERVIEW: Intervening defendants' claim that the authority should have dismissed the applications was based on a provision in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-19(a) directing public service companies to file with the authority proposed amendments of their "existing rates." Intervening defendants argued that at the time the applications were filed, there were no "existing rates" because litigation was then pending concerning the rates. The court held that there were existing rates and thus the trial court had jurisdiction over the subject applications. The electric companies claimed that the authority wrongfully and unreasonably limited the companies to a 13 percent return on equity, but because no party appealed the trial court's decision to overrule those claims, the court found that the rate met both constitutional requirements and those of § 16-19e(a)(4). However, the court found that the authority's ruling that amortization would not be allowed if the expenses had been fully amortized on the books of the company was inconsistent with the purpose of its order authorizing amortization. Because of that inconsistency, the ruling was "arbitrary" within the purview of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183(g)(6).


OUTCOME: The court found error in part in the trial court's decision that upheld the authority's ruling regarding amortization. The court remanded the case to the trial court with directions to modify its decision.

 

648 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Eighth Utilities Dist. v. Town of Manchester


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


176 Conn. 43; 404 A.2d 898; 1978 Conn. LEXIS 1024


May 3, 1978, Argued  
August 29, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the right of the named plaintiff to extend its boundary lines and to furnish fire protection in a certain area, and for injunctive relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Hamill, J.; judgment for the named plaintiff, including injunctive relief, from which the named defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which issued a permanent injunction in favor of plaintiff, a utilities district, enjoining the town from interfering with the district's right to extend its boundary lines and to furnish fire protection to a particular area of the town.


OVERVIEW: A majority of the owners of real property in the area filed applications with the district to be included in its service area. The district voters decided to extend their boundary lines to furnish fire protection to the area. The town claimed that § 4 of 1963 Conn. Acts 184, No. 200 recognized that the town, having provided the area with fire protection continuously since 1957 -- albeit through a contract with the district -- was authorized to continue this service exclusively for so long as it so desired. The court found that the town's argument failed to encompass the other relevant provisions of the Act. Section 2 of 1963 Conn. Acts 184, No. 200 defined the area in which the district was authorized to provide its services and § 6 of 1963 Conn. Acts 184, No. 200 provided the mode by which this could occur. The court agreed with the trial court that this right remained with the area's property owners since 1939 and that by virtue of their application and the district's acceptance of the application, the district was entitled to extend its boundaries to include the area.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's issuance of the permanent injunction enjoining the town from interfering with the district's right to furnish fire protection to a particular section of the town.

 

649 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Stolberg v. Caldwell


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


175 Conn. 586; 402 A.2d 763; 1978 Conn. LEXIS 1031


June 9, 1978, Argued  
August 8, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action of mandamus to require the defendants to make prompt payment to the plaintiff of his teaching salary, consolidated with an amicable suit to determine the legal duties of the parties, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and reserved by that court, Aaronson, J., upon an agreed statement of facts for the consideration and advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff legislator and defendants, the State Comptroller, chairmen and boards of trustees of Connecticut's state colleges, and Connecticut auditors of public accounts, sought a determination of whether the legislator's employment as legislator and state college faculty violated the dual-job ban of Conn. Const. art. 3, § 11. The Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) sought the court's consideration and advice.


OVERVIEW: The legislator had been on the faculty of a state college when he was discharged. Subsequently, a federal court reinstated him with tenure. In between, he was elected to the state legislature. The comptroller stopped paying the legislator his faculty salary. The legislator filed a mandamus action. The court determined that the legislator's employment as faculty at a state college violated the dual-job ban under Conn. Const. art. 3, § 11. A faculty position was an appointive position to a job in the executive branch. Under § 11, a legislator could not hold an appointive position in either the executive or judicial branches. The provision was not vague or overbroad because it specifically prohibited the activities of the legislator. Because the legislator was in violation of the dual-job ban, he impliedly relinquished his faculty position. The legislator could not claim a clear right to his faculty position; therefore, a mandamus action was inappropriate.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the legislator was violating the dual-job ban by holding a faculty position at a state college.

 

650 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Mazzola v. Commissioner of Transp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


175 Conn. 576; 402 A.2d 786; 1978 Conn. LEXIS 1033


February 15, 1978, Argued  
August 8, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an assessment of damages for land taken for highway purposes, brought to the Superior Court in Windham County and referred to Hon. Raymond E. Baldwin, state referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment for the plaintiffs, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state transportation commissioner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in Windham County (Connecticut), which was in favor of plaintiff landowners in their action for review of the compensation for land that the state transportation commissioner condemned for highway purposes.


OVERVIEW: After the state transportation commissioner condemned part of certain property for highway purposes and assessed damages, the landowners applied to the trial court for a review of the compensation. A referee found that the property had a higher fair market value, and the trial court entered a judgment for the landowners. The state transportation commissioner contended on appeal that the referee erroneously included in his valuation portions of the property that were devoted to an unlawful use. The court set aside the judgment and ordered a new trial. The court found that the referee was limited to a consideration of factors that legitimately affected the land's value. The court further found that the referee could not consider the valuation of spaces in a mobile home park that could not comply with the requirements of a mobile home ordinance unless the use was otherwise permissible. The court concluded that it was not reasonably probable that a waiver provision in the ordinance would be upheld and that an amendment was too speculative to have any legitimate effect upon valuation. The court also concluded that the remainder of the ordinance was severable from the waiver provision.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment in favor of the landowners and ordered a new trial in the action for review of the compensation for the land that the state transportation commissioner condemned.

 

651 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hawthorne


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


175 Conn. 569; 402 A.2d 759; 1978 Conn. LEXIS 1041


June 13, 1978, Argued  
August 1, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Zarrilli, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which entered the jury's verdict convicting defendant of robbery in the first degree. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in charging the jury and overruling defendant's claims of law regarding the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another allegedly placed pistols, one at a cashier's neck and one at the cashier's chest, and took the money from the cash register of a gas station. The pistols were recovered from the car from which defendant was apprehended. The cashier identified the pistols at trial as those used in the robbery. The State did not introduce any evidence that either of the pistols were capable of being fired. Defendant did not introduce any evidence that the pistol he used was incapable of being fired. The trial court charged the jury with determining whether the pistol was operable or not. As a matter of first impression, the court determined that § 53a-134(a)(4) was constitutional. The court found that § 53a-134(a)(4) did not impermissibly shift to defendant the burden of proving the inoperability of a firearm displayed during the commission of a robbery as an affirmative defense. The court concluded that the State had no burden of proving that a firearm displayed during the commission of a robbery was operable. The court found no error in the trial court's charge to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Anderson v. Ludgin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


175 Conn. 545; 400 A.2d 712; 1978 Conn. LEXIS 1045


May 11, 1978, Argued  
August 1, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition seeking to review the action of the town clerk and other election officials in certifying that the named defendant was elected to office, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Parskey, J.; judgment dismissing the petition, from which the plaintiff appealed and the defendants cross-appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff candidate challenged the decision of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which dismissed her petition seeking to review the action of defendant officials in certifying that defendant councilman was elected to office.


OVERVIEW: The councilman received the ninth greatest number of votes at the election, and the candidate received the tenth greatest number. Only the top nine vote receivers were declared and certified to have been elected to city council. The issue was whether the minority representation statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-167a, applied to local legislative bodies and, if so, whether the statute, as applied, was unconstitutional. The trial court concluded that § 9-167a was applicable to legislative bodies such as the council, but that it was unconstitutional as applied to the councilman. On review, the court found no error. The court found that because there was no specific reference to "council" or "legislative body" in the statute, it had to be read to exclude such bodies from its scope. The court determined that § 9-167a had been interpreted consistently to exclude legislative bodies. The statute was not applicable, the court held, to local legislative bodies like the city council.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the dismissal of the petition seeking to review the action of the officials in certifying that the councilman was elected to office.

Jones v. Warden, Community Correctional Center


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


175 Conn. 147; 394 A.2d 723; 1978 Conn. LEXIS 936


January 5, 1978, Argued  
May 16, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus alleging unlawful imprisonment, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the court, Berdon, J.; judgment ordering the state to provide a hearing within seven days or to strike from his administrative records the mittimus, from which the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant correctional center warden, who was holding plaintiff inmate, complained of a judgment of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which ordered the warden to strike a previously granted mittimus from his administrative records upon the inmate's execution of a promise to appear, unless the state held a hearing.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that he was being held illegally because the bondsman was discharged from his obligations as surety to the inmate in an ex-parte proceeding without notice to him. The trial court concluded that, while the bondsman and the judge acted properly, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-319 and 54-65 were unconstitutional as violative of due process. After the trial court's judgment and while appeal was pending, the inmate pleaded guilty to a lesser narcotics charge and was awaiting sentencing. Upon review, the court held that the controversy had been rendered moot. Because the inmate had already pled guilty to the charge for which he had posted bond, whatever relief an opinion of the court could afford the warden was no longer relevant because there was no longer any actual controversy. The warden's authority to hold the inmate under the mittimus, which was successfully challenged by the habeas corpus petition, was no longer the basis for the inmate's confinement. Consequently, there existed no possibility that an opinion would give the warden any practical relief. The case, lacking in actual controversy, was moot.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal as moot.

Engle v. Personnel Appeal Board


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


175 Conn. 127; 394 A.2d 731; 1978 Conn. LEXIS 939


December 13, 1977, Argued  
May 16, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision of the defendant board that the plaintiff was not entitled to additional compensation for working "out of class," brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Martin, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee challenged the judgment from the Court of Common Pleas Hartford County (Connecticut), which upheld a decision by defendant Personnel Appeal Board of the State of Connecticut that the employee was not entitled to additional compensation. The primary claim was that approval of the Personnel Commissioner was not required under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-209 (1967) before the employee could be compensated for "working out of class."


OVERVIEW: Although the employee was assigned to work in a higher classification, her employer did not apply for approval of payment at the higher class rate until almost eight months later. Both the Personnel Appeal Board and the trial court determined that payments under § 5-209 required prior approval by the Personnel Commissioner and, because such approval was not obtained, payments were properly denied. On further appeal, the court held that § 5-209 was constitutional, that approval of payments by the personnel commissioner was mandatory, and that § 5-209 had to be complied with strictly. Because such approval was not obtained, payments to the employee were properly denied. Given the barren state of the record, the court could not reach the issue of estoppel raised by the employee. The employee's claim that she was entitled to recovery on a theory of unjust enrichment was similarly without merit because, in the absence of a statute such as § 5-209, there was no right to compensation for duties performed out of class.


OUTCOME: No error was found.

New Haven Water Co. v. North Branford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


174 Conn. 556; 392 A.2d 456; 1978 Conn. LEXIS 869


January 5, 1978, Argued  
April 10, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiff from the action of the defendant in refusing to reduce its assessment of certain personal property, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County and referred to Hon. Patrick B. O'Sullivan, a state referee, who, sitting as the court, rendered judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer water company sought review from the judgment of the State Referee, who rendered judgment in favor of defendant town in an action based on the town's refusal to reduce the assessment of property taxes of the taxpayer pursuant to an amended statute.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers property was assessed by the town. The town failed to use the method of valuation prescribed by Public Act No. 439 but computed the assessment on the basis of reproduction cost less depreciation and, using this formula, arrived at a tax assessment of $ 3,032,720 for each of the two years. The taxpayer sought review of the assessment. The lower court found in favor of the town. The taxpayer appealed. On appeal, the court found that the lower court committed error in upholding the town's assessment. The court held that Public Act No. 439 was not invalid on the ground that the method of assessment it prescribed was one which, by inference, was forbidden by Conn. Gen Stat. §§ 12-64 and 12-71. The court noted that the language of Public Act No. 439 was specific and in no way ambiguous. Accordingly, the court ordered that the taxpayer be refunded the overpayment of taxes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and directed that the amount the taxpayer was overtaxed was to be returned.

Bell v. Planning & Zoning Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


174 Conn. 493; 391 A.2d 154; 1978 Conn. LEXIS 860


December 8, 1977, Argued  
April 4, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiff from the granting of a special zoning permit to the defendant Westport housing authority, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford and tried to the court, Herman, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trustee appealed an order of the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford (Connecticut), which dismissed his appeal of the granting of a special zoning permit to defendant city housing authority allowing for the construction of 50 multifamily housing units for the elderly.


OVERVIEW: The trustee, acting for a rival applicant, appealed a city zoning commission decision approving the housing authority's application to construct housing for the elderly. The appeal was dismissed because the trustee failed to demonstrate aggrievement under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8 and 8-9. The court held that the fact that the granting of the permit might affect the city's comprehensive plan did not render the trustee aggrieved as a matter of law. Further, the facts did not indicate that the trustee's specific interest rendered him "aggrieved" by any modification of the town's plan. The trustee's claim that as a taxpayer he was "aggrieved" by the unconstitutional expenditure of funds on the project was without merit because the trustee failed to show that his rights or interests were specially and adversely affected. The trustee's interest thus was no greater than that of any town taxpayer and did not rise to the level of "aggrievement" required by § 8-8 and 8-9. The trustee did not have standing to assert his claim as an individual that as a person under 62 years of age, he was excluded from occupancy in the proposed project in violation of his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

New Milford v. SCA Services of Connecticut, Inc.

New Haven Sav. Bank v. Valley Investors


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


174 Conn. 77; 384 A.2d 321; 1977 Conn. LEXIS 802


October 7, 1977, Argued  
December 20, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the foreclosure of a mortgage, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County where, after a judgment of strict foreclosure and failure to redeem, the plaintiff sought a deficiency judgment; appraisers were appointed who filed their report, to which the defendant Richard R. Splain filed an objection; the court, Berdon, J., sustained that objection and denied the plaintiff's motion to accept the report, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bank challenged the decision of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which sustained defendant investors' objection to the appraiser's report and denied its motion to accept the appraiser's report in an action for foreclosure of a mortgage.


OVERVIEW: A judgment of strict foreclosure was rendered against the investors and upon their failure to redeem, the bank took title to the mortgaged property. Thereafter, the bank sought a deficiency judgment and made a timely motion, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-14, for the appointment of three disinterested appraisers. The appraisers filed their report and the bank filed a motion for acceptance of the appraisers' report. The investors filed an objection to the report on the ground that one of the appraisers, did not personally conduct a formal evaluation, but relied upon the advice and opinion of other persons. On appeal, the court held that the objection should have been overruled because the facts illustrated that the appraiser inspected the property and reached a conclusion as to value. Under these facts, the court held that trial court erred when found that appraiser failed to exercise his own independent judgment in arriving at the value of the property. Additionally, the court held that the appraiser did not diverge from the strict compliance with § 49-14 by consulting with another appraiser.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision that had denied the bank's motion to sustain the appraiser's report, and had sustained the investors' objection to the report. The court remanded with instructions to accept the report and grant the bank's motion for a deficiency judgment.

Waterbury Motor Lease, Inc. v. Tax Comm'r


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


174 Conn. 51; 381 A.2d 552; 1977 Conn. LEXIS 799


October 5, 1977, Argued  
December 20, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from decisions of the defendant, refusing to refund taxes, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and reserved by the court, McKeever, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought the advisory opinion of the court after it appealed orders of defendant, the Tax Commissioner of the State of Connecticut, which refused to refund sales taxes to the taxpayers that were paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers paid sales taxes under protest and sought a refund from the commissioner. The commissioner denied the requests for refunds. The trial court sought the court's opinion, as the taxpayers claimed that 1975 Conn. Acts 213 was unconstitutional. The taxpayers asserted that while the act created a new classification of persons subject to the sales and use tax, which may have a rational basis, such a classification was unconstitutional because it treated some lessees differently. On appeal, the court found that the challenged statutory provisions were constitutional, holding that within the particular class selected for payment of the tax, namely, lessees, the members were treated equally and uniformly, that there was no denial of equal protection of the laws, and that the fact that the lessor passed on to its lessee the expense of the tax which it had paid in purchasing the vehicle did not make the tax imposed by the act upon the lessees a double tax.


OUTCOME: The court found that the challenged statutory provisions were constitutional.

State v. Williams


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


173 Conn. 545; 378 A.2d 588; 1977 Conn. LEXIS 879


April 6, 1977, Argued  
October 11, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the second degree and with being a persistent dangerous felony offender, and information charging the defendant with two counts of larceny in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in New London County and tried to the jury before Santaniello, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in New London County (Connecticut), which convicted him of robbery in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-135(a)(2), of being a persistent dangerous felony offender as defined by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40 (a), and of larceny in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-123.


OVERVIEW: Along with one other, defendant, who was armed, entered the rear of a restaurant, tied the hands of the two dishwashers, and ushered them into the main room of the restaurant where one of the men announced to the owner and a waitress that it was a holdup. Defendant later stole a vehicle. Defendant was convicted of robbery, larceny, and of being a persistent dangerous felony offender. He was sentenced to a term of not less than 12 years nor more than life on the indictment and not less than one nor more than three years on each count of the information. He sought review. On appeal, the court found no error. The court held that under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-119, the reception of stolen property constituted the crime of larceny when it was received knowing that it had probably been stolen or believing that it had probably been stolen. The court further ruled that proof of possession of recently stolen property by itself, not satisfactorily explained, could support a conviction of larceny. The court declined to review the proper exercise of the trial court's discretion in imposing a sentence that was within the limits fixed by statute for the offense charged.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

 

661 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Heffernan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


173 Conn. 506; 378 A.2d 572; 1977 Conn. LEXIS 875


June 8, 1977, Argued  
September 27, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiffs from the denial by the defendant of a tax refund, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Alexander, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of issues reserved by the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) after defendant commissioner denied their application for a tax refund based on their challenge to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-506, which imposed a tax upon all dividends received by taxpayers with adjusted gross incomes of $ 20,000 or more, and § 12-505, which defined "taxpayer" to include a husband and wife who filed a joint federal return.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed a state capital gains and dividends tax return, paying the prescribed tax. Simultaneously, they filed a claim for refund. The commissioner denied their claim for a refund. The trial court reserved decision pending advice of the court. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional. The statute did not violate equal protection guarantees because it was not invidious or palpably arbitrary. The $ 20,000 exemption provision (subsequently repealed) did not constitute a taking of property without due process of law. A state tax law conflicted with the Fourteenth Amendment only where it proposed, or resulted in, such flagrant and palpable inequality between the burden imposed and the benefit received as to amount to the arbitrary taking of property without compensation. Married taxpayers could take advantage of the benefits accruing under federal law through joint filing or those granted under state law through separate filing. The inequality of result came from the taxpayers' election to avail themselves of privileges offered to all, which did not constitute an infringement upon equal protection guarantees. Denial of the claim was in accordance with law.


OUTCOME: The court found that the challenged provisions were constitutional.

 

662 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Rybinski v. State Employees' Retirement Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


173 Conn. 462; 378 A.2d 547; 1977 Conn. LEXIS 872


April 6, 1977, Argued  
September 13, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an action of the defendant in refusing to permit the plaintiff to change her retirement plan, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County where the court, Covello, J., sustained the defendant's plea in abatement and rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, from which judgment the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed a decision from the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which sustained defendant State Employees' Retirement Commission's plea in abatement and dismissed the action, after finding that the employee was not entitled to judicial review pursuant to the Uniform Administrative Procedure Act (UAPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 4-166 through 4-188, and that the court was without jurisdiction to hear the case.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue for consideration was whether the employee had access to the court through the appeal provisions of the UAPA entitling a party to judicial review of an agency's decision. The only facts found by the lower court related to the plea in abatement. They indicate only that the Commission's decision concerned its denial of the employee's requested change in her retirement plans. In order to obtain judicial review under the UAPA, the employee was required to show that the proceeding in which the Commission denied her request to change retirement plans was a contested case to which the judicial review provisions of the UAPA applied. The court found nothing in the State Employees' Retirement Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. ch. 66, which obliged the Commission to provide an opportunity for a hearing. It further found that the employee had not established that the Commission's proceeding involved a contested case. Thus, the UAPA judicial review provisions did not entitle the employee to appeal. Because there was no other statutory authorization for an appeal to the court from the Commission's decision, the plea in abatement was correctly sustained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision which held that the court of common pleas did not have jurisdiction to consider the employee's appeal.

State v. Maresca


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


173 Conn. 450; 377 A.2d 1330; 1977 Conn. LEXIS 871


May 5, 1977, Argued  
September 6, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of policy playing and destruction of property, and, in the second part, with being a second offender, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the jury before David M. Shea, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty in both parts, and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), where he was convicted of policy playing in violation of former Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-298 and of destruction of property to prevent seizure by a police officer in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-33e. At a second trial with a separate jury defendant was convicted of being a second offender under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-298.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of policy playing, of destruction of property to prevent seizure by a police officer, and of being a second offender. Both trials were by juries of six. Defendant appealed from the judgment rendered on the verdicts. Defendant claimed, among other arguments, that his trials by juries of six were in violation of the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws, U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10, because at the time that the offenses were alleged to have been committed, defendant had the right to be tried by a jury of 12. On review, the court observed that, although defendant elected to be tried by a jury of 12 in each case, the trial court ordered a jury of six. The court went on to note that the United States Supreme Court had held that a jury of six was not unconstitutional. The court also determined that the trial court was not in error in refusing to order a mistrial based upon subtle innuendo about a search of defendant's premises on a prior occasion. Finally, there was no error in the jury charges because the trial court properly instructed the jury in all respects.


OUTCOME: There was no error.

State v. Kinsey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


173 Conn. 344; 377 A.2d 1095; 1977 Conn. LEXIS 859

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of the sale of narcotics, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the jury before Wright, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence and convicted defendant of the sale of narcotics in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in an information with the sale of narcotics and found guilty on a trial to a jury. On appeal, defendant challenged the denial of his motion to suppress evidence and alleged error in rulings on evidence and in the trial court's permitting certain arguments to the jury. The court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence relating to an array of photographs. The court held that the photographic identification procedure employed by the police was not impermissibly tainted. The court noted that the array consisted of photographs of individuals of approximately the same size, age, and build as defendant, and the police officer identified defendant without hesitation. The court held that the trial court did not err in not admitting evidence of alleged third party involvement, as it within the trial court's discretion to determine whether evidence offered was remote or relevant. The court held that the state's attorney did not make improper comments to the jury, as defendant introduced evidence concerning the subject matter of the statements.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

665 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


East Village Associates, Inc. v. Monroe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


173 Conn. 328; 377 A.2d 1092; 1977 Conn. LEXIS 856


June 8, 1977, Argued  
July 26, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiff from an action of the board of tax review of the town of Monroe, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Satter, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town appealed a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut) that sustained plaintiff corporation's appeal of a decision of the city's Board of Tax Review. The board had denied the corporation's petition for relief from the imposition of a conveyance tax pursuant to the Real Estate Conveyance Tax Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-504a (1972), and for removal of the assessor's lien on its property.


OVERVIEW: The corporation owned land in the town. In 1971, the corporation's predecessor in title applied for and received exemptions on the 1971 property tax list for land classified as forest land and farm land. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-504a (1972) was then enacted. Section 12-504a provided for a conveyance tax on any land classified as farm or forest land that was sold within 10 years of classification or acquisition. In 1971 and 1972, agricultural and forest exemptions were not automatically continued from year to year. Taxpayers had to reapply annually. The corporation did not apply for special classification on the 1972 tax list and was taxed that year on the same basis as nonexempt property. The tax assessor recorded a lien and refused to record the corporation's conveyance deeds until the tax was paid. The conveyance tax was intended for prospective application only. Both the classification and sale had to occur after the effective date of § 12-504a to have the tax operate prospectively. The corporation did not reclassify its land after the effective date of § 12-504a; thus, the trial court correctly held that the conveyance tax did not apply to subsequent sales.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

666 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Chetcuti


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


173 Conn. 165; 377 A.2d 263; 1977 Conn. LEXIS 832


April 5, 1977, Argued  
June 7, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Tierney, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted him of kidnapping in the first degree for abducting a young woman with the intent to violate or abuse her sexually, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(A). Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in failing to charge the jury as he requested.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in failing to charge on the elements of the additional crimes of assault in the first degree, assault in the second degree, and sexual contact in the first degree; and in failing to charge on the significance of the abduction as being incidental to the commission of some other crime. The court found that assault in the first degree, assault in the second degree, and sexual contact involved elements not necessary to establish the crime of kidnapping in the first degree. They did not, therefore, fall within the established principle that the lesser offense must not require some additional element not needed to constitute the greater offense. Defendant also claimed that where the abduction and restraint of a victim were merely incidental to some other underlying offense, such as sexual assault, the abduction and restraint could not form the basis for a verdict of guilty on a charge of kidnapping. The court disagreed and found that the legislature had seen fit not to merge the offense of kidnapping with sexual assault or with any other felony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for kidnapping in the first degree.

Horton v. Meskill


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


172 Conn. 615; 376 A.2d 359; 1977 Conn. LEXIS 938


December 8, 1976, Argued  
April 19, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in each case for a declaratory judgment that the system of financing public elementary and secondary education in the state violates provisions of the state and federal constitutions, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Rubinow, J.; judgments declaring the present system violative of the state constitution, from which the defendant state officials in each case appealed and the plaintiffs cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents filed suit against defendant state officials, claiming that the state system of financing public elementary and secondary education violated provisions of the state and federal constitutions. The superior court declared that the present system of financing public education violated portions of the state and federal constitution. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents claimed that the trial court erred by ruling that the system did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment. The state officials claimed that the trial court erred in its findings concerning the quality of education and the relation between expenditures and the quality of education and the effect of the existing financing system in concluding that only two statutory sections that provide for the financing system were unconstitutional, and that the trial court erred in overruling the state official's claims of law. The court held that the trial court correctly determined that (1) sovereign immunity was not an available defense because a holding to the contrary would have foreclosed proper judicial determination of a significant constitutional question; (2) the state system of financing could not pass the strict judicial scrutiny test as to its constitutionally because pupils in poorer communities received an education that was a substantial degree lower in both breadth and quality; (3) the trial court correctly determined that the statute did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment because there was no reason for the court to reject the validity of that determination.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. McLucas


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


172 Conn. 542; 375 A.2d 1014; 1977 Conn. LEXIS 926


December 10, 1976, Argued  
March 15, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of kidnapping resulting in death, and information charging the defendant with the crimes of conspiracy to commit kidnapping, conspiracy to commit murder, and binding with intent to commit a crime, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the jury before Mulvey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of conspiracy to commit murder and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which entered a conviction for conspiracy to commit murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a member of the Black Panther Party. The State contended that the victim was tortured and killed because he was suspected of being a police informer in the party. It was undisputed that the victim was "disciplined" by torture and then was bound and driven to a swamp. On appeal, defendant argued he had standing to challenge the search of another member's apartment on the basis of his membership on the central staff of the Black Panther Party. The court disagreed and affirmed the conviction, holding that defendant lacked standing because defendant did not live in the apartment, had no proprietary interest in it, and it was only sometimes used for office purposes by the Black Panther group. The court also found that defendant's statement was voluntary because defendant had repeatedly been given his Miranda warnings, had indicated that he understood them but wished to waive his rights, and it was defendant who sought to initiate a bargaining process by indicating that he had information regarding the victim's murder.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Rosnick v. Zoning Com. of Southbury


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


172 Conn. 306; 374 A.2d 245; 1977 Conn. LEXIS 896


November 10, 1976, Argued  
February 1, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an action of the defendant commission in approving adoption of an amendment to zoning regulations, brought to the Court of Common Pleas for the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the court, Spallone, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas for the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which dismissed his appeal from an action of appellee Zoning Commission of the Town of Southbury (Connecticut), which had approved adoption of an interim zoning regulation concerning portions of a business district.


OVERVIEW: The landowner asserted that the regulation was unconstitutional and violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2, which required zoning regulations to be uniform to each class of building or use of land throughout the district. On appeal, the court found, as an initial matter, that the landowner's action should be treated as an appeal from the Commission's decision rather than as an action for a declaratory judgment. The court noted that the landowner had not brought in all the possible interested parties, or given them reasonable notice of the action, as required by Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 309(d). The court held that the landowner's appeal must be dismissed as moot because the zoning regulation at issue had expired. The court noted that it did not sit to advise on abstract principles and that the landowner had not shown that this case presented a situation "capable of repetition," yet evading review. The court explained that there was no evidence that the situation with regard to the interim regulation would ever reoccur as to this landowner.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the landowner's appeal from the judgment of the court of common pleas, which had dismissed his appeal from the Commission's action approving adoption of the interim zoning regulation.

 

670 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rice


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


172 Conn. 94; 374 A.2d 128; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 878


October 7, 1976, Argued  
December 14, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the first degree and unlawfully carrying a weapon in a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the jury before Bracken, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of unlawfully carrying a weapon in a motor vehicle and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which rejected defendant's motion to suppress and convicted defendant of unlawfully carrying a weapon in a motor vehicle in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-38.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot his wife, apparently accidentally. As police arrived at the scene, defendant was attempting to back out of the driveway. The police detained defendant solely to preserve the crime scene, but did not ask him to get out of the car. Later, the police learned that defendant was in the car and, when they directed him out of the car, they found a loaded pistol on his person. Defendant was charged with assault in the first degree and unlawfully carrying a weapon in a motor vehicle, was convicted solely on the later charge, and sentenced. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the detention of defendant was not unlawful under the Fourteenth Amendment or Conn. Const. art. I, § 7 because the minimal initial intrusion was justified by the nature of the serious crime that the police were investigating. The court also held that the presumption under Conn. Gen. Stat. 29-38 did not affect defendant's case because the gun was found on defendant's person, not merely found in the car, which was a fact that could impress itself upon a reasonable jury and ensure that the conviction was not based on speculation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which had denied defendant's motion to suppress and convicted defendant of unlawfully carrying a weapon in a motor vehicle.

Eason v. Welfare Comm'r


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


171 Conn. 630; 370 A.2d 1082; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1211


May 5, 1976, Argued  
September 21, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Juvenile Court for the first district committing custody of a minor child to the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County, and tried to the court, Dean, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff non-biological mother sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which dismissed her appeal of a juvenile court's denial of her motion to "reopen" the commitment of a minor child to the welfare commissioner.


OVERVIEW: The non-biological mother filed a motion to "reopen" commitment in juvenile court. The juvenile court ruled that it had no jurisdiction to hear the non-biological mother's motion because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-62(f) failed to include a foster mother as one who could file a motion to revoke. The trial court denied the non-biological mother's appeal. On review, the court found no error. As the non-biological mother did not fall within one of the categories, the court held that the juvenile court did not have jurisdiction to revoke the commitment under § 17-62(f). Similarly, the court held that the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment did not guarantee her the right to initiate a hearing to revoke the commitment to the welfare commissioner. According to the court, the non-biological mother had an opportunity to be heard at the most critical time in the proceedings before the juvenile court. The court denied the non-biological mother's argument under the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment that denied the non-biological mother's appeal.

State v. Villafane


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which, upon a jury verdict, convicted him of murder in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was a juvenile parole violator, was convicted by a jury of murder in the first degree in connection with the robbery of a bar. In affirming, the court held 1) that it was reasonable for the police to have been requested to detain defendant on the basis of a parole violation where he was known to have been previously involved in a homicide and was considered dangerous; 2) that the on-street identification of defendant by an eye-witness to the crime did not violate due process because the encounter did not focus the witness's attention on defendant and because the identification was spontaneous; 3) that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-1a, which provided for the transfer of juvenile proceedings from the circuit court to the juvenile court, had been repealed by the time the superior court retained jurisdiction over the case; 4) that defendant received fair notice of rebuttal testimony that the State planned to offer in response to defendant's alibi witnesses; and 5) that inconsistencies in the testimony of an alibi witness were properly admitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

State v. Darden


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


171 Conn. 677; 372 A.2d 99; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1213


June 2, 1976, Argued  
September 21, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Tierney, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of robbery in the second degree and sentenced defendant to a term of not less than 5 nor more than 10 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his sentence for robbery in the second degree and asserted that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-35 (c)(2), was an impermissible usurpation of the judicial power by the legislature which required that persons convicted of second degree robbery were to be sentenced to a five-year minimum term, which could not be suspended or reduced. The court stated that the legislature could impose mandatory terms of imprisonment for certain crimes and could preclude probation or suspension of a sentence. The court stated that § 53a-35(c)(2) was a valid exercise of the legislature's police power which clearly encompassed the preservation or order and prevention of crimes and misdemeanors. There was a rational relationship between the protection of public safety and the imposition of nonsuspendable sentence for the violent crime of second degree robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for robbery in the second degree.
