State v. Paluga


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


171 Conn. 586; 370 A.2d 1049; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1206


June 4, 1976, Argued  
September 14, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault with intent to murder, rape, binding with intent to commit a crime, kidnapping and indecent assault, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the jury before Thomas J. O'Sullivan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty as charged and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions from the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) for assault with intent to commit murder, rape, binding with intent to commit a crime, kidnapping, and indecent assault.


OVERVIEW: The charges were based on defendant's actions in impersonating a police officer to stop the victim, after which she was attacked with a belt, sexually assaulted, bound with a rope, and thrown into a pond. Defendant challenged his convictions on five counts. On appeal, the court found no error. The court concluded that: (1) it was constitutionally permissible for the trial court to issue a bench warrant in an ex parte procedure at the request of the State Attorney; (2) the instruction allowing the jury to draw inferences from defendant's refusal to waive his clergy privilege was not erroneous because defendant testified as to his conversations with the priest, which were self-serving protestations of his innocence, and he foreclosed the possibility of impeachment of his self-serving testimony if he, in fact, refused to waive the privilege; (3) the jury was entitled to decide if he had waived the privilege based on his statements during his testimony; (4) the instruction was neutral; and (5) even if the instruction was given in error, it was harmless due to the substantial and convincing evidence of guilt.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

675 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rao


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


171 Conn. 600; 370 A.2d 1310; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1207


June 8, 1976, Argued  
September 14, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of marihuana with intent to sell or dispense, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County where the court, Berdon, J., granted the defendant's motion to quash, from which the state appealed.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which granted defendant's motion to quash an information charging him with possession of marihuana with intent to sell or dispense in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480(b). Defendant claimed that he was denied equal protection because marihuana had been irrationally classified with other, more harmful substances, such as amphetamines and barbiturates.


OVERVIEW: The trial court concluded that the legislative grouping or classification of these substances for penalty purposes violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Conn. Const. art. I. The court found that the trial court misconceived its function in reaching its decision. On the basis of the testimony of defendant's expert witnesses and its own studies, the trial court concluded that marihuana had virtually no harmful effect on the human system. It thus decided to its own satisfaction a debatable medical issue, and with no apparent consideration of the various factors involved in combating the wide-spread drug traffic and problems of drug abuse, it concluded that the general assembly had acted irrationally in adopting such classifications. That Congress acted rationally in adopting the same classification as that attacked by defendant had already been expressly decided. The court therefore found that there was at least a rational basis for the inclusion of marihuana among controlled drugs for penalty purposes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the ruling of the trial court granting defendant's motion to quash the information and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Vaughn


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


171 Conn. 454; 370 A.2d 1002; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1192


May 5, 1976, Argued  
August 24, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of rape in the first degree, deviate sexual intercourse, burglary in the first degree, and larceny in the fourth degree, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to a jury before DeVita, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty on all counts and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which convicted him, upon a jury verdict, of rape, deviate sexual intercourse, burglary, and larceny, contending it was error to exclude the testimony of a psychologist concerning defendant's mental deficiencies and subnormal intelligence as they would affect the weight and credibility that the jury should accord to his confession.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for rape, deviate sexual intercourse, burglary, and larceny, contending that the trial court erred in excluding the testimony of a psychologist concerning defendant's mental deficiencies and subnormal intelligence as they would affect the weight and credibility that the jury should accord to his confession. The victim was unable to identify her assailant and the only evidence linking defendant to the crimes was a confession that he gave to the investigating police and three items, neutral in themselves, found in the home of defendant. The court set aside the verdict and ordered a new trial, finding that the trial court abused its discretion in excluding the testimony of the psychologist. While the preliminary question of the voluntariness of defendant's confession was a matter for the trial court, the credibility and weight to be accorded the confession was an issue for the jury. The court concluded that the jury should have been provided the testimony of the psychologist to assist it in considering the physical and mental condition of defendant as factors in judging the weight and credibility to be accorded the confession.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the verdict that convicted defendant of rape, deviate sexual intercourse, burglary, and larceny and ordered a new trial.

State v. Olds


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

171 Conn. 395; 370 A.2d 969; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1186


May 7, 1976, Argued  
August 10, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree, and assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the jury before Naruk, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of robbery in the second degree, unlawful restraint in the second degree, and assault in the third degree, and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) convicted defendant of robbery in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim identified defendant in court and testified that defendant and a companion entered the victim's apartment, robbed him, and beat him into unconsciousness. Defendant attempted to discredit the victim by alleging that the victim was a gambler. Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in denying his motions for a mistrial, a continuance, dismissal, and dismissal of the jury; in charging the jury; in denying defendant the right to be present at a pre-trial conference; and in denying defendant a trial before 12 jurors. The court found no reversible error and held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion. A witness statement that was allegedly withheld by the State was made available to defendant at trial. Defendant was not entitled to be tried by a 12-person jury or to be present at a conference that addressed matters of law only.

Halabi v. Administrator, Unemployment Compensation Act


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


171 Conn. 316; 370 A.2d 938; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1174


May 5, 1976, Argued  
July 27, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision of an unemployment commissioner finding the plaintiff ineligible for benefits, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the court, John F. Shea, Jr., J.; judgment dismissing the appeal and appeal by the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff unemployment claimant appealed a judgment from Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which dismissed the claimant's appeal of a decision of defendant unemployment commissioner, finding the claimant ineligible for benefits.


OVERVIEW: On November 30, 1970, the claimant was terminated from his position as a research assistant at a university. The university was a nonprofit organization, which first became subject to the Unemployment Compensation Act on January 1, 1971. The claimant filed his benefits claim on January 31, 1971, and for about eight months he received benefits from the unemployment compensation fund. On December 3, 1971, the administrator requested that he refund the amount he had received. The commissioner and the trial court upheld this determination. On review, the court affirmed. The court found that the payment of the benefits was in error, and pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-273(b), the claimant was required to reimburse the administrator. The court also held that the denial of the claimant's eligibility for benefits did not unconstitutionally deprive him of equal protection, noting that, in the area of economics and social welfare, a classification did not violate the Equal Protection Clauses of the U.S. or Connecticut Constitutions unless the classification was clearly unreasonable and that educational associations were often singled out from burdens placed on profit-making organizations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Horak v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged a decision from the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which granted the request of appellees, State and Commissioner of Transportation, to dismiss on jurisdictional grounds the action by the landowner for damages caused by the loss of the use and enjoyment of certain property because of precondemnation delays caused by the State and the Commissioner.


OVERVIEW: The landowner acquired property for the construction of a building to enhance his business. The State and the Commissioner notified him that he should not develop the property because of a planned highway construction project. The property was eventually acquired by the State, and after the acquisition the landowner brought an action that sought money damages for the loss of use and enjoyment of the property from the initial notification until the time of the final taking. The trial court dismissed the action on the request of the State and the Commissioner, who urged sovereign immunity. Figarsky v. Historic Dist. Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


171 Conn. 198; 368 A.2d 163; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1155


April 13, 1976, Argued  
June 15, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision of the defendant commission denying an application by the plaintiffs for a certificate of appropriateness to demolish a building, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New London County and tried to the court, Missal, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs, upon the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in New London County (Connecticut), which dismissed the landowners' appeal from a decision of defendant Historic District Commission of the City of Norwich denying an application by the landowners for a certificate of appropriateness to demolish a building.


OVERVIEW: The landowners applied to the Commission for a certificate of appropriateness to demolish a building. The Commission denied the application. The landowners appealed to the trial court. The trial court dismissed the appeal. The landowners appealed, contending that they were to be forced to undergo economic hardship and loss as a result of not being permitted to demolish their building and that the Commission, in denying their application for a certificate of appropriateness, acted illegally, arbitrarily, and in abuse of its discretion. On appeal, the court held that Norwich, Ct., Ordinances § 14-17 constituted a valid exercise of the state's police power, that the Commission, after a full hearing, lawfully, reasonably and honestly exercised its judgment, and that the trial court was correct in not substituting its own judgment for that of the Commission. The landowners, who had the burden of proving that the Commission acted illegally, arbitrarily, in a confiscatory manner or in abuse of discretion, went no further than to present evidence that their house was unoccupied and in need of extensive repairs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which dismissed the landowners' appeal of the Commission's denial of the landowners' application for a certificate of appropriateness.

 

681 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Menillo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


171 Conn. 141; 368 A.2d 136; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1149


February 5, 1976, Argued  
June 1, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of attempting to procure an abortion, brought to the Superior Court for the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Naruk, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to this court. On the granting of the state's petition for a writ of certiorari, the United States Supreme Court vacated the judgment of this court's finding of error and remanded the case for further consideration.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Supreme Court vacated a judgment finding error in defendant's conviction of the crime of attempting to procure an abortion and remanded the case for further consideration.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempting to procure an abortion, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-29 based on evidence that he, a nonphysician with no medical training, performed an abortion on a female in normal good health for a fee. On appeal, the court held that § 53-29 was unconstitutional and "null and void." The United States Supreme Court remanded the case for the court to further consider the validity of § 53-29. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that, although void as applied to physicians, § 53-29 was constitutional as applied to nonphysicians. by virtue of the power granted the legislature by the state constitution. A federal district court declaration that § 53-29 was invalid was not binding in light of the Supreme Court's determination that enforcement of § 53-29 against nonphysicians was constitutional and in light of Connecticut's role as final arbiter of its own laws. The district court's injunction against enforcement of § 53-29 also did not effect the court's decision on a matter of state law.


OUTCOME: The court determined that there was no error in the conviction and affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

682 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Nicoli v. Planning & Zoning Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


171 Conn. 89; 368 A.2d 24; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1142


December 2, 1975, Argued  
May 18, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiff from the conditional approval by the defendant commission of an application for a subdivision, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Hanrahan, J.; judgment modifying the defendant's decision, from which the defendant, upon the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a zoning commission, appealed an order of the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which found that plaintiff developer was an aggrieved person and entitled to appeal the commission's decision that the developer could not construct residential buildings on his land until a proposed public road within the subdivision was connected to a public street or highway in the town.


OVERVIEW: The developer sought the commission's approval for a subdivision. The commission conditionally approved the subdivision. The trial court found that the developer was entitled to appeal the commission's decision. The commission sought review of the trial court's judgment. The court held that the requirements in the town's regulations provided sufficient authority for the imposition of the condition by the commission. The land in question lay within the easternmost section of the town, in an area where there was no direct access by roads or highways located within the town. The land was accessible only by the roads of a municipality and, thus, the town would have been forced to depend upon the highways of the municipality to provide vital public services to the future residents of the proposed subdivision. Conditioning the approval upon access to the acreage by the town's roads was essential for the protection of the public health, safety and welfare of future residents. The commission's conditional approval constituted a valid exercise of its police power because the condition imposed by the commission protected the health and safety of present and prospective town residents.


OUTCOME: The court found that the trial court's judgment was in error and dismissed the developer's appeal.

 

683 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Wagner v. Connecticut Personnel Appeal Board


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


170 Conn. 668; 368 A.2d 20; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1058


February 5, 1976, Argued  
April 20, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an action of the named defendant in refusing to overturn an action of the plaintiff's superintendent in applying for her involuntary retirement from state classified service, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Collins, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal and ordering the plaintiff reinstated with back pay, from which the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the members of the state personnel appeal board, the commissioner of personnel, and the executive head of the hospital that had employed plaintiff employee, sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which entered a judgment that sustained the employee's appeal and ordered the employee reinstated with back pay. The employee had been retired against her wishes.


OVERVIEW: The employee contended that the involuntary retirement provision of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-162(c)(1) violated the equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions and that her involuntary retirement constituted an arbitrary, capricious, and improper act in light of the fact that the personnel policies of Connecticut were expressly based upon principles of merit. The primary issue presented was whether a state employee could be involuntarily retired pursuant to the provisions of § 5-162(c)(1) for no reasons other than age and length of service. The court found that if a state employee could be selectively retired without cause related to effective performance of his duties under § 5-162(c)(1), it would then appear that the legislature authorized indirectly that which it had forbidden directly through discharge procedures. Moreover, if the statute were construed as allowing arbitrary and selective forced retirement, it would not pass constitutional muster. Because the employee could effectively perform her duties, and she was retired only because of her age and length of service, the relief ordered by the trial court was appropriate. Thus, the judgment was upheld.


OUTCOME: The court found that there was no error.

 

684 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


170 Conn. 618; 368 A.2d 140; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1055


January 7, 1976, Argued  
April 20, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to a three-judge court, Bracken, Longo and Meyers, Js.; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), where he was convicted of murder in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Police investigation led to defendant as a suspect in a slaying. Police obtained a search warrant and searched defendant's apartment, where they seized a specific type of ammunition listed in the search warrant, as well as two shotguns. After being advised of his constitutional rights, defendant made certain oral statements to police. The police confiscated defendant's car, where evidence of the crime was discovered. Defendant was charged with and convicted of the murder. Defendant appealed and, among other things, asserted that that the trial court erred in denying three separate motions to suppress items of evidence. On review, the court found no error in the trial court's denial of the motion to suppress the car-related evidence, as the car was seized with probable cause. The court examined whether an in person line-up was required over a photo array and held that the identification by the photo array instead was not shown to be unconstitutional. Finally, the court found that the trial court erred in not suppressing the evidence of two shotguns that were unrelated to the homicide, but the error was harmless. Thus, the judgment was upheld.


OUTCOME: There was no error.

 

685 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Wiegand v. Heffernan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


170 Conn. 567; 368 A.2d 103; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1050


January 13, 1976, Argued  
April 13, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the disallowance by the defendant tax commissioner of claims for the refund of capital gains and dividends taxes paid by the plaintiffs, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, McCarthy, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of a decision of defendant tax commissioner, who disallowed their claims for refunds of capital gains and dividends taxes paid in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 12-505 to 12-522. The appeal was brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) and reserved by the superior court for the advice of the court.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers were residents of the state part of the tax year, but had moved to another state during the year and become residents of that state. During the year, the taxpayers realized dividends and capital gains, and they reported them on their tax returns. The taxpayers requested a refund of the taxes, and the commissioner disallowed the claims. The taxpayers sought review and asserted that they were not "taxpayers" as defined by the tax laws, which they alleged were vague. They argued that the retroactive application to them of a tax enacted after they had abandoned their Connecticut domicile constituted a denial of due process. On review, the court examined the relevant statutes and the definition of a taxpayer. The court found that the taxpayers were properly classified as "residents" and "taxpayers" under the statutory definitions. The court held that the statutory definition of "resident" was not so badly drafted as to be void for vagueness under the due process clause. Also, the absence of language later added, which specifically mentioned part-year residents, could not be construed as providing part-year residents with a loophole by which they could escape tax liability.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that the commissioner correctly ruled.

 

686 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Audet


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


170 Conn. 337; 365 A.2d 1082; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1028


November 7, 1975, Submitted; December 2, 1975, Argued  
March 16, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion by the state for review of the order of the Superior Court for the judicial district of Waterbury, Wright, J., denying the state's motion for permission to appeal.

Motion by the defendant to dismiss the state's appeal from the Superior Court for the judicial district of Waterbury, Wright, J. 



DISPOSITION: Motion dismissed. Motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to dismiss the State's appeal from a trial court order that denied the State's motion to appeal the dismissal of four criminal counts after defendant was convicted on one count of an information. The State also requested consideration of its' motion for review of the trial court's order that denied it permission to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with and convicted of manslaughter. Because the jury was unable to agree on four counts of assault, the trial court dismissed them. It also denied the State permission to appeal the dismissal of those four counts. The State filed an appeal anyway. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the appeal. The State filed a motion for review of the trial court order that denied permission to appeal. The court granted defendant's motion to dismiss and dismissed the State's motion. It noted that the right to appeal conferred by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-96 was a statutory right. The statutory requirements had to be strictly followed. Because the statutory requisites were not met, the appeal was invalid. Section 54-96 was constitutional because the right to appeal conferred by § 54-96 had not detracted from the essential constitutional characteristics of the trial and appellate courts. Furthermore, the court was powerless to consider any appeal by the State that involved a review the denial of the right to appeal because the legislature had conditioned appeals upon permission from the same court whose action would be reviewed.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion to dismiss the State's appeal, and dismissed the State's motion for review of the denial of its motion for permission to appeal.

Page v. Welfare Comm'r


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


170 Conn. 258; 365 A.2d 1118; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1019


November 18, 1975, Argued  
February 24, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an action of the defendant commissioner in determining the amount to be contributed by the plaintiff, a legally liable relative, for the support of her mother, brought to the Circuit Court in the first circuit and tried to the court, Kulawiz, J., which rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Division of the Court of Common Pleas; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant sought review of an order from the Appellate Division of the Court of Common Pleas (Connecticut), which dismissed her appeal from a decision of defendant welfare commissioner that determined that the claimant was liable for the support of her mother.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner determined that the claimant was liable to her mother for monthly support obligations. In determining the claimant's obligations, the commissioner did not allow any exemptions for the claimant's four children. The claimant sought review first in the circuit court and later in the appellate division. Both appeals were dismissed. On further review, the court set aside the judgment. The court held that the commissioner erred in applying state regulations for calculating the claimant's gross income because the regulations clearly provided more exemptions for married men with minor children than they did for married women with minor children. The court reasoned that in promulgating regulations which permitted a husband more exemptions from his gross monthly income than a wife in similar circumstances, the commissioner acted arbitrarily, in abuse of his discretion, and in such a manner as to impinge upon the constitutional rights of the claimant.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment dismissing the claimant's appeal from the commissioner's determination that she was liable to her mother for monthly support. The court remanded the cause with instructions.

 

688 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Beauton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


170 Conn. 234; 365 A.2d 1105; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1016


December 3, 1975, Argued  
February 17, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of having a deadly or dangerous weapon in a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the jury before Mignone, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of the crime of having a deadly or dangerous weapon in a motor vehicle in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-38.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with having a deadly or dangerous weapon in a motor vehicle after police watched him get into a car and retrieved a loaded pistol from the driver's side. The trial court convicted defendant after the State showed that the local official in the jurisdiction of the arrest had not issued a weapons license pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-28 to defendant to carry the pistol. On appeal, the court set aside the conviction. The court held that the State failed to prove its case beyond a reasonable doubt because the State failed to show that defendant had not been issued a weapons license issued by the proper official of the municipality in which defendant had a bona fide residence or place of business plus.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the decision of the trial court, which had convicted defendant of having a deadly or dangerous weapon in a motor vehicle despite the State's failure to show that a weapons permit had not been issued to defendant in the jurisdiction of his residence or business.

 

689 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Simms


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


170 Conn. 206; 365 A.2d 821; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1011


November 18, 1975, Argued  
February 10, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of the sale of heroin, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Mignone, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which, upon a jury verdict, convicted him of selling heroin in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480(a).


OVERVIEW: A witness introduced an undercover officer to defendant. The officer offered to buy heroin from defendant, who told the officer that the sale would have to be made through the witness. The officer gave the witness the money and he and defendant walked about 20 feet away and exchanged the money for the drugs. Defendant called the witness to testify. The witness asserted his privilege against self-incrimination and refused to testify. The trial court allowed the witness to leave. Defendant was convicted. The court affirmed, finding that the accused's right to compel testimony had to give way to the witness's privilege against self-incrimination. The court held the witness's invocation of the right was proper because the evidence disclosed that the witness actually participated in the drug sale sufficiently to be charged as a principal. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-47a was to be used to secure testimony from a recalcitrant witness for the benefit of the prosecution and it did not require the prosecution to use its authority to grant immunity to the accused's witnesses when necessary to do justice.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of selling heroin was affirmed.

 

690 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Roundhouse Constr. Corp. v. Telesco Masons Supplies Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


170 Conn. 155; 365 A.2d 393; 1976 Conn. LEXIS 1001


December 10, 1975, Argued  
January 27, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the foreclosure of a mechanic's lien, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County, where the defendants Fischer by counterclaim and cross complaint sought damages, invalidation of mechanics' liens filed by the plaintiff and the other defendants, and an injunction to restrain the imposition of those liens, and the issues were tried to the court, Berdon, J.; judgment for the defendants Fischer granting an injunction and invalidating the liens, from which only the plaintiff appealed to this court, which found no error. On petition by the plaintiff to the United States Supreme Court for a writ of certiorari that court vacated the judgment and remanded the case for further consideration.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of no error reaffirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon remand from the United States Supreme Court, which vacated a judgment of the Supreme Court of Connecticut affirming a judgment that invalidated mechanics liens filed by plaintiff in its suit to foreclose its liens against defendant, because the lien statutes violated the due process clauses of state and federal constitutions, the court considered whether its judgment in affirmation was based on state or federal constitutional grounds.


OVERVIEW: In an action by plaintiff to foreclose its mechanics' liens against defendant, the trial court invalidated the liens, ruling that the Connecticut mechanic's lien statutes, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 49-33 through 49-40a, were unconstitutional as violative of the due process clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Conn. Const. art. I, § 20, and enjoined plaintiff from imposing the liens. The court affirmed, but the United States Supreme Court vacated the judgment, and directed the court to consider whether its affirmance was based on federal or state constitutional grounds. In conformity with the direction of the remand, the court ruled that the due process clauses in both constitutions had the same meaning and, based upon that meaning of the due process of law clauses in both the federal and state constitutions, reaffirmed its prior judgment and found no error in the judgment of the trial court, which found the Connecticut statutory procedure governing mechanics' liens to be unconstitutional and which invalidated plaintiff's liens.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed its prior judgment in support of the trial court judgment upon ruling that the due process clauses in both the federal and state constitutions have the same meaning.

State v. Brown


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


169 Conn. 692; 364 A.2d 186; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 865


October 9, 1975, Argued  
December 9, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of the sale of heroin, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the jury before Radin, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which convicted him of three counts of the sale of heroin in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480(a).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of three counts of the sale of heroin in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480(a). On appeal, the court found that the prosecution proved defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court's finding was based on evidence that an undercover police agent met defendant and had a conversation with him concerning narcotics. Defendant told the agent to meet him at a specified corner. At that location defendant gave the agent 15 bags of heroin for $ 45. On another occasion the agent bought heroin from an individual who the agent observed buying the same from defendant. On the final occasion, the agent went to defendant's house and purchased heroin from defendant. The court also found that the trial court had not erred in denying defendant's challenge to the jury array because, contrary to defendant's contention, the court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-217 was not impermissibly vague. Accordingly, defendant's convictions were affirmed on appeal.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

692 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kyles


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


169 Conn. 438; 363 A.2d 97; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 833


May 8, 1975, Argued  
September 2, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of escape from a correctional institution and two counts of assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the jury before David M. Shea, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which, upon a jury verdict, convicted him of escape from a correctional institution and two counts of assault in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was arrested for robbery with violence. While pending trial, he escaped from a correctional center. The state nolle prossed the charge of robbery with violence, however, the defendant was convicted of the escape and two counts of second degree assault. The defendant filed motions to dismiss alleging that his detention was illegal and justified his escape. He challenged the assault and escape statutes as unconstitutional because they did not preserve the defense of illegal confinement. The court affirmed the convictions finding that under Connecticut statutory law, illegal confinement was not a defense to escape or to assault on a correctional officer. The court held that the defendant's proper remedy for any illegal detention was by resort to the courts by means of a writ of habeas corpus. The court held that the defendant's sentence received for escape did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment because it was within the statutory limits and was not disproportionate to the offense. The court held the defendant's due process rights under both the state and federal constitutions were not violated.


OUTCOME: The defendant's conviction of escape and two counts of second degree assault, and his sentences, were affirmed.

 

693 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Gentile v. Altermatt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


169 Conn. 267; 363 A.2d 1; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 822


April 9, 1975, Argued  
August 5, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of an act concerning no-fault automobile insurance, for an injunction, and for other relief, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Missal, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, residents, taxpayers, passenger vehicle owners and persons injured in automobile accident, brought an action against defendant state officials for declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of Connecticut's no-fault automobile insurance act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 38-319 - 38-351, in the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which reserved judgment for the advice of the court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought a declaration that the Connecticut no-fault motor vehicle insurance act (no-fault act) was unconstitutional. Plaintiffs contended that Conn. Const. art. first, § 10, restricted the power of the legislature to abolish a cause of action recognized at common law. The state officials argued that an injury from the negligent operation of an automobile could not have been contemplated as an incorporable common-law right by the framers of the constitution of 1818. The court rejected the argument that the no-fault act eliminated constitutional right of redress, since the no-fault act merely provided reasonable alternative procedure. The court also rejected the argument that equal protection was denied to class of individuals not permitted to bring suit, and that such action denied right to jury trial. Further, the court determined that the portion of the statute requiring mandatory security was a proper exercise of state police power.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the act was constitutional because it provided an adequate alternative remedy to redress for recognized injuries, did not deny equal protection or right to a jury trial, and the portion of the statute requiring mandatory security was a proper exercise of state police power.

 

694 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Warren


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


169 Conn. 207; 363 A.2d 91; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 814


May 9, 1975, Argued  
July 22, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Superior Court in New Haven County, Saden, J., committing the defendant to confinement in a state mental institution following a verdict and judgment of not guilty by reason of insanity of the crime of murder in the first degree.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which ordered his confinement in a state mental institution pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-47 following a verdict and judgment of not guilty by reason of insanity of the crime of murder in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that defendant was mentally ill to the extent that his release would constitute a danger to himself and others and that there was a strong possibility that defendant, if released, might not continue use of his antipsychotic medication. Defendant argued that the trial court's findings were unsupported by the evidence. The court found no error in the judgment. The court concluded that the findings were supported either directly by the evidence or by logical inferences drawn by the trial court. The court rejected defendant's contention that the proof offered by the State did not meet the burden of proof required by § 53a-47. The court also rejected defendant's argument that the preponderance of the evidence test of § 53a-47 violated the due process and equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court concluded that there was no constitutional requirement that the burden of proof necessary for a civil commitment be the same as the burden of proof necessary for the commitment of one who was found not guilty by reason of insanity.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment that ordered defendant's confinement in a state mental institution.

 

695 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. King


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


169 Conn. 140; 363 A.2d 68; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 806


April 1, 1975, Argued  
July 15, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants from continuing the expulsion of the named plaintiff from a public school, and for damages, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Hanrahan, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs and appeal by the defendants.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant board of education sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut) in favor of plaintiffs, the mother and the child, in the child's action for an injunction restraining the board of education from continuing the expulsion of the child from a public school pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-234 and for damages incurred by the mother who paid tuition for her the child to attend a private school.


OVERVIEW: The child was permanently expelled from high school as a result of his alleged participation in a gang assault. During the period of his expulsion, the mother paid private school tuition. The mother and child commenced an action against the board of education and the trial court found in their favor. The board of education appealed. The court modified the judgment in part. The court held that the trial court was not in error in concluding that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-234 was invalid as an illegal delegation of legislative power. The court found that § 10-234 was vague because the phrase "inimical to the best interests" varied so much in meaning that a person of common intelligence could not necessarily guess at its meaning. However, the court ruled that it was an error to award the mother damages for paying private school tuition because while functioning under § 10-234 the board of education was acting in a quasi-judicial capacity and therefore was entitled to the defense of governmental immunity. Therefore, the judgment as to the mother was set aside and the case was remanded with directions to render judgment for the board of education on the issue of damages.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the trial court by holding that the trial court erred in awarding the mother damages. The court set aside the judgment as to the mother and remanded the case with direction to render judgment for the board of education on the issue of damages.

 

696 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Kuser v. Orkis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


169 Conn. 66; 362 A.2d 943; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 796


April 9, 1975, Argued  
July 1, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Bastardy action concerning two children, brought to the Circuit Court in the second circuit where the issues were tried to the court, Sicilian, J.; judgment for the plaintiff on the paternity of one child only and appeal by the defendant to the Appellate Division of the Court of Common Pleas, which rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an alleged putative father, sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Division of the Court of Common Pleas (Connecticut), which affirmed the superior court's entry of judgment for plaintiff mother in her bastardy action, which was commenced pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-435.


OVERVIEW: In the mother's bastardy proceeding, her attorney, as a commissioner of the superior court, issued a warrant for defendant's arrest. Defendant was arrested and later released upon his posting of a bond. On the same day as the arrest, defendant was served with a copy of the complaint; in response, he later entered a general appearance in the proceeding. Defendant made several subsequent appearances in the proceeding. On appeal from the superior court's finding that defendant was the father of the mother's oldest child, the appellate court found that the procedure leading to defendant's arrest was unconstitutional because the determination of probable cause to issue the arrest warrant was not made by a neutral and detached magistrate; however, the appellate court concluded that, under the circumstances, the trial court's judgment was not invalid. Upon review, the court held that personal jurisdiction was obtained over defendant when he was served with the complaint and when he later appeared in the proceeding. Thus, assuming, arguendo, that the arrest procedure permitted Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-435 was unconstitutional, personal jurisdiction was still properly obtained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

697 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Owens-Corning Fiberglass Corp. v. Lewis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


169 Conn. 76; 362 A.2d 968; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 797


May 7, 1975, Argued  
July 1, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mechanic's lien, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Daly, J.; judgment for the plaintiff awarding damages and appeal by the defendant.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut) in favor of plaintiff materialman with respect to his action to foreclose a mechanic's lien.


OVERVIEW: The materialman furnished supplies and materials to a subcontractor engaged in the construction of buildings and improvements on the owner's property. The materialman brought an action against the owner to foreclose a mechanic's lien filed to secure payment of the unpaid balance owed for the supplies and materials. The owner contended that the Connecticut mechanic's lien statutes, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 49-33 to 49-40a, were unconstitutional in that they violated the Due Process Clauses of the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution and the corresponding provisions of the Connecticut Constitution. The trial court rendered judgment in favor of the materialman. On appeal, the court set aside the trial court's judgment. The court determined that the merits of the appeal were determined by its decision in a prior case. The court determined the fact that the materialman was required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-35 to give the property owner written notice that it was furnishing materials and intended to make a claim was not sufficient to cure the constitutional deficiencies in the mechanic's lien statutes that the court noted in the prior case.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings in accordance with the court's opinion.

 

698 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pastet


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


169 Conn. 13; 363 A.2d 41; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 791


April 4, 1975, Argued  
June 24, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application for modification of sentence and motion to open judgment for purpose of resentencing the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the court, Saden, J.; judgment vacating the sentence of death and imposing a sentence of life imprisonment, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), defendant filed an application for modification of his death sentence and filed a motion to open the judgment for the purpose of resentencing him. The trial court vacated the sentence of death and imposed a sentence of life imprisonment, from which defendant appealed to the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, and sentenced to death. The United States Supreme Court decided Furman v. Georgia. The Court's opinion invalidated the imposition of death sentences for certain Connecticut cases. Defendant's case was not one of those cases; however, he filed a motion to reopen the judgment in his case. A psychiatric examination was ordered to inquire into his mental status prior to resentencing proceedings. He was diagnosed with a personality disorder, but he was not legally insane. Defendant was then sentenced to life imprisonment. The court found no error in the trial court's resentencing. Defendant claimed that the court lacked the authority to sentence him to life imprisonment. The court found that it would have been futile for the trial court to convene a jury for the purpose of "recommending" the only punishment which the trial court remained authorized under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-10 to impose on defendant after Furman upon a conviction of first degree murder. The court also found that it was not error for the trial court to find that defendant was "judicially sane" when he was resentenced.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's resentencing of defendant to life imprisonment. Defendant was able to understand the nature of the sentencing proceedings, why he was being punished, and the nature of his punishment. The trial court was not bound by an earlier declaration that defendant was "insane" for purposes of exemption from execution of the prior death sentence.

 

699 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rose


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


168 Conn. 623; 362 A.2d 813; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 994


February 4, 1975, Argued

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in two parts charging the defendant with (1) violation of the state narcotic drug act and (2) being an habitual offender, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County where the issues under the first part were tried to the jury before Tedesco, J.; verdict of guilty; the defendant pleaded guilty under the second part, and the court rendered judgment of guilty under both parts, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of having heroin under his control in violation of 1967 Conn. Acts 555, and of being a habitual offender, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-121, based on his plea of guilty to the habitual offender status.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the superior court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence, in certain rulings on the admissibility of evidence, in denying his motion for a mistrial, and in imposing his sentence and denying his motion to dismiss the habitual offender charge. The court found that there was sufficient probable cause for the warrant based on information from two informants. The court also found that the affidavit supporting the warrant sufficiently corroborated the informants' statements and connected the asserted illegal activity with the apartment. The court found that the absence of an indication by the superior court that it examined the warrant was not conclusive evidence that the warrant was not examined. The court concluded that the superior court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion for a mistrial because the court properly instructed the jury regarding irrelevant and mistakenly admitted testimony and properly sustained objections to the cross-examination of officers regarding defendant's wife's addictive use of the narcotics found. Finally, the court concluded that defendant's sentence was within the statutory limits.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

State v. Clemons


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


168 Conn. 395; 363 A.2d 33; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 967


February 5, 1975, Argued  
April 29, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of assault with intent to kill, carrying a pistol without a permit, resisting arrest, and possession of heroin with intent to sell, and, in the second part, with being a third offender, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County, where the issues under the first part were tried to the jury before Levine, J.; the jury found the defendant guilty of possession of heroin with intent to sell, and the issues under the second part were then tried to the court, which found the defendant guilty; from the judgment, the defendant appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which convicted him following a jury trial of possession of heroin with intent to sell in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480(a). Defendant was also convicted as a third offender pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-121.


OVERVIEW: Defendant threw down bundles of heroin and pointed a revolver at four officers who approached him in a restaurant to arrest him on a bench warrant. The jury found defendant guilty of possession of heroin with intent to sell. The court held that no error occurred. First, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to hold an evidentiary hearing on defendant's conclusory allegations that the affidavit in support of the bench warrant contained false allegations. Second, the court held that § 19-480(a) was not unconstitutionally vague. Third, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's request for an expert witness funded by the state to provide an independent toxicological examination. Defendant failed to show that such expert testimony was material and necessary to provide an adequate defense since he admitting to possessing some heroin and never contested that heroin was found in the remaining packets. Finally, the armed possessor of a quantity of narcotics far greater than the amount a drug user would usually have in his possession for his own use could be found to possess those narcotics with the intent to sell.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the trial court's judgment.

Brecciaroli v. Connecticut Comm'r of Environmental Protection


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


168 Conn. 349; 362 A.2d 948; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 959; 5 ELR 20319


January 14, 1975, Argued  
April 15, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the defendant's denial of the plaintiff's application for a permit to conduct a regulated activity on land owned by the plaintiff and designated as tidal wetland, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Collins, J.; judgment for the defendant; the plaintiff filed a motion to open and modify the judgment which was denied, and from this action and from the judgment the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant challenged the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which denied the applicant's challenge to a decision of respondent Commissioner of Environmental Protection, refusing to open and modify that judgment, denying his application for a non-conforming use of his land.


OVERVIEW: The applicant owned property that the Commissioner found fell within the bounds of wetlands. The applicant sought to fill his property, which required a non-conforming use of the land be permitted. The applicant argued that the denial of his application to fill his property constituted a taking without compensation. The court found that the denial only constituted denial of one specified use of the property and that that use was not reasonable when balanced against the public harm that would result from the covering of the wetlands. The applicant could be permitted to fill a smaller portion of the wetland and he could apply for that use. Until the applicant had applied for another use, the denial of the application to fill the wetlands was not an unconstitutional taking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying the applicant's motion for modification of a judgment.

Lublin v. Brown


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


168 Conn. 212; 362 A.2d 769; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 941


January 7, 1975, Argued  
March 25, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of an occupational tax on attorneys and for a refund of all monies collected for that tax, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County, and reserved by the court, Cohen, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorney filed an action against defendant, the Tax Commissioner of the State of Connecticut, challenging the constitutionality of an occupational tax on attorneys. The action was reserved by the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) for the advice of the court.


OVERVIEW: The attorney sought a declaratory judgment that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-81b was unconstitutional, null, void, and unenforceable. He also sought a refund of all money collected by the Commissioner pursuant to the statute. The court found that the tax was not oppressive or unconstitutionally discriminatory in that it treated attorneys as a class in a manner substantially similar to the treatment accorded other professions. Attorneys were no more exempt from taxation than other professions and occupations and had no cause to complain so long as the tax contribution required from them was reasonable and not the result of hostile and oppressive discrimination. The attorney failed to sustain the burden of proving that, as to him and other persons similarly situated, the provisions of § 51-81b violated the equal protection provisions of the Connecticut Constitution or the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court awarded judgment to the Commissioner, holding that the occupational tax was constitutional.

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the administrator of estate of decedent, sought review of an order of the Superior Court in Fairfield County at Stamford (Connecticut), which denied his application for the admission of an out-of-state attorney as trial counsel pro hac vice the estate's medical malpractice action.

OUTCOME: The court found no error and affirmed the order of the trial court and denied the administrator's application for the admission of an out-of-state attorney as trial counsel pro hac vice the estate's medical malpractice action.

Grover v. Manchester


Nos. 7591, 7606


Supreme Court of Connecticut


168 Conn. 84; 357 A.2d 922; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 927


December 10, 1974, Argued  
March 4, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals by the named defendant from an award of the workmen's compensation commissioner for the first district, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County, Collins, J., and to the Superior Court in Hartford County, Driscoll, J., and reserved by both courts for the advice of this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a hearing denying plaintiff police officer's widow workmen's compensation benefits after her husband died of a coronary occlusion, the workmen's compensation commissioner declined to answer questions raised by defendant town about the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c. The questions were reserved to the court from the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut) and the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: At the time of the police officer's death, he was employed as a member of the police department of the town. When first employed, he successfully passed a physical examination, which revealed no evidence of hypertension or heart disease. The questions reserved to the court were whether Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c, which provided for the town's payment of benefits to police officers and firemen who died of heart disease that was not detected at a physical examination prior to employment, even if the disease was not employment-related, deprived the town of property without due process of law in violation of the Due Process Clauses of the United States and Connecticut Constitutions; and whether the class preference created by § 7-433c contravened Conn. Const. art. 1, § 1. The court concluded that § 7-433c served a proper public purpose and that the fact that it incidentally conferred a direct benefit upon a certain class of individuals did not render it in violation of Conn. Const. art. 1, § 1. The questions submitted by reservation from the court of common pleas were answered in the negative. The court dismissed the reservation from the superior court for lack of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: In regard to the reservation from the court of common pleas, the court ruled that the statute was constitutional. The court dismissed the reservation from the superior court for lack of jurisdiction.

Morris v. Timenterial, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


168 Conn. 41; 357 A.2d 507; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 919


November 7, 1974, Argued  
February 25, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion by the defendants for discharge of attachments, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and granted by the court, Mulvey, J., and appeal by the plaintiffs to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attaching parties sought review of an order of the Superior Court, New Haven County (Connecticut), which granted defendant real property owner's motion to discharge attachments made pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-281.


OVERVIEW: The lower court ordered the attachments to be released because the attaching parties did not secure their prejudgment remedies as provided by 1973 Conn. Acts 431 § 7. The attaching parties did not make a motion for a hearing and a finding of probable cause to sustain the validity of the claims. The lower court dissolved the attachments based upon its interpretation of § 7 as requiring the dissolution of attachments made prior to it and not validated in accordance with it. The court held that the lower court's interpretation of § 7 was in error. The dissolution of attachments was strictly limited to causes provided for by statute. 1973 Conn. Acts 431 made no reference to the dissolution of an attachment. Consequently, 1973 Conn. Acts 431 § 7 was to be read to permit the validation of an attachment whose constitutional validity was in doubt. An unconstitutional attachment was not dissolved perforce of the Public Act, but failed to be effectual if it was determined that it was not constitutional and not validated.


OUTCOME: The court found error in the judgment of the lower court in discharging attachments.

Shaskan v. Waltham Industries Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


168 Conn. 43; 357 A.2d 472; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 920


November 13, 1974, Argued  
February 25, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mortgage, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County at Stamford and tried to the court and judgment of foreclosure by sale, Tierney, J.; stipulation for determination of priorities, and reserved by the court, Tunick, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff first mortgage holder filed a foreclosure action against defendants, several judgment creditors and a bank. After a judgment of foreclosure was entered in the Superior Court in Fairfield County at Stamford (Connecticut), the proceeds of the sale were held for distribution. The case was referred for appellate review for a determination of the priorities of the judgment creditors and the bank.


OVERVIEW: The judgment creditors placed attachments on a debtor's property, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-279. However, the attachments were made without regard to the debtor's due process rights. Judgment liens were subsequently recorded against the property. A bank took a second mortgage on the property to secure a pre-existing debt before the judgments were entered. After the property had been foreclosed upon, a dispute arose as to whether the judgment liens related back to the date of the filing of the attachments. The bank contended that it was entitled to priority because the liens did not relate back. The bank alleged that the attachments were unconstitutional because the debtor's due process rights were violated. The court determined that the bank had no standing to challenge the alleged violation of the debtor's constitutional rights. In general, a person was only permitted to assert his own constitutional rights or immunities. One that was not injured by the operation of a law was not deprived by it of his constitutionally protected rights. The bank did not meet its burden of showing facts essential to its standing.


OUTCOME: Because the court concluded that the bank had no standing to challenge the distribution of the proceeds, the question reserved was not answered.

State v. Townsend


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


167 Conn. 539; 356 A.2d 125; 1975 Conn. LEXIS 1104


October 10, 1974, Argued  
February 4, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information, in two counts, charging the defendant with the crime of assault with intent to murder, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Tierney, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of aggravated assault, from which judgment the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted him of two counts of aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for questioning by police officers who were gathering information on militant groups. Defendant then pulled a gun and fired shots at the officers. Defendant escaped and was not arrested until later when he surrendered to police. Defendant challenged his assault conviction, and the court found no error in the judgment. Further, defendant was not arbitrarily deprived of his right to a hearing as to probable cause in violation of equal protection or due process guarantees, and the affidavits supporting the bench warrant for his arrest were sufficient. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in excluding statements offered to prove the officers' reputation for violence, and the search of defendant's vehicle was proper.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment.

Whitfield v. Empire Mut. Ins. Co.

OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought recovery for damages in a car substituted for one being repaired. Textron, Inc. v. Wood


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


167 Conn. 334; 355 A.2d 307; 1974 Conn. LEXIS 757


October 2, 1974, Argued  
December 3, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining certain questions concerning the taking of property for highway purposes, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and referred to Hon. Howard W. Alcorn, state referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment answering a question in favor of the plaintiff; 1 the defendant filed a motion to open the judgment which was denied, and from this action and from the judgment the defendant appealed.


1 In view of the answer to the first question, an answer to the second became unnecessary.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Commissioner of Transportation sought review of the decision from the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which granted a declaratory judgment to plaintiff property owner determining that his land had been effectively taken by the Commissioner and the date of such taking.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner notified the property owner of the necessity to acquire the property by ordering the property owner to be out of its plant by 1967, by filing a map which had the statutory effect of depicting the property as part of a legally laid out state highway, and by publishing its intent to advertise for bids. Yet no statutory procedure to take the property was undertaken until 1973, when the Commissioner finally filed the certificate of taking pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-73(b). However, in 1967, the property owner moved its operations out of the plant in response to the Commissioner's notification. The property owner filed a motion for a declaratory judgment after the Commissioner filed the certificate of taking in 1973. The Commissioner asserted the principle of sovereign immunity against the action, but the court held that the principle had no application because the property owner merely sought a declaration of legal rights. The court concluded that the property was taken in the constitutional sense in 1967 because the Commissioner's stated intent that year to take the property constituted a substantial interference with the property owner's rights.
