State v. Smith


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


167 Conn. 328; 355 A.2d 257; 1974 Conn. LEXIS 756


October 9, 1974, Argued  
November 26, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of heroin and marihuana and possession of heroin with intent to sell, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before O'Sullivan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him of possession of heroin and marihuana, and possession of heroin with intent to sell when, at the time of his arrest he was not a drug dependent person.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with, inter alia, possession of heroin with intent to sell by a person who was not a drugdependent person at the time of his arrest. On direct examination, defendant testified that he snorted six or seven bags of heroin a day in order to avoid becoming an addict. On cross-examination he testified that he was not dependent on heroin at the time of his arrest, and evidence was introduced that he did not have tracks or scars from injecting heroin, or the deterioration in his nose that was typical of people who snorted heroin. Defendant claimed that there was insufficient evidence to support the jury verdict convicting him of, inter alia, possession with intent to sell when at the time of his arrest he was not a drug dependent person. The court held that the jury could have concluded that the State proved beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was not a drugdependent person at the time of his arrest. The court also rejected defendant's claim that the statute was unconstitutional because it did not exculpate persons who were drugdependent at the time of the crime. Intent to sell was an element of the crime, and the statute it did not punish mere drugdependence.


OUTCOME: There was no error.

 

713 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Hillier v. East Hartford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


167 Conn. 100; 355 A.2d 1; 1974 Conn. LEXIS 730


June 7, 1974, Argued  
August 13, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries alleged to have been caused by a defective highway, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the jury before Wright, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiff and appeal by the defendant.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which found in favor of plaintiff injury victim in her negligence action to recover damages for the injuries that she received from a defective highway.


OVERVIEW: The victim received injuries when she fell on an icy sidewalk. The victim failed to provide notice to the city for more than one year after the fall occurred. The court reversed the superior court's judgment because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-149 provided that no action for any injury that was received because of a defective road could have been maintained against the city unless written notice was provided within 30 days of the incident. 1971 Conn. Spec. Acts 169 specifically validated the victim's notice and granted her permission to institute and prosecute an action against the city. The giving of timely notice was a condition precedent to the existence of a cause of action against the city and in the absence of notice, the recovery against the city was barred. Section 169 would only have been valid if it affected the remedy rather than the grounds of the action; no right of the opposing party was affected; or the state recognized an honorary obligation so that substantial justice could have been realized. Section 169 violated Conn. Const. art. 1, § 1, which provided that no one was entitled to exclusive public emolument or privileges from the community.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the superior court's judgment and remanded the case to the superior court to render a judgment in favor of the city.

 

714 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. Connecticut Product Development Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


167 Conn. 111; 355 A.2d 72; 1974 Conn. LEXIS 731


June 11, 1974, Argued  
August 13, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of an act establishing the Connecticut Product Development Corporation, for an injunction and other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Naruk, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens sought a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 32-32 through 32-46.


OVERVIEW: The statute at issue established a quasi-public instrumentality designating the development corporation to implement its provisions. The statute's purpose was to encourage new products in Connecticut. The citizens claimed that statute unconstitutionally authorized the use of public funds for a private benefit and not for a public purpose in violation of Conn. Const. art. 1. The court noted that the legislature had wide discretion in drafting legislation. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional. The court reasoned that the citizens only disputed the business judgment of the legislature and that was not enough overcome the strong validity of the legislation. The court stated that the citizens failed to sustain their burden of overcoming the presumption in favor of the statute's constitutionality by showing beyond a reasonable doubt that it entitled successful applicants to exclusive public emoluments without any purpose to serve the public welfare. The court concluded that the statute also contained adequate standards to guide the development corporation in the exercise of its discretion in determining which applicants should receive public assistance.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the validity of the statute.

 

715 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Szarwak v. Warden, Connecticut Correctional Institution


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


167 Conn. 10; 355 A.2d 49; 1974 Conn. LEXIS 724


June 7, 1974, Argued  
July 23, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus, alleging unlawful imprisonment, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Parskey, J.; judgment for the plaintiff and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant correctional institution sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which found in favor of plaintiff in plaintiff's habeas corpus proceeding challenging the imposition of his sentence on the grounds that the prosecution violated its plea agreement and that the sentence imposed by the circuit court constitutionally exceeded the circuit court's jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: As the result of a plea agreement, plaintiff pled guilty to the reduced charges against him. When plaintiff learned that he was going to receive a sentence exceeding that recommended by the prosecutor, he moved to withdraw the plea. The prosecutor opposed the motion and the circuit court denied it. In plaintiff's subsequent petition for habeas corpus, the superior court found that because plaintiff sought to withdraw the guilty plea and did receive a sentence exceeding the prosecutor's recommendation, the prosecution had breached its agreement by objecting to the motion. In reversing this determination, the court held that there could be no breach of the agreement where there was no motion to withdraw the plea after the sentence was imposed since a sentence in excess of that recommended was a condition precedent. Moreover, the court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-1a, which gave jurisdiction to the circuit court over crimes punishable by a fine of not more than $ 5000 or imprisonment for more than five years, was unconstitutional since it materially detracted from the essential characteristics of the superior court as created by Conn. Const. art. 5, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment with respect to the plea agreement, but affirmed with respect to the unconstitutionality of the circuit court's recommended sentence. The court remanded the case to the superior court with direction that the inmate be discharged from custody unless the circuit court vacated the sentence and imposed a constitutionally permissible sentence.

 

716 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Marshall


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


166 Conn. 593; 353 A.2d 756; 1974 Conn. LEXIS 932


February 6, 1974, Argued  
July 9, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County at Waterbury and tried to the jury before Armentano, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the crime charged, and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for first-degree murder from the Superior Court in New Haven County at Waterbury (Connecticut), alleging multiple errors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim were prospective members of a motorcycle gang. Defendant told a third party that he would like to kill the victim because he refused to contribute money to aid in the defense of gang members charged in pending rape cases. The third party provided defendant with a pistol and cartridges. Pursuant to a search warrant, police searched defendant's home, finding the murder weapon and cartridges. Defendant's first assignment of error was based upon the cumulative effect of the denial of two motions, a motion to exclude from the courtroom the single newspaper reporter present and a motion to examine the jury to inquire whether any juror had read an article in a local newspaper, an article defendant claimed was prejudicial. The court found no trial court error in both motions' denial. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to poll the jurors regarding the newspaper article. Also, the trial court had properly and adequately charged the jury when they were impaneled, and during the course of the trial, not to read, listen to, or watch media coverage of the trial. Also, there was no absolute right to exclude the newspaper reporter from the trial.


OUTCOME: The court, finding no trial court error in defendant's conviction for first-degree murder, affirmed. The court found evidence regarding defendant's motive relevant and correctly admitted against him.

 

717 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Naylor v. Brown


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


166 Conn. 581; 353 A.2d 709; 1974 Conn. LEXIS 930


May 7, 1974, Argued  
July 2, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decree of the Probate Court for the district of Madison taxing a power of appointment over a marital deduction trust, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and reserved by the court, Hull, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) submitted four questions on appeal for the advice of the court. Plaintiff executor had brought the cause of action against defendant tax commissioner after the tax commissioner asserted that the decedent's exercise in part and nonexercise in part of the general power of appointment was a taxable transfer under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-345a.


OVERVIEW: The decedent, prior to her death, had partially exercised her power of appointment in a martial deduction trust. The executor reported as nontaxable the power of appointment granted the decedent by her husband. The defendant tax commissioner claimed that the decedent's exercise in part and nonexercise in part of the general power of appointment was a taxable transfer. The lower court agreed with the contention of the tax commissioner and held that both the exercise and non-exercise by the decedent of the power of appointment constituted at her death a taxable transfer under § 12-345a. The court found that § 12-345a permitted taxation in the decedent's estate of the transfer of the marital deduction trust created under the will of her husband because the statute was clear and the imposition of a tax was a legislative function that the court had no choice but to follow. The court held that the statute clearly and plainly applied to the transfer and that the thing burdened was the right to receive. The court further held the statute constitutional as the legislature had deemed that the exercise or omission to exercise a power of appointment was taxable.


OUTCOME: The court found affirmatively that the lower court did not err in finding that the exercise in part and nonexercise in part of the executor's decedent of the general power of appointment under a marital deduction trust was a taxable transfer as contended by the tax commissioner.

State v. Clemente


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


166 Conn. 501; 353 A.2d 723; 1974 Conn. LEXIS 926


December 11, 1973, Argued  
July 2, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in three counts charging the defendant with the crimes of indecent assault and conspiracy to commit the crimes of rape, indecent assault, sodomy, robbery with violence and aggravated assault, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the court, Shapiro, J.; judgment of guilty on all counts and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a jury verdict of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) for indecent assault, conspiracy to commit rape, indecent assault, sodomy, robbery with violence, and aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction by a jury for indecent assault, conspiracy to commit rape, indecent assault, sodomy, robbery with violence, and aggravated assault. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in refusing to order production of complaining witness statements pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-86b, which required the prosecution to produce such statements. The court affirmed the trial court's decision that § 54-86b violated the Connecticut Constitution. The court held that if § 54-86b was given effect, it would infringe upon the superior court in its exercise of discretion and in controlling discovery which is within the court's inherent power and, thus, there would be an encroachment on both the operational and the structural levels of the court. The defendant also claimed that out-of-court photographic identification was impermissibly suggestive and constitutionally unfair. The court held that the photographic identification procedure was not so impermissibly suggestive as to give rise to a very substantial likelihood of irreparable misidentification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction by the jury.

Connecticut Steel Co. v. National Amusements, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


166 Conn. 255; 348 A.2d 658; 1974 Conn. LEXIS 890


February 7, 1974, Argued  
March 26, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mechanic's lien, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and referred to Hon. Patrick B. O'Sullivan, state referee, who, exercising the powers of that court, rendered judgment of foreclosure of the lien; the judgment was opened on motion of the named defendant and the case erased from the docket, and the plaintiff appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff steel company appealed a decision by the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which reopened a judgment on the motion of defendant landowner and erased the steel company's judgment of foreclosure of a mechanic's lien from the docket.


OVERVIEW: The steel company brought an action to foreclose a mechanic's lien against property of the landowner based upon services and material the steel company had provided in erecting structural steel, steel joists, and a steel deck on the property. A state referee, exercising the powers of the superior court, rendered judgment for the steel company. While its appeal was pending, the landowner filed with the trial court a motion to reopen judgment and to erase for want of jurisdiction, claiming that the steel company did not obtain final judgment within two years from the date the action was commenced as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-39. The trial court opened the judgment and erased the case from the docket. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err in its application of the time limitations of § 49-39 because the limitation on the time for obtaining final judgment was the same as the limitation on the time for commencing the action. The court determined that § 49-39 did not require any action on the part of the landowner before the lien became ineffective and that § 49-39 was jurisdiction because it was a limitation on the right to a remedy.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's decision to erase the judgment of foreclosure of the mechanic's lien.

State v. Sober

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in a four-count information with (1) breaking and entering with criminal intent in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Acts 452, and (3) two counts of assaulting a police officer in violation of § 2 of the same public act. New Haven v. Public Utilities Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


165 Conn. 687; 345 A.2d 563; 1974 Conn. LEXIS 1063


October 11, 1973, Argued  
January 15, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant commission authorizing the construction of transmission line facilities, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County; motion for modification of supersedeas by defendants The United Illuminating Company and The Connecticut Light and Power Company granted, McGuinness, J.; the case was tried to the court, Hanrahan, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal and appeal by the named plaintiff et al.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, city, associations, groups, and citizens, appealed an order of defendant Public Utilities Commission (PUC), permitting defendant power companies to construct overhead electrical transmission lines. The appeal acted as a supersedeas of the order. The Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County (Connecticut) granted the power companies' motion for modification of the supersedeas. The plaintiffs appealed a judgment dismissing their appeal.


OVERVIEW: The plaintiffs made the claim that modification of the supersedeas was to avoid the applicability of the Public Utility Environmental Standards Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 16-50g -- 16-50w. On appeal, the court found that contrary to that claim, the language of the Act indicated that it did not affect construction commenced prior to April 1, 1972, and thus was not applicable to the power lines' construction. The court also found that only the city was an aggrieved party for the purpose of taking the appeal and that the remaining plaintiffs were not aggrieved parties. Aggrievement under state law required a specific, personal, and legal interest in the subject matter of the decision as distinguished from a general interest. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-35, aggrievement is a prerequisite to a right of appeal; thus, the plaintiffs other than the city lacked standing to appeal. The court also found that the PUC's decision was not illegal, arbitrary, unreasonable, or an abuse of its discretion. The city sought the installation of underground transmission lines but the PUC found that they were considerably more expensive and less reliable.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment of the lower court.

State v. Watson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


165 Conn. 577; 345 A.2d 532; 1973 Conn. LEXIS 775


October 4, 1973, Argued  
December 19, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Separate informations charging each defendant with the crimes of robbery with violence, binding with criminal intent and having a weapon in a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the jury before Barber, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty and appeals by the defendants.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; new trial limited to the third count in each information.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Four defendants sought consolidated review of a judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which convicted each of them of robbery with violence in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-14; binding with intent to rob in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-19; and possession of an unlicensed weapon in a motor vehicle in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-38. Defendants were separately charged in three-count informations.


OVERVIEW: In a preliminary hearing, the court ruled against defendants' motion to suppress. Defendants raised various arguments on appeal, including that the police lacked the legal authority to stop the vehicle, to order them to exit the vehicle, to remove items from the vehicle or to detain them; and therefore, they claimed it was error to admit the items removed from the vehicle, including a pistol, into evidence. The court affirmed defendants' convictions as to two of the counts in the information. However, the court reversed their convictions on the third count of possession of an unlicensed weapon in a motor vehicle. A jury charge specifically referenced that part of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-38 that defined the presence of a weapon in a vehicle as prima facie evidence of the crime. That charge required the convictions to be reversed. The court found that the prima facie provision of § 29-38 had the inevitable effect of placing on the alleged violator the burden of proving his innocence, and therefore, was an unconstitutional denial of due process. However, the court determined that the remainder of the statute was severable and valid.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions of robbery with violence and binding with intent to rob were affirmed. Defendants' convictions of possessing an unlicensed weapon in a motor vehicle under the third count of the informations were reversed.

The court found that the only procedural avenue mentioned for bringing claims was the Workmen's' Compensation Act.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

Langs v. Harder


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


165 Conn. 490; 338 A.2d 458; 1973 Conn. LEXIS 763; 80 A.L.R.3d 759


October 5, 1973, Argued  
December 4, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision of the defendant finding Everett C. Langs, a minor, ineligible for welfare assistance, brought to the Circuit Court for the fourteenth circuit and tried to the court, Belinkie, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal and appeal by the plaintiff to the Appellate Division of the Court of Common Pleas, which reversed the judgment and thence, on the granting of certification, the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Commissioner of Welfare appealed from the judgment of the Appellate Division of the Court of Common Pleas (Connecticut) that reversed the decision finding plaintiff minor ineligible for welfare assistance. The minor had received payments under the Aid to Dependent Children (ADC) program.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner discontinued ADC payments made to the recipient on behalf of the minor after the minor received a settlement in a personal injury case. The settlement funds were held in a savings account under the supervision of the Probate Court. The Commissioner's decision was upheld by the hearing officer and the circuit court but was reversed by the appellate division. On review, the court overturned the appellate division's opinion, finding that the Commissioner did not abuse his discretion or act arbitrarily and unreasonably when he suspended payments on behalf of the minor. Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 17-90, 17-94 provided that the Commissioner was permitted to grant aid only to eligible applicants and to suspend or discontinue aid when necessary to comply with the sections. The court held that the settlement award constituted a resource, as the term was defined in implementing regulations, for purposes of determining eligibility for ADC payments. The court further found that the award was sufficiently available for the Commissioner to take it into account. The court also rejected the claim that the provisions violated the Due Process, Equal Protection and Supremacy Clauses.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment, remanded the matter, and directed the appeals court to render judgment dismissing the minor's appeal.

 

727 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Stern v. Stern


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


165 Conn. 190; 332 A.2d 78; 1973 Conn. LEXIS 726


May 1, 1973, Argued  
June 29, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the defendant from an order of the Superior Court in New Haven County, Levine, J., granting the plaintiff alimony pendente lite.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant husband appealed an order of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which awarded temporary alimony to plaintiff wife, asserting that the alimony pendente lite award under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46-21 was unconstitutional because it discriminated against him on the basis of his sex.


OVERVIEW: The husband asserted that § 46-21 violated the Fourteenth Amendment because it provided for alimony for wives but not husbands. The wife asserted that the husband lacked standing to make a challenge to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46-21 because he had not sought alimony pendente lite and had not established that he would have been entitled to support. The court held that the husband had standing because there was sufficient nexus between his equal protection rights and the financial burden imposed by the award made under § 46-21. The court agreed that females similarly situated to the husband could not be compelled to pay temporary alimony under § 46-21. Section 46-21 discriminated on basis of sex. The Equal Protections clauses of the federal and state constitutions did not prohibit all discrimination based on different classifications. The sex-based classification of § 46-21 was not unreasonable or arbitrary and had a fair and substantial relationship to the object of the statute. The legislature had the authority to make changes to spousal support proceedings, if necessary. Section 46-21 was constitutional and provided a sufficient jurisdictional base for the trial court's alimony award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's alimony pendent lite award to the wife.

Astarita v. Liquor Control Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


165 Conn. 185; 332 A.2d 106; 1973 Conn. LEXIS 725


June 8, 1973, Argued  
June 20, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the denial of an application for a grocery store beer permit, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Sponzo, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which the defendant city of Meriden et al. appealed to this court.

The appellee (plaintiff) filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and one of its zoning enforcement officers, appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut) that sustained the appeal of plaintiff, an unsuccessful applicant for a liquor license, after the liquor control commission denied his application for a grocery store beer permit.


OVERVIEW: Desiring a grocery store beer permit, the applicant requested that a zoning enforcement officer certify that the city zoning laws did not prohibit the sale of alcohol under such a permit at his grocery store, but the officer refused to sign a certification of compliance with the zoning ordinance. Rather than appealing to the zoning board of appeals, the applicant petitioned to the liquor control commission for a permit. Following a public hearing, the commission denied the application because the issuance of a permit for that location would violate city zoning laws. The applicant appealed, and the court of common pleas sustained the appeal. The city and its zoning enforcement officer appealed. In finding error and setting aside the judgment of the court of common pleas, the court concluded that the applicant failed to exhaust his administrative remedies. Upon being aggrieved by the zoning enforcement officer's decision, the applicant should have petitioned for review before the zoning board of appeals. Where such relief was available, it was improper for the applicant to seek judicial review on the very issue that should have been presented to the administrative agency.


OUTCOME: There was error, the judgment of the court of common pleas was set aside, and the case was remanded with directions to dismiss the appeal.

 

729 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Zoning Com. of Groton v. Tarasevich


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


165 Conn. 86; 328 A.2d 682; 1973 Conn. LEXIS 712


April 6, 1973, Argued  
June 5, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants from operating a trailer park and assessing a penalty for operation beyond the injunction date, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New London County and tried to the court, Bracken, J.; judgment granting the injunction and setting the penalty, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, owners of a mobile home park, appealed a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in New London County (Connecticut), which found for plaintiff zoning commission in the commission's action to enjoin the owners from operating their mobile home park without a license. The trial court also assessed a daily penalty against the owners for operation beyond the date of the injunction.


OVERVIEW: The commission sought to enjoin the owners from operating their mobile home park without a license and sought a penalty for each day of operation beyond the date of an injunction. The trial court granted the commission's request. The owners appealed, arguing that they were excused from compliance with Groton, Ct., Zoning Regs. No. 56 because the ordinance did not contain sufficiently definite standards to govern the exercise of the licensing power. Upon review, the court held that after revocation of the provisionally-issued license, it was incumbent on the owners to make application for a license and to satisfy the requirements of the ordinance, including certificates from the director of health and the building inspector, proof of ownership, and the public hearing fee. The owners had not at any time since the revocation of their license made application for a license under the provisions the ordinance. The owners, by their inaction, acquiesced in the revocation of their license. The mere possibility that, had the owners applied for a license, the commission might arbitrarily have denied their application did not place the issue of the validity of the ordinance before the court.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

Gelinas v. Nelson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


165 Conn. 33; 327 A.2d 565; 1973 Conn. LEXIS 705


April 3, 1973, Argued  
May 23, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Paternity proceedings, brought to the Circuit Court in the fourth circuit and tried to the jury before Monchun, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiff and appeal by the defendant to the Appellate Division of the Circuit Court, which affirmed the judgment; from the judgment of the Appellate Division, the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On certification, defendant putative father appealed a judgment of the Appellate Division of the Circuit Court (Connecticut), which affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of plaintiff mother in her action seeking to establish paternity and an award of child support.


OVERVIEW: The mother commenced a paternity action against the putative father alleging that he was in fact the father of her child and seeking child support. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the mother. The putative father appealed, arguing that the evidence before the jury was insufficient to support its verdict and that the attorney general appeared after final judgment in the trial court without having moved to intervene as an interested party. Upon review, the court held that in the absence of any evidence clearly indicating the time when the mother had intercourse with a person other than the putative father, the jury did not err in finding by a preponderance of the evidence the putative father was the father of the child. There was no indication from the record that the trial court was apprised of the putative father's objection to intervention by the attorney general. Although there were procedural irregularities, they did not constitute reversible error because the State had a clear interest in the outcome of the appeal and because the putative father showed no prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

Sumara v. Liquor Control Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

May 4, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant commission suspending a restaurant liquor permit on two charges, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Tolland County and tried to the court, Hamill, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal on the first charge and modifying the penalty imposed on the second charge, from which the defendant commission appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Liquor Control Commission, appealed from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Tolland County (Connecticut), which sustained the appeal of plaintiff restaurant owner from an action of the commission suspending the owner's restaurant liquor permit on one charge and modified the penalty imposed on the second charge.


OVERVIEW: In a hearing in which the owner appeared pro se, the commission found two violations of its regulations and suspended the owner's permit for 30 days on each charge, concurrently. The first violation, that the owner permitted a disturbance, brawl, and unlawful conduct, permitting the premises to become a nuisance, was supported by testimony of a police chief. The second violation was the owner's criminal conviction and failure to disclose prior arrests. The trial court, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-60, disregarded the chief's testimony as inadmissible, thus sustained the appeal from the first charge. The trial court found the second charge supported, but modified the penalty under § 30-60. On appeal, the court found error, and remanded for dismissal of the appeal. The court noted that while some of the chief's testimony was hearsay, his personal knowledge established some of the incidents supporting the commission's finding, thus the finding was not arbitrary and should not have been disturbed. The court held that § 30-60 did not allow the trial court to substitute its judgment for the commission, thus the modification of the suspension was improper.


OUTCOME: The court found error in the common pleas court judgment, set the judgment aside, and remanded with direction to dismiss the appeal.

 

732 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Villafane


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


164 Conn. 637; 325 A.2d 251; 1973 Conn. LEXIS 968


February 7, 1973, Argued  
May 2, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County; the defendant's plea in abatement and motion to quash sustained, Saden, J., and, on permission being granted, the state appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court, Fairfield County (Connecticut). Defendant was indicted for the crime of first-degree murder by an 18-member grand jury. He entered a plea of not guilty to the murder indictment and filed a plea in abatement and a motion to quash the indictment, which were sustained. The court granted the State permission to appeal pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 54-96.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was of Puerto Rican parentage. Spanish surnames had been used to determine the number of Puerto Rican electors eligible for grand jury duty in the county. Defendant's plea in abatement and motion to quash were sustained on grounds that defendant had established a prima facie case of systematic exclusion of Puerto Rican electors from grand jury service and that the method of selection used violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment because it failed to give Puerto Rican individuals a fair chance of being selected to serve on a grand jury. The State urged, inter alia, that it was error to sustain the plea and motion. Upon review, the court held that the trial court erred in quashing the indictment and in concluding that Spanish-surnamed persons were not exposed to a fair chance of selection as grand jurors because the conclusion that defendant had established a prima facie case was based on impermissible statistical proofs. Defendant's offer overestimated the percentage of Spanish-surnamed electors and thus rendered any conclusion based on it erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court found error. The plea in abatement and motion to quash were erroneously sustained. The court reinstated the grand jury indictment.

 

733 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Moynahan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


164 Conn. 560; 325 A.2d 199; 1973 Conn. LEXIS 962


January 3, 1973, Argued  
April 5, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of receiving stolen goods, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County at Waterbury and tried to the jury before Zarrilli, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court in New Haven County at Waterbury (Connecticut) for the crime of receiving stolen goods. Defendant assigned 32 errors to the rulings that had occurred during the course of the trial. The main issue concerned the jury charge as to the required elements of the crime of receiving stolen goods under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-65.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found in possession of a stolen television. Defendant was convicted of the crime of receiving stolen goods under § 53-65, which provided that the offense was committed by a person who received and concealed stolen goods or articles, knowing them to be stolen. On appeal the court found that the trial court's charges on the elements of knowledge and concealment were proper. The trial court, in relying on circumstantial evidence to prove knowledge, cautioned the jury that carelessness of the accused in ascertaining the facts was not enough, but that they must have found actual knowledge at the time the television was received and that such knowledge could have been inferred from the circumstances if they were such that a reasonable man of honest intentions should have come to that conclusion. The jury was instructed that concealment was not limited to proof that the stolen property was hidden or kept out of sight; it was enough that the property was withheld from the owner and made difficult for the owner to discover and could have been concluded if the jury believed that the television was placed by defendant in his sun porch out of view of the general public.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment convicting defendant of receiving stolen goods.

 

734 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Hartford Fire Ins. Co. v. Brown


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


164 Conn. 497; 325 A.2d 228; 1973 Conn. LEXIS 950


November 14, 1972, Argued  
March 21, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to vacate and set aside or to modify an assessment of penalties and interest against the plaintiffs for untimely payment of tax, and for general equitable relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County, where the defendant's demurrer to the prayers for relief was overruled, Rubinow, J., and the case was tried to the court, Radin, J.; judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiffs appealed.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) in favor of appellee in an action to vacate and set aside or modify an assessment of penalties and interest for untimely payment of taxes, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-204.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurance companies brought suit challenging the assessment of penalties by appellee tax commissioner. The trial court entered judgment in favor of appellee, and appellants challenged. On review the court found proper jurisdiction existed and held that the relationship between taxpayer and State was not like the traditional debtor-creditor relationship. The court held the question of timely payment was one dictated by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-204 and affirmed the trial court's findings that appellants had failed to make timely payment of taxes. The court further found that § 12-204 did not create an arbitrary and unreasonable classification against appellants, and it had ample remedies at law to challenge the assessed penalties. The court therefore rejected appellants' claims that the penalties violated their right to equal protection of the laws and affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the trial court's findings that appellants failed to pay taxes in a timely manner was not in error, and the statute dictating the terms of timely payment and assessment of penalties was not arbitrary and capricious in its imposition of penalties against appellants.

State v. Cobbs


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which, after a jury trial, convicted defendant of first degree murder, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-9.


OVERVIEW: The victim was found strangled and stabbed to death in his apartment. Defendant was seen by a friend in front of the apartment, putting a towel with blood or flowers on it in the back of a car, and told the friend that he killed a man. He later sold the friend a watch belonging to the victim. While in custody, he was read his Miranda rights. He initially refused to be questioned without a lawyer, but after speaking with his grandmother, admitted that he and a friend had attacked the victim. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court found no constitutional violation in the selection of grand jurors absent any proof of discrimination. The court held that while the method for selecting petit jurors used by six of the 23 towns from which the panel was chosen violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-221, it did not affect the entire panel, thus defendant has no basis for a challenge to the array. The court ruled that Miranda did not require a warning that defendant could stop answering questions at any time, and that the State established a voluntary waiver of defendant's right to counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court judgment.

McTigue v. New London Education Asso.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


164 Conn. 348; 321 A.2d 462; 1973 Conn. LEXIS 935; 88 L.R.R.M. 2614


December 7, 1972, Argued  
February 21, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action, in the first case, for an injunction to restrain the defendants from engaging in a strike, for damages and other relief, brought to the Superior Court in New London County, where the court, Armentano, J., issued an injunction enjoining the defendants from engaging in a strike and the court, Shea, J., granted a motion to cite the defendants for contempt; judgment adjudging the defendants to be in contempt, from which the defendants appealed.

Action, in the second case, for an injunction to restrain the defendants from engaging in a strike and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in New London County, where the court, Longo, J., issued an injunction enjoining the defendants from engaging in a strike and the court, Shea, J., granted a motion to cite the defendants for contempt; judgment adjudging the defendants to be in contempt, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a teacher's association and 182 individual teachers, appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in New London County (Connecticut), finding them in contempt for violation of an injunction enjoining them from engaging in a strike. The injunction was issued pursuant to motion filed by plaintiff, a board of education.


OVERVIEW: The board of education sought injunctions in two instances prohibiting the association and its teachers from engaging in a strike. On both occasions, the trial court issued injunctions stating that if a strike was implemented, the participants would be fined. The teachers subsequently engaged in a one-day strike after which they were cited for contempt of court. Although the teachers returned to their jobs on the next work day, the trial court found the association and certain teachers to be in contempt and ordered fines. On appeal, the association and the teachers argued that the contempt hearings were criminal hearings and that they had been denied rights implicit in a criminal trial. The court agreed, noting that the fines were made payable to the State and were designed to uphold the authority of the trial court. The court found that because the work stoppages had ceased, the fines imposed were not to coerce compliance but to punish for past violations. The court further held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-153e, which placed a prohibition on strikes by certified professional employees of the board of education, was constitutional and not violative of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The court found error. The judgments of contempt were set aside and a new trial was ordered in each case on the contempt issue.

 

737 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Caldwell v. Meskill


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


164 Conn. 299; 320 A.2d 788; 1973 Conn. LEXIS 928


December 7, 1972, Argued  
January 24, 1973, 1 Decided


1 For records and briefs see Vol. A-566.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of a partial and a conditional veto by the named defendant, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Naruk, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, legislators and cities, filed an action for a declaratory judgment as to whether defendant governor's veto was valid under Conn. Const. art. IV, §§ 15, 16. The Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), on request of plaintiffs, the governor, and the remaining defendants, the secretary of state, transportation commissioner, and the comptroller, filed a stipulation of facts and reserved the dispositive questions for the court.


OVERVIEW: The superior court reserved the following questions to the court: Does the governor have the power, under §§ 15, 16, to veto some sections of a bill while permitting others to become law? If not, does he have the power to provide, if his partial veto was successfully challenged, that his action be considered a veto of the entire bill? If not, was the secretary of state required to record the entire bill and certify it as law? The court found that § 16 conferred a limited power of partial veto in the case of appropriation bills. The governor's veto powers provided three options: he could have disapproved a bill and returned it to the legislature; he could have approved a bill, and it became law; or he could have done nothing, whereupon the bill became a law at the expiration of the five-day period. A partial veto of a non-appropriation bill was invalid and the answer to the first question was "No." The governor's conditional approval was not finalized within the five-day period, therefore the answer to the second question was "No." As the governor effectively vetoed none of the bill, it became a law at the expiration of the five-day, so the answer to the third question was "Yes."


OUTCOME: The court advised the superior court that the answers to the three questions reserved for the advice of the court were: Question 1, "No;" question 2, "No;" question 3, "Yes."

State v. Cofone


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


164 Conn. 162; 319 A.2d 381; 1972 Conn. LEXIS 665


November 9, 1972, Argued  
December 6, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Dannehy, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which accepted the jury verdict of guilty of murder in the first degree, and on a recommendation by the jury, set the penalty at death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with choking the victim to death during a robbery. Because defendant had been sentenced under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-10, which, under the holding of two United States Supreme Court cases decided while the case was on appeal, allowed unconstitutionally broad discretion in determining whether the death sentence should be imposed, the sentence was set aside. However, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that the jury could have reasonably concluded that defendant had the specific intent to deprive his victim of her property and that the murder was committed in the perpetration of a robbery. The court rejected defendant's claim that the evidence indicated that he was not sane at the time of the killing, noting that the testimony at to defendant's sanity was in dispute, and the credibility of the expert witnesses was to be determined by the trier of fact. The court also rejected defendant's claim that he was indicted for two distinct and separate offenses in one count because the indictment charged murder in the first degree and that the murder was willful, deliberate, and premeditated, and committed while in the perpetration of a robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but set aside the death penalty and remanded the case to the superior court with directions to impose a sentence of life imprisonment.

Miller v. Schaffer


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


164 Conn. 8; 320 A.2d 1; 1972 Conn. LEXIS 641


October 13, 1972, Argued  
October 17, 1972, 1 Decided


1 For record and briefs see Vol. A-566.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] In the above-entitled case, the Supreme Court on October 17, 1972, issued the following ruling from the Bench

On August 23, 1972, the Superior Court rendered judgment in the present case making certain corrections of clerical errors in the redistricting plan submitted by the reapportionment board, ordered that the plan as corrected be implemented and that the election of members of the General Assembly prescribed by article third, § 8, of the constitution of Connecticut be held pursuant to that plan in accordance with a detailed schedule. From that judgment the defendants appealed to this court.

On September 5, 1972, this court determined that it was in the public interest that these appeals from the judgment of the Superior Court be heard as soon as possible and motions for an expedited appeal were granted. The appeals were heard on October 13, 1972, the earliest possible date on which counsel were ready to proceed. In view of the present uncertainty concerning the exercise of the constitutional right of the electors of the state to elect members of the General Assembly at a general election to be held on the Tuesday after the first Monday of November in this year, it is [***2] in the public interest that the decision reached by this court be announced immediately.

It is clear that the Superior Court did not attempt to determine the federal constitutional issues now pending before the Supreme Court of the United States. Its judgment (1) corrected the clerical errors in the plan; (2) determined that a failure to elect the state legislative body would cause irreparable harm to the people of the state of Connecticut and violate their rights under the Connecticut constitution; (3) declared that the state board plan is valid and effective on an interim basis for the election mandated by the constitution for this fall; and (4) adopted a calendar setting up a schedule of dates to set in motion the state election process.

It is the opinion of this court that the conclusions of the trial court were legally correct and cannot be disturbed. A written opinion will be filed in due course.

This court will retain jurisdiction of this case.

Action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of a plan for revision of the districts represented in the General Assembly and an order requiring election officials to conduct primaries and elections in accordance therewith,  [***3] brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Sidor, J.; judgment ordering changes in the redistricting plan, ordering its implementation and the conduct of elections for members of the General Assembly in accordance with the plan and detailed schedules, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state and town officials, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which, in the action of plaintiff citizens and electors for a declaratory judgment and an order in the nature of mandamus, ordered changes in a plan for redistricting the districts represented in the legislature and ordered its implementation and the conduct of elections in accordance with the plan and detailed schedules.


OVERVIEW: The citizens and the electors brought an action seeking a declaratory judgment and an order in the nature of mandamus to declare a plan of apportionment adopted by a reapportionment board to be valid and effective for the next election and to require the state and municipal officials to conduct elections in accordance with the plan. The court declared the plan as construed and reformed to be valid and effective for interim use. The state and municipal officials argued that the trial court lacked capacity to make corrections to the plan. The court stated that there could be no doubt of the equity power of the trial court to make corrections to the plan. In construing legislative remedies for malapportionment enacted under the pressure of impending election deadlines, courts had to adopt flexible techniques to discharge the duty they shared with legislatures to secure constitutional apportionments in accordance with decisions of the United States Supreme Court. The trial court's conclusion that the board plan segmented towns in order to meet the federal equal population requirement was amply supported by the subordinate facts and did not violate state constitutional requirements.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the trial court's conclusions were legally correct and could not be disturbed.

State v. Aillon

October 6, 1972, decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned for review of the judgment of the superior court (Connecticut), which denied his motions for release on bail from his confinement as the result of his arrest on three charges of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was confined following his arrest on three separate charges of murder. The trial court denied his motion for release on bail under Conn. Gen. Hope v. Cavallo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


163 Conn. 576; 316 A.2d 407; 1972 Conn. LEXIS 798


June 6, 1972, Argued  
September 20, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in two counts to recover damages for personal injuries and property damage, alleged to have been caused by the negligence of the defendants, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County, where a motion by the defendants pursuant to Practice Book § 306 was found in their favor, FitzGerald, J., and thereafter the defendants' motion for judgment was granted, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.

The appellee, the state of Connecticut, filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the judgment from the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which found for defendants, the State and a guardsman, in plaintiffs' negligence action arising out of a collision involving plaintiffs' vehicle and a truck issued to the Connecticut Air National Guard by the United States. The trial court held as a matter of law that the State did not own the truck and could not be liable under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-556.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the guardsman was immune from personal liability under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. Plaintiffs assigned error in the trial court's failure to conclude that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-556 permitted an action against the State and argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165 was unconstitutional. Plaintiffs alleged that the truck driven by the guardsman was owned by the State, in that the State at the time of the accident, through the Connecticut Air National Guard, had the exclusive control and possession of it under the provisions of Air National Guard Reg. 67-1; that the State had a special ownership in the vehicle as bailee at the time of the collision; and that the State had specifically insured the vehicle under the definition in its insurance policy defining the term "owned automobile." Finding error, the court held that where a truck was in the continual, exclusive, and total possession and use of the State, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-556 contemplated that liability under the statute had to be imposed on the State if the vehicle was insured. Because that holding was dispositive of plaintiffs' appeal, the court did not discuss plaintiffs' other assignments of error.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with the court's ruling that the State could be held liable for plaintiffs' personal injuries and property damage because the truck was in the continual, exclusive, and total possession and use of the State and was insured.

Hames v. Hames


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


163 Conn. 588; 316 A.2d 379; 1972 Conn. LEXIS 799


June 6, 1972, Argued  
September 20, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County for an annulment, a divorce and partition of real estate; motions for custody and support of minor children, alimony and counsel fees pendente lite granted, Testo, J., from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant alleged husband appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which ruled that the parties were legally married under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46-3 and ordered payment by the alleged husband on motion by plaintiff alleged wife for custody pendente lite and support of minor children, alimony, and counsel fees in an action brought by the alleged wife for an annulment, a divorce, and partition of real estate.


OVERVIEW: The parties agreed to re-marry after a prior divorce. The parties obtained a marriage license but did not participate in a marriage ceremony after the divorce. The parties resumed marital life and had three children. The alleged wife brought an action against the alleged husband, seeking an annulment, a divorce, and equitable relief. Following a hearing on a motion by the alleged wife for pendente lite custody of the parties' minor children, support, and alimony, the trial court found that the parties were legally married under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46-3 and ordered payment by the alleged husband as sought in the motions. The alleged husband appealed, attacking the trial court's determination that there was a valid marriage. On appeal, the court held that the purported marriage, which was deficient for want of due solemnization, was voidable rather than void insofar as the term "voidable" may have implied an absolute nullity. Religious doctrines notwithstanding, the parties were legally divorced. Even though the alleged wife appeared with the alleged husband in obtaining a marriage license, there was no solemnization for the purposes of § 46-3.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's judgment, which had ruled that the parties were legally married, and remanded the case for further proceedings not inconsistent with the court's opinion.

Peterson v. Sullivan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


163 Conn. 520; 313 A.2d 49; 1972 Conn. LEXIS 794


June 13, 1972, Argued  
July 27, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision of the defendant disallowing the plaintiffs' claim for a tax refund, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Rubinow, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which affirmed defendant tax commissioner's decision denying the taxpayers' claim for a refund of a capital gains tax which they had paid.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers owned various capital assets that they had acquired prior to July 1, 1969 and which they sold during the period from July 1, 1969 and December 31, 1969. They timely filed a Connecticut capital gains tax return and paid tax. The taxpayers computed their net capital gain on a form prescribed by the tax commissioner by deducting the adjusted basis in the goods from the proceeds derived from the sales and exchanges. The taxpayers thereafter filed an amended return for the same period, which showed a net capital loss and sought a refund of the tax paid as overpayment of their capital gains tax. The tax commissioner denied the claim and the court affirmed. Realization of gain by the sale or exchange of a capital asset was the time fixed for the imposition of the tax. Because both Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 12-505-12-522 (1969), (1971) specifically incorporated the federal system of taxing capital gain, the tax commissioner was correct in holding that the cost basis for determining the amount of the taxpayers' capital gain was determined under the provisions of the federal Internal Revenue Code, which was, generally, cost.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which affirmed the tax commissioner's denial of the taxpayers' claim for a refund of a capital gains tax which they had paid.

 

745 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Slavitt v. Ives


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


163 Conn. 198; 303 A.2d 13; 1972 Conn. LEXIS 764


March 7, 1972, Argued  
June 6, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the assessment of damages for land taken for highway purposes, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and referred to Hon. Samuel Mellitz, state referee; judgments for the plaintiffs on the referee's amended reports, MacDonald, J., from which the plaintiff The Holson Company appealed in each case to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error in The Holson Company case; error in part in the Slavitt case and new trial ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee highway commissioner condemned two properties, each of which was being rented by appellant lessee. After the commissioner filed assessments of damages, the lessee appealed to the Superior Court of Fairfield County (Connecticut), which in separate judgments for each property awarded the lessee damages for the value of its trade fixtures and for the value of its leasehold interest. The lessee appealed both judgments.


OVERVIEW: The lessee conducted a business in adjoining buildings located on the two properties. The court first held that the lessee's interest in the first property should have been valued as of May 9, 1966, the date the commissioner took the lessee's right of access to the property, rather than as of the later date on which the lessee was physically dispossessed of the property. Thus, the court concluded, although the referee appointed by the trial court did not err in adopting the valuation method presented by the commissioner's expert witness, a new trial was required on the issue of the valuation of the leasehold as of May 9, 1966. The court added that in awarding compensation for trade fixtures, it was proper for the referee to consider what effect those fixtures that had become an integral part of the realty might have on the value of the building. The court held that the lessee was not entitled to the fair and reasonable value of its moving expenses. Stating that the lessee would have sustained those expenses at the termination of its leases anyway, the court held that such losses were consequential in nature and were not compensable unless the legislature provided for them.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no error in the case involving the second property. Holding that there was error in the case involving the first property, the court remanded that case for a new trial limited to the issue of the valuation of the leasehold interest in the first property.

 

746 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


163 Conn. 52; 301 A.2d 547; 1972 Conn. LEXIS 749


February 2, 1972, Argued  
May 3, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of the illegal sale of narcotics, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the jury before Grillo, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which convicted him of the crime of the illegal sale of narcotics.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in a jury trial of sale of narcotics in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480 (a). Defendant's motion to set aside the verdict was denied by the trial court. In an undercover operation, defendant sold 30 glassine bags of heroin to an undercover officer. Another officer observed the sale through a one-way glass window on a truck about six feet away. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in admitting the 30 glassine bags into evidence because the State failed to establish that the bags were the same bags he sold to the officer by producing all the witnesses who handled the bags until trial. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct jurors on the lesser-included offense of possession of a narcotic drug. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction because there was no hard and fast rule that the State must exclude or disprove all possibility that the article or substance had been tampered with. The court also held that an accused was only entitled to have the jury instructed as to a lesser offense if there was a rational basis for an acquittal on the offense charged and a conviction on the included offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

747 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Application of Griffiths


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


162 Conn. 249; 294 A.2d 281; 1972 Conn. LEXIS 876


October 8, 1971, Argued  
January 26, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for a decree that Fre Le Poole Griffiths be admitted to take the bar examination and that she be declared eligible for admission to the bar, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and heard by the court, Wright, J.; judgment denying the petition, from which the applicant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner bar applicant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which denied her petition for admission to take the bar examination and declared that she was ineligible for admission to the bar under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 8(1). The applicant, a resident alien, claimed that § 8(1) violated the Equal Protection Clause, the Supremacy Clause, and the First Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The bar applicant, an alien, claimed that the restriction of bar admission to U.S. citizens discriminated against aliens, depriving them of equal protection of laws. The applicant also contended that § 8(1) contravened the federal power over immigration and unconstitutionally burdened her right to determine her nationality, violating her First Amendment rights. The Trial court disagreed. On appeal, the court held that § 8(1) did not violate the applicant's equal protection rights because it was reasonable and did not invidiously discriminate against aliens. The court reasoned that the state had a compelling interest in insuring that members of the bar did not owe their primary allegiance to a foreign power because of their status as officers of the court. The court held that § 8(1) was not repugnant to the federal power over immigration because it did not unreasonably burden the applicant's interstate movement or interfere with her right to share in economic or social benefits in her community of residence. Because § 8(1) was not designed to restrict the rights of aliens but to protect the rights of U.S. citizens, the court held that it did not violate the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied the bar applicant's petition to be admitted to the bar examination and that also declared that the applicant was ineligible for admission to the bar because she was not a U.S. citizen.

 

748 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


162 Conn. 215; 292 A.2d 903; 1972 Conn. LEXIS 872


December 8, 1971, Argued  
January 19, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of narcotics, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the court, Wright, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) convicted defendant of possession of narcotics. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: While conducting a search for dynamite in defendant's apartment pursuant to a valid search warrant, police officers found marijuana in defendant's refrigerator. Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress the evidence and in refusing to require the State to reveal the name of the informer. The court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence and to reveal the identity of the confidential informant. The search was carried out pursuant to a valid search warrant and the marijuana was properly seized as evidence of a crime. Because the informer was not involved in any crime involving the dynamite, the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to compel the State to reveal the informer's identity. Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in admitting the marijuana into evidence because the State failed to prove that the evidence had been properly preserved. The court held that the marijuana was properly admitted into evidence. The State's evidence clearly identified the marijuana as the substance that was removed from defendant's apartment and the chain of custody was properly handled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of narcotics.

Supreme Court of Connecticut


162 Conn. 605; 291 A.2d 227; 1971 Conn. LEXIS 515


Submitted November 24, 1973  
November 30, 1971, decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for review of the action of the Circuit Court for the fourteenth circuit dismissing an appeal and terminating a stay of execution after judgment on default. Motion dismissed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for review of an order of the Circuit Court for the Fourteenth Circuit (Connecticut) dismissing her appeal and terminating a stay of execution after judgment on default for failure to post an appellate bond.


OVERVIEW: The trial court rendered a default judgment against defendant in a summary process action. The judgment was appealed to the appellate court. While the appeal was pending, defendant filed a motion for review with the court, which was denied in the absence of a finding pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 694. Defendant made a second filing of the same motion and also made a request for a finding to the court. In dismissing the motion for review, the court held that a motion for review could not be addressed to the court pending a final decision by the appellate court. The court also held that a request for findings was required to be filed with the trial court and not addressed to and filed with the court.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the motion for review.

State v. Delgado


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


161 Conn. 536; 290 A.2d 338; 1971 Conn. LEXIS 589


June 3, 1971, Argued  
November 23, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to a statutory court, Shapiro, Loiselle and Barber, Js.; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of his conviction and sentence of the Superior Court, Hartford County (Connecticut). An indictment had charged defendant with the crime of murder in the first degree. It was alleged that he shot and killed a police officer. The case was tried to a statutory three-judge court. A judgment of guilty was entered and, after a full hearing, the death penalty was imposed.


OVERVIEW: The police officer was shot and killed by defendant while he was taking defendant to the police station after arresting him on a valid warrant. While the officer was driving, defendant grabbed the steering wheel. The officer stopped the cruiser and the two struggled. They wrestled on the ground, both struggling for the officer's gun. One shot was fired, hitting defendant. Defendant struck the officer several times on the head with the nightstick and took his gun. While the officer was lying still, face down, defendant stood over him and shot the officer repeatedly in the back and head. Defendant was subsequently apprehended. Several eyewitnesses, who were passengers on a bus passing the scene, established that defendant shot and killed the officer. Defendant claimed that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he was guilty of murder in the first degree. The court found no error in defendant's conviction and sentence for first-degree murder, as the evidence supported the conclusion that defendant's killing of the officer was wilful, deliberate, premeditated, and with malice aforethought. Nor was imposition of the death penalty an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in defendant's conviction and sentence for murder in the first degree.

State ex rel. Kelman v. Schaffer

DISPOSITION: Error; judgments directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff potential electors filed an application for a writ of mandamus and declaratory judgment action against defendants, secretary of state and related parties, for a determination of whether an elector under age 21 was prohibited from holding municipal office. The potential electors sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut) in favor of defendants.


OVERVIEW: The potential electors sought a writ of mandamus ordering that their names be placed on the ballot as candidates for the town council. The potential electors also requested a declaratory judgment that the Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-1 was unconstitutional as violative of the U.S. Const. amend. XXVI. The trial court denied the petitions for writs of mandamus and rendered a declaratory judgment that the statute did not prohibit citizens under the age of 21 from holding municipal office in the towns where they resided. The court held that the potential electors failed to comply with the jurisdictional requirements of notice to or joinder of necessary parties and, therefore, the trial court lacked jurisdiction to have entertained the potential electors' claims. The declaratory judgment claim should have been dismissed for lack of jurisdiction.
