State v. Darwin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


161 Conn. 413; 288 A.2d 422; 1971 Conn. LEXIS 576


June 3, 1971, Argued  
July 6, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in Tolland County and tried to a statutory court, MacDonald, Barber and Palmer, Js.; judgment of guilty of murder in the second degree and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court, Tolland County (Connecticut) for murder in the second-degree and the orders denying his motions to suppress and to dismiss. Defendant was sentenced to the state prison for life for the conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested on a coroner's warrant. A vehicle owned by his wife was searched and evidence was seized. He was charged by indictment with first degree murder. Prior to trial, he filed a motion to suppress the evidence seized in the search of the vehicle, which was granted. After the vehicle was returned to his wife, a search warrant was obtained and evidence was again seized from the vehicle. He was then convicted of second degree murder and that conviction was subsequently reversed by the United States Supreme Court. He then filed a motion to suppress the evidence and to dismiss, which were denied. He was convicted by a three-judge panel of second degree murder. On appeal, the court set aside his conviction. The search warrant was defective because there were insufficient facts upon which the magistrate could have found probable cause and the motion to suppress should have been granted. With regard to the admission of testimony regarding incriminating statements made by defendant in jail, the trial court erred by failing to determine whether he was aware that prior warnings applied to his conversations in jail and whether he waived his right to have counsel present.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's judgment convicting defendant and ordered a new trial.

Hartford v. Larrabee Fund Asso.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


161 Conn. 312; 288 A.2d 71; 1971 Conn. LEXIS 565


April 8, 1971, Argued  
June 21, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of a special act of the legislature applicable to a charitable trust, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Rubinow, J.; judgment for the plaintiff and appeal by the named defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) in favor of plaintiff trustee in the trustee's action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of 1941 Conn. Spec. Acts 161, which was applicable to a charitable trust.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a will, a portion of a testator's estate was bequeathed in trust, to create a fund for specified purposes, to be distributed in a specified manner, and an unincorporated association was formed for distribution. Subsequently, the association requested the passage of a special act incorporating the association, which resulted in 1941 Conn. Spec. Acts 161, and the association became a corporation. The trustee brought a declaratory judgment action determining the constitutionality of the special act. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the trustee, and the corporation sought review. On appeal, the court found that not only the purposes of the trust, but the method of distribution and the composition of the distributing body, were testamentary in nature. The court held that, by incorporating the association and revising its structure, the legislature had reinterpreted the will, which was unconstitutional. The court ruled that the special act was void because it violated Conn. Const. art. 2 concerning the separation of powers.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment in favor of the trustee in its action to determine the constitutionality of a special act that was applicable to a charitable trust. The court affirmed that the special act was unconstitutional.

 

754 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Ducharme v. Putnam


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


161 Conn. 135; 285 A.2d 318; 1971 Conn. LEXIS 543


March 5, 1971, Argued  
April 20, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the defendants from a finding and award of the workmen's compensation commissioner for the second district, brought to the Superior Court in Windham County and tried to the court, Loiselle, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city employer appealed the dismissal by the Superior Court in Windham County (Connecticut) of their appeal of a workmen's compensation commissioner's decision in favor of plaintiff, a police officer employee, in a workmen's compensation action.


OVERVIEW: The employee passed his physical examination to be a police officer. While at work, the employee suffered a heart attack. The employee claimed that he was automatically entitled to workmen's compensation benefits because of the statutory presumptive conclusion created by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433a. Section 7-433a provided that any heart attack suffered while at work as a police officer was to be deemed to have arisen out of and in the course of employment once the physical examination was passed. The employer claimed that the heart condition was pre-existing. The superior court dismissed the employer's appeal of a decision in favor of the employee. The court reversed, holding that the conclusive presumption was unconstitutional pursuant to the Due Process Clauses of the federal and state constitutions. The employer should have been allowed the opportunity to prove that it was not liable. While the legislature had the authority to provide a gift to police officers, § 7-433a was not intended to be a gift but a conclusive presumption. The employer, though a city, had a legal interest and standing to challenge § 7-433a, though the employer was created by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision in favor of the employee and ruled in favor of the employer.

Hotchkiss Grove Ass'n v. Water Resources Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


161 Conn. 50; 282 A.2d 890; 1971 Conn. LEXIS 536; 1 ELR 20248; 2 ERC (BNA) 1487


March 4, 1971, Argued  
March 30, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant commission in issuing a permit to instal a stone pier, mooring piles, a ramp and a float, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Klau, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, neighborhood association and abutting landowners, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal from the decision of defendant Water Resources Commission of the State of Connecticut. The Commission issued a permit to install a stone pier and moorings to the applicants because the work did not violate any provision of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 25-7b.


OVERVIEW: The applicants applied to the Commission for permission to erect a stone pier from the property into the waters of Long Island Sound. The Commission found no violation of § 25-7b. Plaintiffs appealed to the trial court. The trial court dismissed their appeal. On appeal, the court found error, set aside the judgment, and ordered a new trial. The court found that the Commission's failure to notify plaintiffs of the hearing was not a denial of due process because a hearing was available through an appeal to the courts before the permit became effective. The court found that § 25-7b was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority because it contained sufficient standards. The court found that the role of the reviewing court was to determine if the Commission had acted legally. The court noted that if the Commission had held a hearing, the review would have been based on the record. Since there was no hearing, the trial court should have allowed plaintiffs to offer testimony and evidence so that it could determine if the Commission acted legally. The failure of the trial court to allow evidence was reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court found error, set aside the judgment of the trial court, and ordered a new trial.

Bartlett v. Zoning Com. of Old Lyme


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


161 Conn. 24; 282 A.2d 907; 1971 Conn. LEXIS 533; 1 ELR 20177


March 4, 1971, Argued  
March 24, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant amending the zoning regulations, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New London County and tried to the court, Bracken, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant zoning commission challenged a decision of the Court of Common Pleas in New London County (Connecticut), which sustained plaintiff landowner's challenge to an action of defendant adopting a change of zone affecting plaintiff's land.


OVERVIEW: Defendant made a change to the zoning of plaintiff's land in an effort to protect wetlands. Plaintiff appealed the change. The trial court sustained plaintiff's appeal, and defendant sought review. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The rezoning, which imposed very strict limitations on property designated as wetlands, deprived plaintiff, for all practical purposes, of the use of his land. Even if plaintiff were granted a special exception to the zoning, he was still be deprived of any practical use of his land. The court held that the restrictions were so unreasonable and confiscatory as to amount to a taking of the land for a public use, and, because there was no provision for compensation, the adoption of the zoning regulations, so far as they affected the property of plaintiff, violated both the U.S. Constitution and Conn. Const., art. I, § 11. As to plaintiff's property, the action complained of was unreasonable, confiscatory and unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no error in the decision of the trial court sustaining plaintiff's appeal of zoning regulations that operated to deprive him of the use of his land without just compensation.

Aunt Hack Ridge Estates, Inc. v. Planning Com. of Danbury


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


160 Conn. 109; 273 A.2d 880; 1970 Conn. LEXIS 604; 1 ELR 20192; 2 ERC (BNA) 1164


October 8, 1970, Argued  
December 1, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of General Statutes § 8-25 and a subdivision regulation adopted pursuant thereto, and for an injunction, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and reserved by the court, Fitz-Gerald, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which reversed an injunction the landowners obtained against defendant planning commission The landowners had brought an action for a declaratory judgment against the planning commission to determine the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-25 and a subdivision regulation adopted pursuant thereto.


OVERVIEW: The subdivision regulation required the landowners to provide for a park or playground on their land. The issue before the court was whether the subdivision regulation and the portion of § 8-25, which pertained to open spaces for parks and playgrounds, was unconstitutional. When the landowners acquired the property, there was no subdivision regulation requiring a park or playground. The landowners claimed that § 8-25 was unconstitutional because it was vague and uncertain, lacked required standards, was an arbitrary and discriminatory abuse of the police power and amounted to an unauthorized tax for the use of the land. The court disagreed and held that § 8-25 and the regulation were valid and constitutional exercises of the state's police power. The court found that the setting aside of land for recreational use by the planning committee was rationally related to the public welfare and was reasonably impartial as it provided for a minimum park or playground area of 10,000 square fees, or a maximum area of four percent of the total area of the subdivision. The court found such requirements were clear and sufficiently specific.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the planning commission and held that the subdivision regulation imposed by the planning commission against the landowners was constitutional.

 

758 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Furtney v. Simsbury Zoning Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


159 Conn. 585; 271 A.2d 319; 1970 Conn. LEXIS 506


June 3, 1970, Argued  
July 14, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the granting of an application for a change of zone, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, O'Sullivan, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, opponents of a change of zone for two parcels of land from single family residential to designed business development zone, appealed a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal of a decision of defendant local zoning commission. The commission had approved the change of zone on the application of defendant option holder, who had an option to purchase the land in question.


OVERVIEW: The option holder sought the change in zone in order to build a shopping center on the land. The town plan commission had voted to recommend that the application be denied, but after a hearing before the commission, the requested change was granted. On review, the court rejected the opponents' claim that two commission members were disqualified to sit as members of the commission in the instant case, finding that the fact that one of the members had business dealings with the option holder was not enough to disqualify him; nor was the fact that he had a prior opinion about the best use of the land in question. The second member was challenged on the ground that he had not been properly appointed to the commission, but the court found that, although the member had not been properly sworn in, he was a de facto officer and not subject to challenge n that ground. The court also held that, in approving the change of zone, the commission considered the proper factors and that the change of zone did not violate the comprehensive plan of the town. Noting the limited scope of review of local zoning decisions, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: Finding no error, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

759 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harris


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


159 Conn. 521; 271 A.2d 74; 1970 Conn. LEXIS 499


May 8, 1970, Argued  
June 23, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in two counts charging the defendant with the crimes of illegal possession of a narcotic drug and larceny, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the jury before Devlin, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty on the first count and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which found him guilty of possessing, or having under his control, a narcotic drug.


OVERVIEW: The police obtained a warrant for the search of defendant's home based on information received from a confidential informant. Heroin was found secreted in the house, and he was convicted of possession of a narcotic drug. He challenged his conviction, and the court affirmed. The affidavit that supported the warrant was properly based on not only the police officer's knowledge but also the knowledge of the informant. Thus, there was a substantial basis for the judge to conclude that heroin was probably present in the premises described. It was not improper to prevent defendant from obtaining the identity of the confidential informant where defendant failed to show that the disclosure of the informant's identity was essential to assure a fair determination of the issues. Defendant failed to allege that disclosure of the informant's identity supported his defense. It was not error to admit evidence of needle marks on defendant's arm because he claimed that he no longer used heroin and that he was unaware of the existence of the heroin in his home. Further, he failed to prove that he had any statutory authorization for possession of the drug.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of the narcotic drug heroin.

 

760 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Menillo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


159 Conn. 264; 268 A.2d 667; 1970 Conn. LEXIS 469


February 3, 1970, Argued  
March 11, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion by the defendant for a review of the order of the Superior Court in New Haven County at Waterbury, Meyers, J., denying bail.



DISPOSITION: Motion granted; new hearing ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Superior Court in New Haven County at Waterbury (Connecticut), which denied bail.


OVERVIEW: Apparently in the course of committing an abortion upon a woman, defendant killed her. As a result, a grand jury indicted him for the crime of murder in the first degree. After the grand jury had returned the murder indictment, defendant made an application to be admitted to bail, which the superior court denied. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the superior court erred in deciding that the grand jury's first-degree murder indictment was conclusive proof that defendant was within the constitutional exception disentitling him to bail, Conn. Const. art. first, § 8, and that, as a matter of law, bail was not permissible in any capital case. Hence, defendant's application for bail had to be remanded for a new hearing to determine whether he fell within the constitutional exception denying bail in a capital case "where the proof was evident or the presumption great," Conn. Const. art. first, § 8. The court further held that bail should be denied in a capital case, when the circumstances indicated a fair likelihood that the defendant was in danger of a jury verdict of first-degree murder.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the superior court's order denying bail and directed the superior court to grant a new hearing on defendant's motion for bail, to be conducted in conformity with the court's opinion.

 

761 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Fishman v. Stamford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


159 Conn. 116; 267 A.2d 443; 1970 Conn. LEXIS 455


December 3, 1969, Argued  
February 3, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants from condemning land for redevelopment purposes, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County at Stamford and tried to the court, Sidor, J.; judgment for the defendants and appeal by the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner appealed from a judgment entered by the Superior Court in Fairfield County at Stamford (Connecticut), which found in favor of defendants, a city and others, in the owner's action for an injunction restraining defendants from condemning the owner's land for redevelopment purposes.


OVERVIEW: The city's Urban Redevelopment Commission adopted a redevelopment plan for an area that included the owner's small parking lot. Although the Commission originally did not intend to take the parking lot, it subsequently voted to take it. Accordingly, the Commission modified the redevelopment plan to include the parking lot as property to be taken. The owner asserted, inter alia, that the modification of the plan failed to conform to statutory guidelines and that the taking violated his due process rights. On appeal, the court rejected all of the owner's contentions of error. The court held that the Commission was authorized to modify the plan pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-136. Moreover, the Commission acted in strict accordance with § 8-136. There was no merit in the owner's claim that he was entitled to a hearing on the legality of the taking before the taking became final. Furthermore, the reuse of the parking lot property for church purposes was not a taking for private purposes or a direct grant to religion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of defendants.

 

762 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Collins v. York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


159 Conn. 150; 267 A.2d 668; 1970 Conn. LEXIS 458


January 8, 1970, Argued  
February 3, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus alleging unlawful imprisonment, brought to the Superior Court in New London County and tried to the court, Wright, J.; judgment for the plaintiff and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Connecticut State Farm for Women, sought review of an order of the superior court (Connecticut) that granted plaintiff's petition for habeas corpus. Her petition alleged that her confinement was illegal because the circuit court, which had convicted her of being in manifest danger of falling into habits of vice in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-379, had sentenced her to a term in excess of its authority.


OVERVIEW: When plaintiff, age 16, pled guilty to being in manifest danger of falling into habits of vice, she was committed to an indeterminate term at the state farm. After she violated parole, she was returned to the state farm. She sought habeas corpus on grounds that the circuit court had authority only to confine her for one year. The court reversed the grant of her petition. The court based its decision on an interpretation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-81a, which set out the circuit court's jurisdiction and its inability to impose imprisonment for a term beyond 1 year, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-379, which allowed unmarried females over the age of 16 who were in danger of falling into habits of vice to be committed to a state institution until they reached age 21, and Conn. Gen. Stat. 18-65, which dealt with the authority of a court of criminal jurisdiction to commit females over the age of 16 to state institutions. Because Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 54-81a and 17-379 were adopted in the same act, the legislature intended to give the circuit court the jurisdiction which had existed previously in justices of the peace to commit girls such as plaintiff to a state institution until they were age 21.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the superior court's judgment granting plaintiff's petition for habeas corpus. The court remanded the case with direction to render judgment for the state school.

 

763 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Sheridan v. Planning Bd. of Stamford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


159 Conn. 1; 266 A.2d 396; 1969 Conn. LEXIS 509


November 5, 1969, Argued  
December 23, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, in the first and second cases, from the action of the defendant board in amending the master plan, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford and tried to the court, Levine, J.; judgments dismissing the appeals, from which the plaintiffs and the defendants appealed to this court.

Appeal, in the third case, from the action of the defendant board in approving an amendment of the zoning regulations, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford and tried to the court, Levine, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs and the defendants appealed to this court.

Appeal, in the fourth case, from the action of the defendant board in granting an application for a change of zone, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford and tried to the court, Levine, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.

The plaintiffs filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error in form of judgment; judgment directed. No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs and defendants appealed from judgments of the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford (Connecticut), which dismissed the appeals of plaintiffs from the action of defendant board in amending the master plan, approving an amendment of the zoning regulations, and granting an application for a change of zone.


OVERVIEW: Four appeals, which essentially arose from one transaction, were tried together. They all involved the same piece of property. A trustee intended to obtain a change in the master plan and zoning map so that slightly more than half of the tract could be used for industrial purposes. Plaintiffs appealed the action of the board and the court dismissed the appeals. Plaintiffs and defendants appealed and the court held that only two acts of a planning board were binding without further action by a zoning commission or other municipal agency: action on a subdivision plan, and designation of and assessments for municipal improvements. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-30 provided for appeals from designation of municipal improvements and assessments. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-28 must be interpreted as permitting appeals solely from actions taken on subdivision applications. The court decided that two of the appealed required dismissal based on lack of jurisdiction. The court found error in the trial court's conclusions and held that that plaintiffs in one case were not aggrieved as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the case with the zoning board. The court found error in the form of the judgment in the cases involving the planning board and the board of representatives and set aside each judgment with directions to the trial court regarding the forms of judgment.

Broadriver, Inc. v. Stamford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


158 Conn. 522; 265 A.2d 75; 1969 Conn. LEXIS 628


October 14, 1969, Argued  
December 3, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants from proceeding with the condemnation of the plaintiff's land, for a judgment that the defendants have no right, title or interest in the plaintiff's land, for damages, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County at Stamford and tried to the court, Sidor, J.; judgment for the defendants and appeal by the plaintiff.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sought review of the decision of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which entered judgment in favor defendant city in the property owner's action seeking an injunction in order to restrain the city from proceeding with the condemnation of its land.


OVERVIEW: The property owner, a corporation, prayed for an injunction to restrain the city from condemning its property and to restrain the city from filing further condemnation papers. On appeal, the property owner attacked the city's "taking" procedure. First, the property owner alleged the certificate of taking was not issued by the clerk of the court, nor recorded in the town clerk's office within the time period set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-129. The court found that the city's procedure was proper because the city refrained from taking any further steps until the trial court acted on the property owner's complaint. Moreover, the court held that the clerk did not issue the certificate of taking until the trial court denied the property owner's application for temporary injunctions. Additionally, the trial court stated the 90 days requirement set forth in § 8-129 was to guard against harm caused by an unreasonable delay. However, the court held that, under the circumstances, strict compliance with the 90 day time requirement was not required in order to accomplish a valid taking of the property owner's land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

765 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Appeal of Bailey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


158 Conn. 439; 262 A.2d 177; 1969 Conn. LEXIS 618


October 8, 1969, Argued  
November 6, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Marian Bailey from the order of the Juvenile Court for the first district transferring Jesse Bailey, Jr., a minor, from the Connecticut School for Boys to the Connecticut Reformatory, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and reserved by the court, Radin, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order from the Juvenile Court for the First District (Connecticut), which was brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut) and reserved by that court. The juvenile court transferred appellant's son from the Connecticut School for Boys located in Meriden (Meriden) to the Connecticut Reformatory, a correctional institution for boys under 21 years of age located in Cheshire (Cheshire).


OVERVIEW: The juvenile court transferred appellant's son from Meriden to Cheshire. Appellant argued that because Cheshire was a penal institution, her son was entitled to a public hearing and a jury trial before he could be transferred. Appellant and the attorney general requested the superior court to reserve for the court the question whether Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-77 (formerly Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-394) (repealed) was unconstitutional because it allowed incarceration in a penal institution without actual conviction. The court answered the question in the negative. The actual character of Cheshire in relation to appellant's son determined whether Cheshire was a penal institution. The statement of facts in the reservation contained nothing about the character of Cheshire, its facilities, or how it handled transferees from Meriden such as appellant's son. It contained no facts on which the court could hold that Cheshire was a penal institution. Although commitment to Cheshire was authorized upon conviction, it was only authorized if the superior court found that the convict was amenable to reformatory methods. That alone implied that Cheshire was clearly different from a jail or prison.


OUTCOME: The court answered the reserved question in the negative.

Sullivan v. Fairfield County Trust Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


158 Conn. 325; 260 A.2d 568; 1969 Conn. LEXIS 609


June 4, 1969, Argued  
June 23, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decree of the Probate Court for the district of Cornwall denying that a succession tax was due and owing on an inter vivos transfer in trust, brought to the Superior Court in Litchfield County and tried to the court, Shapiro, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Tax Commissioner of the State of Connecticut appealed a judgment from the Superior Court, Litchfield County (Connecticut) that dismissed an appeal from a probate court decision denying that a succession tax was due and owing on an inter vivos trust administered by defendant executors.


OVERVIEW: Under a grandfather's will, the decedent's father was given power to appoint the residuary estate by will. The father's will continued the trust after his death, at which time the trust vested in his issue, including the decedent. The father disposed of his own residuary estate by creating a trust for the benefit of his children, including the decedent, conditioned on the children's execution of an irrevocable inter vivos trust indenture similar to the father's residuary trust. The consideration for the trust was the money vesting from the grandfather's estate. The decedent timely created the required trust and lived on the income from the corpus of the trust until her death. The parties agreed that the trust fell under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-341b (1964) for purposes of taxation. The Commissioner argued that offset provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-341b(d) regarding taxation of the consideration for the trust did not apply because consideration had to come to the transferor from the transferee. On appeal, the court disagreed. Section 12-341b only required that the transferor receive consideration. It did not prescribe the source of the consideration.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

Simmons v. Parizek


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


158 Conn. 304; 259 A.2d 642; 1969 Conn. LEXIS 606


May 9, 1969, Argued  
June 17, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action of ejectment claiming possession of premises and damages, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County, where a demurrer to the complaint was sustained, Radin, J., and, the plaintiff failing to plead further, judgment was rendered for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which granted a demurrer filed by defendant members of an aeronautics commission of the State of Connecticut in an ejectment action that was filed by the owner.


OVERVIEW: The owner alleged that the members wrongfully entered upon his land, dispossessed him, and deprived him of rents and profits. The members' demurrer was based on the ground that the action was one against the State and that it was not maintainable without the consent of the State. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly sustained the demurrer to the complaint. The court stated that the allegations in the complaint might have contained all of the essential elements for an action in ejectment, however, it lacked allegations essential in an action to recover property that was wrongfully taken by state officials. The court noted that the action was one against the State and that consent had not been obtained to maintain an action against the State. The court determined that the State was the real party in interest because, if the owner won, the judgment would have affected the activities of the state. The court concluded that the owner did not allege facts that indicated that the members took or held his property unconstitutionally or without statutory authority, therefore, that the action could not be maintained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which sustained the members' demurrer to the owner's complaint.

 

768 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carnegie


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


158 Conn. 264; 259 A.2d 628; 1969 Conn. LEXIS 601


May 7, 1969, Argued  
June 3, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in two counts charging the defendant with the crimes of forgery and obtaining money by false pretenses, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the jury before Klau, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty on both counts and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) which found her guilty, by jury verdict, of forgery, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-346, and of obtaining money by false pretenses, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-360.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after she was identified by a bank teller as the person who cashed a stolen check. The court upheld the conviction on appeal, holding that the pretrial confrontation between the identifying witness and defendant at the police station was not so suggestive and unfair so as to constitute a denial of due process. The court found that the bank teller testified with certainty as to her recollection of defendant and that there was no evidence that she was coached or influenced to identify defendant. The court further held that the single showing of defendant for identification purposes was not a violation of due process. The court held that defendant was not entitled to have the assistance of counsel when she was shown singly to the bank teller for identification purposes. The trial court did not err by excluding evidence of defendant's willingness to take a lie-detector test because such tests were not recognized as a reliable and accurate means of ascertaining the truth. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in ruling on defendant's discovery motions.


OUTCOME: No error was found.

 

769 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Robert Emmet & Son Oil & Supply Co. v. Sullivan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


158 Conn. 234; 259 A.2d 636; 1969 Conn. LEXIS 598; 45 A.L.R.3d 1261


April 3, 1969, Argued  
May 6, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the disallowance by the defendant of a claim for a refund of a portion of the sales and use tax paid on the purchase of an automobile out of the state, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Longo, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a determination made by defendant tax commissioner as to the taxpayer's liability for sales and use tax paid on the purchase of an automobile out of state. The taxpayer appealed to the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), and the court reserved the case to address the issues.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer purchased his vehicle in Rhode Island, and used a trade-in toward a portion of the sales price. No sales or use tax was paid to the state of Rhode Island. When the taxpayer registered the vehicle in Connecticut, he paid, under protest, an amount of tax attributable to the amount allowed by the seller for the trade-in vehicle. From the disallowance of its claim for a refund, the taxpayer appealed. The court reserved the matter to address the situation whereby a resident who purchased a motor vehicle for use in Connecticut and as part payment of the purchase price traded in another automobile was required to pay a greater tax if he purchased the motor vehicle from an out-of-state dealer than he was required to pay if he made a purchase on the same terms from a dealer in Connecticut. The court decided that the legislative scheme violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, clause 3, and it ordered a refund to the taxpayer of the unconstitutional tax paid with interest. The court concluded that Connecticut did not have an adequate justification for the taxing scheme and that the statute worked a discrimination against interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court ordered a refund to the taxpayer.

Panaroni v. Johnson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


158 Conn. 92; 256 A.2d 246; 1969 Conn. LEXIS 581


February 5, 1969, Argued  
April 1, 1969, Decided

DISPOSITION: Error in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landlords appealed the decision of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which awarded plaintiff tenant damages for personal injuries sustained in a fall down an unenclosed outside stairway.


OVERVIEW: The tenant brought an action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained in a fall down a stairway which the tenant alleged had been retained in control of the landlords. The landlords claimed that the stairway leading solely to the tenement of the tenant was wholly demised under the written lease and therefore was under her control. The trial court found in favor of the tenant. The court affirmed except as to the amount of damages awarded and ordered a new trial, holding that (1) because the housing code of the city was applied to the controversy, there was an obligation on the part of the landlord to repair the premises apart from the lease and the contractual agreement of the parties; (2) because the lease was ambiguous, the trial court did not err in admitting parol evidence of the conversations between the parties prior to the execution of the lease to aid in its interpretation and in the ascertainment of the intent of the parties; and (3) the trial court erred in including in its charge to the jury a statement concerning the tenant's inalienable right to pursue happiness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the tenant except as to the amount of damages awarded and ordered a new trial.

Cascio v. Town Council of West Hartford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


158 Conn. 111; 256 A.2d 685; 1969 Conn. LEXIS 582


March 6, 1969, Argued  
April 1, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant in disapproving an application for a change of zone, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, McGrath, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners, whose application for a change of zoning was denied by defendant town council, complained of a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal from the disapproval of their application for a change of zone of a parcel of land from residence AA to residence G and for a change of zone for the same parcel from the residence G district to a special development district.


OVERVIEW: The application for the two-step change of zone made by the landowners, if approved, would have allowed a use of the property resulting in a greater density than would otherwise have been permitted in a residence AA district. The town plan and zoning commission recommended that the application be approved, but the town council voted to disapprove it. The record disclosed, inter alia, that there was opposition by adjoining homeowners to the application; that the area was suitable for the construction of single-family residences; that the land was not suited for 192 apartment units; that the parcel in question was suited for apartments and ultimately should be so zoned but not at this time; and, that approval of the zone change would create a traffic hazard which would violate one of the expressly stated purposes of the zoning regulations, which was to lessen congestion in the streets. Upon review, the court held that the action of the council in denying the application for a change and in leaving the property in its previous classification was based on reasonable grounds and could not be said to have been illegal, arbitrary, or an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no error.

Manufacturers Hanover Trust Co. v. Bartram


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


158 Conn. 48; 255 A.2d 828; 1969 Conn. LEXIS 575


February 6, 1969, Argued  
March 18, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the distribution of capital gains dividends, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County at Stamford and reserved by the court, Tierney, J., for the advice of this court.

The named defendant et al. filed a motion for reargument which was denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant remaindermen appealed an order of the Superior Court in Fairfield County at Stamford (Connecticut), which denied its motion for reargument in an action by plaintiff trustees for a declaratory judgment determining the distribution of capital gains dividends.


OVERVIEW: Eight trusts were created by the will of decedent. Six trusts consisted of entirely, and the other two substantially, of shares in a personal holding company. That company transferred its shares to a mutual fund that periodically distributed dividends to its shareholders. The will itself was silent in regard to the allocation of capital gains dividends. The remaindermen claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45-113, as amended by 1965 Conn. Acts 263, governed the allocation of all capital gains dividends received by the trustees after June 15, 1965, the effective date of the amendment. The trustees, on the other hand, claimed that the legislature never intended, and constitutionally could not provide, that this amendment affected trusts created prior to its effective date. The court held that when the trustees received the capital gains dividends, the remaindermen acquired a vested property right in those dividends under the provisions of the 1965 amendment, and the later attempt by the 1967 legislature to change the nature of those dividends or their allocation was constitutionally impermissible and necessarily wholly ineffective.


OUTCOME: The court held that the trustees should not distribute the dividends as income.

Bianco v. Darien


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


157 Conn. 548; 254 A.2d 898; 1969 Conn. LEXIS 537


December 4, 1968, Argued  
February 19, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants from interfering with the operation of a private garbage collection facility on the plaintiffs' premises, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford and tried to the court, George, J.; judgment for the defendants and appeal by the plaintiffs.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which entered judgment in favor of defendants, a town and a zoning enforcement officer, in an action filed by the landowners for an injunction to restrain defendants from interfering with the operation of a private garbage collection facility on the landowners' premises.


OVERVIEW: The landowners maintained 10 garbage trucks on their business property. In 1965, the zoning enforcement officer of the town notified the landowners that storage of the trucks was not permitted. The landowners filed an action for an injunction to restrain defendants from interfering with the operation of their garbage collection business and truck storage. Judgment was entered in favor of defendants. On review, the court held that: (1) the trial court erred in concluding that the landowners had an adequate remedy available to them by way of either an administrative review or an appeal; (2) the landowners could not avail themselves of the doctrine of estoppel, and defendants were not chargeable with laches; (3) defendants did not abandon the provisions of the zoning regulations as applied to storage of the trucks on the landowners' property; (4) successive reenactments of Darien, Conn., Zoning Regs. §§ 220.39 and 451 (1957) did not transform the landowners' use into a valid nonconforming use; and (5) the failure of the town to enforce zoning regulations against neighboring properties did not constitute a violation of the landowners' right to equal protection under the law. No error.


OUTCOME: The court held that the trial court's judgment for defendants was correct.

Bloom v. Water Resources Com.

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff adjoining businesses appealed an order of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which dismissed the businesses' appeal from the action of defendant state water resources commission in issuing a permit to defendant waterfront landowner to construct a travel-lift well, ramps, floats and mooring piles and to dredge an area in the river upon which the property was situated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant landowner sought a permit to construct a marina and to dredge the river in order to allow pleasure boats to have access to the marina. Adams v. Rubinow


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


157 Conn. 150; 251 A.2d 49; 1968 Conn. LEXIS 501


June 11, 1968, Argued  
November 20, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of an act concerning the administration of the Probate Court system, and for an injunction, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Driscoll, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, 30 probate judges, brought an action against defendant state and probate court officials before the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which reserved the action for advice of the court. The judges claimed that 1967 Conn. Acts 558 was unconstitutional, and they sought answers to certain enumerated questions upon a stipulation of facts.


OVERVIEW: The state and the probate court officials were involved in the passage of 1967 Conn. Acts 558, which legislated rules for the administration of and practice and procedure in the probate courts. The judges sued, seeking a declaration that the Act was unconstitutional and seeking responses to certain questions. The superior court reserved the action for advice from the court. The court held that portions of 1967 Conn. Acts 558 §§ 15, 16, 19 were unconstitutional, but said it could not answer some questions due to their nonconformity with Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 310(b). Although the Legislature could not make rules of administration, practice, or procedure binding the courts created by Conn. Const. art 5, § 1 (1965), it could regulate the lower courts with reasonable rules. The court held that 1967 Conn. Acts 558 created mostly ministerial rules, and found unconstitutional only those provisions which encroached upon the probate court's functioning. The court held that the Act as a whole could survive the portions stricken as unconstitutional, the court held, despite the lack of a severability provision, in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-3.


OUTCOME: The court advised the superior court that the portions of 1967 Conn. Acts 558 §§ 15, 16, 19 providing for the suspension of a judge of probate by the chief court administrator and authorizing the probate court administrator to fix probate fees were unconstitutional. The court asserted that it could not answer any other questions, and did not tax costs.

Williams v. Reincke


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


157 Conn. 143; 249 A.2d 252; 1968 Conn. LEXIS 500


October 9, 1968, Argued  
November 6, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus alleging unlawful imprisonment, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Palmer, J.; judgment dismissing the writ, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, prison inmate, appealed the dismissal of a writ of habeas corpus brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) alleging unlawful imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from dismissal of a writ of habeas corpus, the court held there was no error. The prison inmate, armed with a revolver, robbed a bank As he was leaving the bank with the stolen money and the revolver, an automatic camera in the bank photographed him. A girl who accompanied the inmate to the bank informed the police that the inmate had committed the robbery. The inmate pleaded guilty to robbery with violence and was imprisoned. He did not challenge his arrest until he filed his application for habeas corpus. The inmate argued that his arrest was illegal because it was made pursuant to a warrant unsupported by oath and that the police illegally searched his hotel room and illegally seized property. The petition was denied, and the inmate appealed. The court held that an illegal arrest by itself was not sufficient to warrant habeas corpus relief. Also, the mere occurrence of a constitutional violation was not sufficient to render a plea of guilty involuntary. So long as the guilty plea was voluntarily made, it would withstand a collateral attack despite the fact that some of the accused's constitutional rights were infringed. Also, the search without a warrant was valid.


OUTCOME: The court held there was no error in the dismissal of a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant board in granting a special exception for a sanitary landfill operation, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Cohen, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff neighboring property owners appealed a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal of the action of defendant Zoning Board of Appeals of the Town of Glastonbury (Connecticut) in granting a special exception for a sanitary landfill operation.


OVERVIEW: The board originally denied the request for a special exception because the properties immediately adjacent to the access road would be permanently and substantially injured. On the second application, the town proposed relocating the access road 350 feet from the nearest dwelling and eliminated 1.3 acres of the disposal area, which were most observable from a neighboring property. The court concluded that the board properly granted the second application. It determined that the modified proposal was substantially changed to comport with the building zone regulations. Also, the record disclosed ample evidence to support the board's conclusion that the sanitary landfill operation, as proposed in the second application, would serve the general public and would not permanently or substantially injure neighboring property. The court also found that the trial court did not err in upholding the board's decision that the sanitary landfill disposal area would not constitute a public nuisance. Finally, the court rejected the neighboring landowners' claim that the conditions that circumscribed the operation of the sanitary landfill proposal were so vague that they could not be enforced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Carvette v. Marion Power Shovel Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


157 Conn. 92; 249 A.2d 58; 1968 Conn. LEXIS 492


October 3, 1968, Argued  
October 23, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the reformation of a contract, for damages, and for other relief, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County, where the defendant filed a special defense of lack of jurisdiction; judgment dismissing the action, Zarrilli, J., from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state resident appealed an order from the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which granted the motion of defendant foreign corporation to dismiss the resident's action for breach of contract for lack of in personam jurisdiction, contending that the provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 33-411 were not applicable because the cause of action matured prior to the statute's effective date.


OVERVIEW: The resident purchased a backhoe from the corporation, an Ohio business not qualified to conduct business in Connecticut. The backhoe was delivered in Connecticut and, when the resident defaulted in the payments, the corporation brought a replevin action in Connecticut to recover it. The resident brought an action for breach of contract for the corporation's failure to cure the defects in the equipment and service of process was perfected upon the corporation pursuant to the long arm statute, § 33-411. The corporation filed a motion to dismiss for lack of in personam jurisdiction, contending that § 33-411 was not applicable because the cause of action matured prior to its effective date. The trial court granted the motion and the resident appealed. The court found error and remanded the cause for further proceedings not inconsistent with the court's opinion, finding that § 33-411 was a procedural statute because it did not affect the obligations of the parties under their contract and, as such, it could be applied retroactively. The court concluded that given the conduct of the corporation within the state there was no injustice in the retroactive application of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court found error and remanded the cause for further proceedings not inconsistent with the court's opinion.

 

779 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Mayock v. Martin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


157 Conn. 56; 245 A.2d 574; 1968 Conn. LEXIS 488


June 5, 1968, Argued  
July 23, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus alleging unlawful confinement, brought to the Superior Court in New London County and tried to the court, Longo, J.; judgment dismissing the writ, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus that alleged his confinement in a state hospital was illegal because his present mental condition did not require, not did it legally justify, his involuntary confinement or custodial care. The Superior Court, New London County (Connecticut) dismissed the writ. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed that he was being illegally confined because of his religious beliefs in violation of the first and fourteenth amendments to the United States constitution and of Conn. Const. art. 1, §§ 3, 20. He urged that he was not likely to injure any other person; that, at the very worst, the state was concerned with a mere possibility that he would remove a foot; and that even if he did remove a foot, there was no evidence that the removal would prevent him from leading a useful and productive life. The finding did not support petitioner's claim that he was being confined solely because of his religious beliefs. The trial court's conclusion that the bizarre conduct of petitioner was inconsistent with the peace and safety of the state was amply supported by the finding of subordinate facts. The theory that petitioner asked the court to adopt overlooked the statutory definition of a mentally ill person which, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-176, was not limited to one who required treatment for the welfare of others or the community but included, as well, one who required treatment for his own welfare.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no error in the trial court's decision.

 

780 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Rothkopf v. Danbury


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


156 Conn. 347; 242 A.2d 771; 1968 Conn. LEXIS 612


March 5, 1968, Argued  
April 16, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of a portion of the Home Rule Act and the legality of the consolidation ordinance of the town and city of Danbury, for an injunction and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and reserved by the court, LaMacchia, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of a portion of the Home Rule Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 7-195 through 7-201, the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut) reserved three questions for the advice of the Connecticut Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: In an action for a declaratory judgment regarding the legality of the government of a city, the trial court reserved three questions for consideration by the higher court. The court found that there were several impediments to its consideration of the questions reserved. First, the court noted that a trial court or judge could not confer jurisdiction on the court merely by reserving questions for its advice. The court noted that defendants had filed an answer pleading res judicata, which plaintiffs had denied. The court noted that the issue still remained to be determined and that the determination could mean that the advice of the court would not enter into a decision of the case. The court therefore held that the reservation was premature. In addition, the court held that plaintiffs had no standing as individuals to challenge the constitutional and legal existence of the city. The court therefore refused to answer the reserved questions.


OUTCOME: The court refused to answer the questions reserved by the trial court.

Karp v. Zoning Bd. of Stamford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


156 Conn. 287; 240 A.2d 845; 1968 Conn. LEXIS 606


February 6, 1968, Argued  
April 2, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the named defendant in amending the zoning regulations, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford and tried to the court, Tierney, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, various individuals, appealed a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal of a decision from defendant zoning board. Plaintiffs challenged the zoning board's decision to amend Stamford, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 14 entitled "Dispensing of Alcoholic Liquors."


OVERVIEW: Stamford, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 14(b) prohibited, inter alia, the use of premises for the sale of alcoholic beverage under package store and druggist permits if any entrance to such building or premises was within 1500 feet radius from any other building or premises being used for the sale of alcoholic liquor under such permits. The amendment provided that the restriction would not apply to removal of an existing package store permit or druggist permit issued by the liquor control commission, if the existing site or location was being taken or threatened to be taken in the exercise of eminent domain. Plaintiffs claimed that the action of the zoning board violated the equal protection laws. The court concluded that the amendment was not arbitrary, capricious, discriminatory, or unreasonable, nor did not violate plaintiffs' constitutional rights. The establishment of the regulation was within the legislative capacity of the zoning board, and the court could not say that the classification approved was unreasonable. Moreover, it could not be said that the regulation did not bear a reasonable relation to the public welfare within the particulars specified in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that there was no error in the trial court's judgment, which dismissed plaintiffs' appeal.

Hoblitzelle v. Frechette


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


156 Conn. 253; 240 A.2d 864; 1968 Conn. LEXIS 602


February 9, 1968, Argued  
March 14, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application claiming that the moderator should have declared the plaintiffs to have been elected to the board of aldermen in New Haven, brought to Hon. Anthony E. Grillo, a judge of the Superior Court, and reserved for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The New Haven Superior Court (Connecticut) reserved questions for the court in plaintiff aldermen's lawsuit claiming that a moderator should have declared them to have been elected to the board of aldermen.


OVERVIEW: The aldermen filed a lawsuit claiming that a moderator should have declared them to have been elected to the board of aldermen. The court refused to answer the questions reserved by the appellate court. The court determined that a trial court or judge could not confer jurisdiction on the court merely by reserving questions for its advice. The court did not entertain a reservation in an action that was not ready for final judgment unless the questions presented were reasonably certain to enter into the decision of the case and it appeared that their determination was in the interest of simplicity, directness, and economy of judicial action. The case was brought pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-328 (Rev. to 1964). The court held that two cases were pending, each with different parties and on a different subject matter, one in the superior court and one in a U.S. District Court. The District Court's judgment purported to assert complete direction and control of all aspects of the nomination and election of aldermen in the county in question. The U.S. District Court had jurisdiction to decide the basic questions presented to the court in the case.


OUTCOME: The court refused to answer the questions reserved.

J & M Realty Co. v. Norwalk


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


156 Conn. 185; 239 A.2d 534; 1968 Conn. LEXIS 593


December 6, 1967, Argued  
February 27, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant in disapproving an application for a subdivision, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Aaronson, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner appealed from a judgment by the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which affirmed defendant city common council's disapproval of the landowner's application for a subdivision.


OVERVIEW: The landowner's application for a subdivision was approved by the city planning commission, but was disapproved by the city common council. The landowner appealed to the trial court, claiming that the action of the common council was arbitrary and unreasonable in that no account was taken by the council of the action of the planning commission's approval of the subdivision and that the action of the council was invalid because of 1947 Conn. Spec. Acts No. 214, as amended by 1955 Conn. Spec. Acts No. 616. The court held on appeal that the trial court erred in holding that the council was acting legislatively rather than administratively. The council was performing the function of a planning commission, and in so doing, it was acting administratively. Although there was no specific provision which stated that the council had to set forth the reasons for its disapproval, the requirement that a resubmission should be based on a substantial change of the conditions assumed that the applicant must have knowledge of the reasons for the disapproval.


OUTCOME: The court ruled in favor of the landowner and directed the council to set forth the reasons for disapproving the landowner's subdivision application.

 

784 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State Nat'l Bank v. Planning & Zoning Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


156 Conn. 99; 239 A.2d 528; 1968 Conn. LEXIS 584


January 3, 1968, Argued  
January 30, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant in denying an application for a change of zone, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Williams, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal and from the judgment and from the denial of a motion to open the judgment, the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant zoning commission sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield (Connecticut), which sustained an appeal brought by plaintiffs, a bank as lessee and a property owner, from the commission's denial of the bank's application for a change of zone from residential to commercial.


OVERVIEW: The bank made the application for the zonal reclassification so that it could erect a commercial banking facility on the leased land. Plaintiffs maintained the trial court was correct in sustaining their appeal, claiming that the commission acted illegally, arbitrarily, and in abuse of its discretion in denying the application. Plaintiffs asserted that a commercial zone represented the highest and best use for the property. The court concluded that the maximum possible enrichment of a property owner was not a controlling purpose of zoning. Instead, the purpose was to encourage the most appropriate use of land throughout the municipality. The court found error in the judgment and directed a dismissal of the appeal. The court concluded that the denial of the application was based on reasonable grounds and was not arbitrary or confiscatory. The court found reasonable justification for the action of the commission in not disturbing the residential zonal classification of the land in question, having in mind the preservation of the residential characteristics of the properties in the surrounding area and the attempt to prevent intrusion of business and commercial uses.


OUTCOME: The court found error in the judgment that sustained plaintiffs' appeal. The court set aside the judgment and remanded the case with directions to dismiss the appeal.

 

785 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Towles


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


155 Conn. 516; 235 A.2d 639; 1967 Conn. LEXIS 578


October 5, 1967, Argued  
November 9, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of violation of the Uniform State Narcotic Drug Act, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the jury before Palmer, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which, following a jury trial, found him guilty of possessing and selling a narcotic drug in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-246. Defendant argued error in the denial of his motion to suppress evidence, in admitting currency and a plastic bag containing marihuana, in the denial of his motion for a mistrial, and in rulings excluding certain evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought to suppress the admission of two marked currency bills taken from his person after a warrantless arrest, claiming that the arrest was illegal. On appeal, the court, stating the that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress, concluded that the search of defendant's person was incident to a valid arrest, that he was arrested on the speedy information of other officers, that the arresting officer had reasonable ground to believe that defendant had committed a felony, and that the search was not unconstitutional. The court also stated that it found no error in the trial court's conclusion that under the circumstances the search of defendant's person was a legal search made incident to a valid arrest, and defendant was not entitled to an order suppressing the two marked bills. The court stated that there was no error in the evidential rulings and held that defendant's motion for a mistrial was properly denied because the person to whom defendant sold the drugs was not a witness, nor was there any claim that he had given any information which formed the basis of the arrest.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's decision that defendant was guilty of possessing and selling a narcotic drug.

Waterford v. Grabner


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


155 Conn. 431; 232 A.2d 481; 1967 Conn. LEXIS 567


June 14, 1967, Argued  
July 20, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction to restrain the defendants from carrying on the commercial removal of earth products from their land without a permit, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New London County and tried to the court, Dannehy, J.; judgment for the defendants and appeal by the plaintiffs.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a town and a building inspector, sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in New London County (Connecticut), which denied their request for an injunction against defendant gravel company.


OVERVIEW: The company was engaged in the business of selling and processing sand and gravel from its own property. The town adopted zoning regulations permitting sand and gravel pits. In 1960, the town adopted an ordinance requiring a permit for the removal of sand and gravel. In April 1964, the building inspector ordered the company to cease its operations until they obtained the required permit. The company refused, asserting that its operation constituted a valid nonconforming use. Plaintiffs commenced an action to enjoin the company from continuing its operations until it complied with the ordinance. The company alleged that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The trial court held that the company's business was a valid nonconforming use. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred by denying the injunction because the trial court's judgment was based upon an unsound proposition of law. The court found that the trial court's refusal to issue the injunction was based upon its conclusion that the company's operations were a valid nonconforming use. However, the trial court failed to decide the constitutionality of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's judgment, which had been in the company's favor, and ordered a new trial.

State v. Darwin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


155 Conn. 124; 230 A.2d 573; 1967 Conn. LEXIS 533

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court in Tolland County (Connecticut) of murder in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: A woman was murdered after attending a club meeting that defendant also attended. When clothing that defendant voluntarily gave police evidenced semen and blood stains, warrants were issued for his arrest. While in custody, defendant had a fainting spell and confessed to the murder upon reviving. On the following day, defendant reenacted the crime in detail and completed a written confession after being warned that his statement could be used against him. On appeal, the court held that defendant's appearance at the next trial court session after the day of his arrest was timely under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-1b (1963) and that his arraignment made within two hours of his arrest was timely under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-43 (1963). The court found that the trial court had probable cause to issue a warrant to seize defendant's automobile that was independent of its initial illegal seizure. The court also held that the trial court did not err in finding that the state sustained its burden of proving in the totality of the circumstances, including the absence of counsel, that defendant's reenactment of the crime and his second confession were voluntary and thus, admissible into evidence.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's decisions.

Wamphassuc Point Property Owners Asso. v. Public Utilities Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


154 Conn. 674; 228 A.2d 513; 1967 Conn. LEXIS 726


February 9, 1967, Argued  
April 4, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the defendant commission directing the installation of safety devices at a railroad grade crossing, brought to the Superior Court in New London County and tried to the court, Thim, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal of the individual plaintiffs, from which the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Public Utilities Commission and railroad trustees, appealed an order from the Superior Court in New London County (Connecticut), which reversed the Commission's determination and granted judgment to plaintiffs, individual property owners, on their claims that a road near their property was a public highway and not a private drive, subject to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-119a.


OVERVIEW: The road contained a dangerous intersection with railroad tracks, and the railroad applied to the Commission for the installation of control and safety devices under § 16-119a. Section 16-119a provided that if a road was a private drive, the cost of the installation of the devices was to be apportioned between the property owners, the city, state, and the railroad. At a hearing, over the objections of the property owners and the town, the Commission determined that the road was a private drive. The costs were apportioned. The trial court reversed. On appeal, the court noted that the Commission's determination was based on the fact that the road was laid out in 1872 and that a statute enacted in 1883 required that public roads pass either under or over a railway crossing. The failure of the local authorities to cause the road to conform to the 1883 statute was the basis for the Commission's decision. Except for the failure to comply with the statute, the road had all indications of a public highway. The trial court had properly limited its consideration to the evidence used by the Commission in reaching the conclusion that §16-119a was not applicable to the road.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that reversed the Commission's order. The court affirmed that the road was a public highway and not a private road.
