Teuscher v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


154 Conn. 650; 228 A.2d 518; 1967 Conn. LEXIS 722


December 7, 1966, Argued  
March 30, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant in sustaining the order of the zoning enforcement officer to cease and desist from the removal of gravel from the plaintiff's property, and for other relief, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Jones, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sought review of a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which dismissed his appeal of an action of defendant zoning board of appeals sustaining an order of a zoning enforcement officer. The order required the property owner to cease and desist from the removal of gravel from his property.


OVERVIEW: A zoning officer served the property owner with an order to cease and desist from the removal and sale of gravel from his property. The board of zoning appeals affirmed the order. When the trial court dismissed his appeal, the owner sought further review and asserted that the decision of the board was illegal, arbitrary, and in abuse of its discretion because the gravel pit was a legal, nonconforming use that existed before the zoning ordinance at issue was adopted. The court noted that whether the gravel pit was or was not a nonconforming use was not controlling and that it was not necessary for the court to decide the claim of a nonconforming use. The court held that even if the ordinance restricted a beneficial use to which the property had previously been devoted, it was not unconstitutional if the ordinance was otherwise a valid exercise of the town's police powers. The court therefore affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the appeal because the owner had not sustained his burden of proof that the ordinance was discriminatory and therefore unconstitutional. The court concluded that the ordinance was a proper exercise of the police power and was constitutionally valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Knights of Columbus Council v. Mulcahy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


154 Conn. 583; 227 A.2d 413; 1967 Conn. LEXIS 712


January 5, 1967, Argued  
March 7, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a temporary injunction restraining the defendants from revoking a bingo permit pendente lite, for a declaratory judgment, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, MacDonald, J.; judgment for the defendants and appeal by the plaintiff.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error in form of judgment; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff fraternal organization sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which was rendered in favor of defendant police officials in the fraternal organization's action seeking a temporary injunction restraining the police officials from revoking a bingo permit pendente lite, for a declaratory judgment, and for other relief.


OVERVIEW: A dispute arose between a fraternal organization that conducted bingo games and police officials concerning the legality of Sunday bingo games under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-300. The trial court held that § 53-300 was constitutional and prohibited the issuance of permits for the playing of bingo on Sunday. On appeal, the fraternal organization asserted that, pursuant to its permit to conduct bingo games issued under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-169, it could conduct the games on any day of the week. The court disagreed and held that in giving effect to both §§ 7-169 and 53-300, § 7-169 could, with complete reasonableness, be read to limit the conduct of bingo games to only one day in each weekly interval without in any way impinging upon the prohibition in § 53-300 against the conduct of secular business on Sunday. The court held that the trial court did not err in holding that § 53-300 was constitutional but remanded the case with direction to render judgment confined only to the parties to the action because it found that the form of the judgment was too broad.


OUTCOME: The court agreed with the conclusion of the trial court but found error in the form of the judgment. The court remanded the case with direction to render judgment confined only to the parties to the action.

Windsor v. Windsor Police Dep't Employees Asso.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


154 Conn. 530; 227 A.2d 65; 1967 Conn. LEXIS 707


January 5, 1967, Argued  
February 21, 1967, Decided

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which granted defendant state labor relations board's motion to erase the town's appeal of a decision of the board from the court's docket for lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: A town filed a petition seeking review of a decision of the state labor relations board, which, in part, determined that a unit appropriate for collective bargaining purposes for the town's police department would include all uniformed and investigatory employees of the department, excluding the chief and deputy chief. 794 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wilkas


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


154 Conn. 407; 225 A.2d 821; 1967 Conn. LEXIS 690


December 8, 1966, Argued  
January 6, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of selling alcoholic liquor to a minor, brought to the Circuit Court in the fourth circuit and tried to the jury before Martin, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to the Appellate Division of the Circuit Court, which affirmed the judgment; from the judgment of the Appellate Division, the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On granting of certification, defendant appealed from the judgment of the Appellate Division of the Circuit Court (Connecticut), which affirmed a circuit court verdict finding defendant guilty of selling liquor to a minor. The court granted certification to consider whether the State proved alcohol content but refused to consider whether a charge that allowed the jury to consider defendant's silence as evidence of guilt was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not take exception to the trial court's charge to the jury as to what inferences they could draw from defendant's failure to testify. During his appeal on other grounds, the United States Supreme Court ruled that U.S. Const. amend. V, made applicable to the states by U.S. Const. amend. XIV, prohibited instructing a jury that an accused's silence could be considered evidence of guilt. The appellate court refused defendant's motion to add a challenge to the charge to his appeal. The court initially denied certification for the constitutional question because it was not raised at trial and because, at the time, state procedural requirements for raising a federal constitutional question could be followed. While the appeal was pending, however, the Supreme Court held in a similar case that failure to observe state procedural requirements was not a bar to an assertion, on appeal, of the Griffin rule. Justice required that the court entertain defendant's constitutional claim. Under the retroactive effect of the Griffin rule, the trial court erred in commenting on defendant's failure to testify. The court did not consider any other issue.


OUTCOME: The court granted certification on the constitutional ground but declined to consider whether the State proved alcohol content. The court found that the judgment was in error, set the judgment aside, and ordered a new trial.

 

795 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Bennett v. Glynn


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


154 Conn. 237; 224 A.2d 711; 1966 Conn. LEXIS 447


October 7, 1966, Argued  
November 23, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the nature of quo warranto, for an injunction, and for a declaratory judgment determining whether the Minority Representation statute applies to the Hartford board of tax review, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Palmer, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court reviewed a question reserved by the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), in an action in the nature of a quo warranto for an injunction and a declaratory judgment. The question reserved by the superior court was whether Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-167a, the Minority Representation Statute applied to the Board of Tax Review of the City of Hartford.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs claimed that the Minority Representation Statute, which required no more than two out of three members of a board, commission, or committee of the state or political subdivision thereof to be of the same party. Defendants claimed that the statute did not apply to the Board of Tax Review, a three person, elected board. The court answered the question in the affirmative holding that the Minority Representation Statute applied to the Board of Tax Review. There was no suggestion of an intent in § 9-167a that, if minority representation could not be achieved under the terms of the statute as to an elective body in a particular municipality, the General Assembly did not intend to have the statute apply to an appointive body in the same municipality. Even if the Board of Tax Review were an agency or arm of the common council, that would have no bearing on the applicability to the Board of the Minority Representation statute. The Board of Tax Review was not an agency or arm of the common council. Rather, it is an agency or arm of the City of Hartford in carrying out its municipal function of taxation as authorized, and delegated to it, by the state.


OUTCOME: The court answered the question in the reservation in the affirmative. The Minority Representation Statute applied to the Board of Tax Review of the City of Hartford and not more than two members of that Board may properly belong to the same political party.

 

796 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Grievance Committee of Bar v. Dacey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


154 Conn. 129; 222 A.2d 339; 1966 Conn. LEXIS 435; 22 A.L.R.3d 1092


June 7, 1966, Argued  
July 19, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proceeding in equity to restrain the defendants from the illegal practice of law, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Thim, J.; judgment for the plaintiff and appeal by the defendants.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a county bar association grievance committee, brought an action seeking an injunction to restrain defendant, a corporate mutual fund dealer, from engaging in the unauthorized practice of law in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-88. The dealer sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which entered judgment for the committee. The dealer's motion for reargument was denied.


OVERVIEW: The dealer provided his customers with a booklet explaining generally the use of trusts, wills, and tax consequences, and he provided forms for such arrangements. The dealer did not urge the clients, as the booklet suggested, to consult with an attorney. Rather, the dealer assisted in the preparation of the trust and will, which provided that the corpus of the trust would be invested through the dealer, thus, providing the dealer a commission. The court affirmed the judgment. The court rejected the dealer's interpretation of § 51-88 that it only prohibited the practice of law outside of the court if it was conducted as a business. Under the rule that when information given was directed toward a particular person and his needs and to a particular instrument prepared for his execution, such action constituted the practice of law, the court found that the dealer clearly engaged in the practice of law. Section 51-88 was not unconstitutionally vague. The limited injunction granted did not violate the dealer's right of free speech because it did not deprive the dealer of any rights to which he could claim an entitlement. The dealer's objections to the evidentiary admissions were denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court, which granted the committee's request for an injunction against the dealer restraining his unauthorized practice of law.

 

797 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Carilli v. Pension Com. of Hartford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


154 Conn. 1; 220 A.2d 439; 1966 Conn. LEXIS 417


May 4, 1966, Argued  
June 6, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus to compel the defendant to award the plaintiff a special disability retirement allowance, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Radin, J.; judgment for the defendant and appeal by the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which rendered a judgment for appellee city pension commission in a mandamus action filed by the employee to compel the city pension commission to award him a special disability retirement allowance.


OVERVIEW: The employee was employed as a member of a city's fire department. The employee also held a moonlighting job with the United States post office. As a result of a heart attack that arose out of his fire department employment, the employee suffered a permanent, partial disability. As a result, the employee was unable to continue his fire department employment. The employee, who had returned to his post office job, applied for a special disability allowance under the provisions of 1957 Conn. Spec. Acts 347, § 1(f). The city pension commission denied the application on the ground that he could derive an income that was not 10 percent below his fireman income. The trial court subsequently rendered a judgment for the city pension commission in a mandamus action filed by the employee to compel the city pension commission to award him a special disability retirement allowance. That decision was affirmed on appeal. The court found that the trial court correctly rejected the employee's claim that the act's phrase "income he was earning at the time he incurred such disability" included income received from sources other than compensation for his services as a city fireman.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

798 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Hardware Mut. Casualty Co. v. Premo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


153 Conn. 465; 217 A.2d 698; 1966 Conn. LEXIS 549


January 6, 1966, Argued  
March 1, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of the 1963 act concerning the establishment of rates of insurance, and the validity of notices issued by the named defendant, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Cotter, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed a declaratory judgment action which sought a determination of whether Conn. Public Acts No. 347 (1963) was unconstitutional and alleged that two purported directives were invalid as unauthorized and unreasonable.


OVERVIEW: Conn. Public Acts No. 347 (1963) ("the Act") amended Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 38-116, 38-187 and 38-189 (e), which regulated the making of rates by insurance companies. Plaintiffs alleged the Act was unconstitutional. The court held that the Act was not unconstitutional on the basis that it contained vague phrases because the phrases were technical phrases that were understood by the insurance industry. The Act was not an illegal delegation of legislative power to the insurance commissioner because insurers' judgment could not be excluded from rate making and plaintiffs failed to meet their burden of proving that the Act's requirements were so inadequate as to constitute an illegal delegation of power. The "deemer clause" of the Act was not unconstitutional because the presumption of the clause was rebuttable. Exhibit B was not a directive because it was a preliminary guide and had not effect or binding force.


OUTCOME: The act was constitutional because plaintiffs failed to prove the requirements were so inadequate as to constitute an illegal delegation of legislative power, and the act did not create a conclusive presumption. The purported directives were not directives because they were preliminary guides and had no binding effect.

 

799 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Buck v. Morris Park, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


153 Conn. 290; 216 A.2d 187; 1965 Conn. LEXIS 437


November 4, 1965, Argued  
December 30, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mortgage, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County at Waterbury, where, after judgment of foreclosure and failure to redeem, appraisers were appointed who filed their report, to which the defendant filed a remonstrance, and the plaintiff having filed a motion for a deficiency judgment, the court, Cotter, J., denied the remonstrance, accepted the report, and rendered a deficiency judgment, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a foreclosure action after a judgment of foreclosure and failure to redeem, defendant mortgagor appealed the judgment from the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) denying the mortgagor's motion for remonstrance, accepting the report of an appraiser, and rendering a deficiency judgment in favor of plaintiff mortgagee. The mortgagor claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-14, that authorized the appraiser's report, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagee obtained a foreclosure on the mortgagor's property, which the mortgagor failed to redeem. Upon motion of the mortgagor, the trial court appointed three disinterested appraisers, and they appraised the mortgaged property and made written report to the court as required by § 49-14. The mortgagor filed a remonstrance to the acceptance of the report, which the court overruled. The report was accepted, and a judgment was rendered for the deficiency. On review the mortgagor claimed that § 49-14 was unconstitutional in that it makes no provision for notice of the meeting of the appraisers to be given to the mortgagee so that the latter may introduce evidence on the question of value. In support of this contention, the mortgagor argued that the appraisers should conduct a hearing and hear evidence in a manner similar to the procedure followed by referees and committees in assessing damages for the taking of land for purposes of condemnation. The court rejected the arguments, finding that it must be borne in mind that the action was for the foreclosure of a mortgage. The court found that due process was satisfied with notice of the appointment of appraisers.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

 

800 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Riley v. Liquor Control Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


153 Conn. 242; 215 A.2d 402; 1965 Conn. LEXIS 429


November 9, 1965, Argued  
December 9, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, in each case, in the first count, from the action of the defendant in refusing to accept the plaintiffs' application for a package store liquor permit and action, in each case, in the second count, for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of the 1963 act concerning the limitation on interest in retail permits, and for an injunction, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (by transfer, in the second case, from the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County) and tried to the court, Googel, J.; judgment for the defendant, in each case, on the first count and for the plaintiffs, in each case, on the second count declaring the act to be unconstitutional, and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the liquor control commission, sought review of judgments from the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which issued a declaratory judgment in favor of plaintiffs, two applicants for package store liquor permits and their backer, determining that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-48a was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The applicants each applied for package store liquor permits. Each applicant had the same backer. The commission refused to accept the applications on the ground that § 30-48a prohibited any backer from having an interest in more than two alcoholic beverage retail permits. The applicants appealed on the ground that the refusal was illegal, arbitrary, and an abuse of discretion. They also added a second count, seeking an injunction restraining the commission from invoking the provisions of § 30-48a and a declaratory judgment determining the rights of the parties. The trial court found for the commission on the first count and neither applicant appealed. On the second count, the trial court rendered a declaratory judgment that § 30-48a was unconstitutional but did not grant injunctive relief. On appeal by the commission, the court set aside the declaratory judgment and remanded with directions to dismiss the second count for lack of jurisdiction. A declaratory judgment action could not be rendered because the record, briefs, and argument made it clearly apparent that persons having an interest in the subject matter of the case were not parties and did not have notice of the action.


OUTCOME: The court found error as to the declaratory judgment count of the complaint, set aside the declaratory judgment in favor of the applicants and their backer, and remanded with direction to dismiss that count of their complaint for lack of jurisdiction.
